Dispute on Divisibility of Kitaba for a Jointly Owned Slave
Presentation of intra-Hanafi dispute on kitaba divisibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on kitaba divisibility for jointly owned slaves and identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of the disagreement.

Core Idea
Kitaba divisibility determines whether payment belongs to the contracting co-owner or is shared.

This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the kitaba contract for a jointly owned slave. When one co-owner permits the other to write the kitaba and receive payments, who owns the money if the slave becomes insolvent? The answer depends on the underlying principle: is kitaba divisible (Imam Abu Hanifa) or indivisible (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad)? Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to trace how a single legal principle—divisibility of contracts—generates differing rulings in related chapters like emancipation and kitaba.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their actions
We have a slave jointly owned by two. One co-owner (A) gives permission to the other (B) to write a kitaba for A's share and to receive payment. B does so, receives part of the payment, then the slave becomes insolvent.
The permission is key: without it, A would have the right to rescind the contract.
2
State Imam Abu Hanifa's position and its basis
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the payment belongs exclusively to B, the contracting co-owner. The basis is that kitaba is divisible (tajazzi al-kitaba): each share can be independently contracted. The permission transfers A's right to B, and A loses his right to rescind.
This is the view presented in the matn as the default.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and its basis
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the payment is shared between both co-owners. They argue that kitaba is not divisible; the contract is a single obligation binding both. Therefore, the slave is a mukatib for both, and any payment belongs proportionally to both.
This parallels the same dispute in emancipation (i'taq).
4
Note the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Imam Abu Hanifa, B keeps all received money; under the Sahibayn, B must share it with A. This directly affects the finances of the co-owners.
The passage does not indicate which view is mufta bihi; the text presents Imam's view as the author's preferred phrasing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب كتابة العبد المشترك لما فرغ من كتابة عبد غير مشترك شرع في كتابة العبد المشترك لأن الأصل عدم الاشتراك ؛ قاله في غاية البيان. وقال أكثر الشراح : ذكر كتابة الأثنين بعد كتابة الواحد لأن الاثنين بعد الواحد قال رحمه الله : (عبد لهما إذن أحدهما لصاحبه أن يكاتب حصته بألف ويقبض بدل الكتابة فكاتب وقبض بعضه فعجز فالمقبوض للقابض) يعني إذا كان العبد بين اثنين إذن أحدهما لصاحبه إن يكاتب حظه . وتعبير المؤلف بقوله لهما أولى من تعبير صاحب الهداية حيث قال بين رجلين لأن المثنى يستوي فيه المذكر والمؤنث فيشمل ما إذا كان رجلين أو امرأتين أو رجل وامرأة. وقال في العناية : وفائدة الإذن أن لا يكون له حق الفسخ كما يكون له إذا لم يأذن وفي الأصل وعامة المشايخ لم يشترطوا لصحة الفسخ القضاء أو الرضا، والإمام العلامة نجم الدين النسفي شرط له القضاء أو الرضا اهـ. وهذا هو قول الإمام. وقالا : هو مكاتب لهما والمقبوض بينهما، وأصله أن الكتابة تتجزي عند الإمام، وعندهما لا تتجزى كما ذكر في الاعتاق وفي الشارح: وفائدة إذنه بالقبض أن ينقطع حقه بين
Chapter on the kitaba of a jointly owned slave. When he finished the kitaba of a non-jointly owned slave, he began with the kitaba of a jointly owned slave, because the original state is non-joint ownership. This is stated in Ghayat al-Bayan. Most commentators said: He mentioned the kitaba of two after the kitaba of one, because two comes after one. He (the author) said: 'A slave belonging to two, one of them giving permission to the other to write a kitaba for his share for one thousand and to receive the kitaba payment; so he wrote the kitaba and received part of it, then the slave became insolvent; then what was received is for the one who received.' That is, when a slave is between two, one gives permission to the other to write a kitaba for his share. The author's expression 'lahuma' (for them two) is better than the author of al-Hidayah's expression 'between two men', because the dual includes both masculine and feminine, so it covers two men, two women, or a man and a woman. He said in al-Inaya: The benefit of the permission is that he does not have the right of rescission, as he would have if he did not permit. In al-Asl and according to most mashayikh, they did not stipulate a judgment or consent for the validity of rescission, but Imam Najm al-Din al-Nasafi stipulated a judgment or consent. This is the statement of Imam (Abu Hanifa). And they two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He is a mukatib for both of them, and what is received is between them. The basis of this is that kitaba is divisible according to Imam, and according to them it is not divisible, as mentioned in the chapter on emancipation. And in the commentary: The benefit of his permission to receive is that his right is cut off between...
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on kitaba for a jointly owned slave (al-'abd al-mushtarak) and presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani).

The specific case: A slave is owned by two people. One co-owner (A) gives permission to the other (B) to write a kitaba for A's share and to receive the payment. B writes the kitaba for A's share, receives some payment, then the slave becomes insolvent. The question: to whom does the received money belong?

Imam Abu Hanifa's position: The received money belongs to the one who received it (i.e., B, the contracting co-owner), because the permission enabled him to act. The benefit of the permission is that A loses his right to rescind the contract. According to most mashayikh, rescission does not require a court order or the other's consent, but Imam al-Nasafi stipulated such conditions. This ruling is based on the principle that kitaba is divisible (tatajazzi): each share can be independently contracted.

Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's position: The slave is a mukatib for both co-owners, and the payment is shared between them. This is because kitaba is not divisible (la tatajazzi): the contract is a single indivisible obligation. Therefore, any payment received belongs to both proportionally.

The passage notes that the author's phrasing 'lahuma' (to both) is more inclusive than the phrasing in al-Hidayah ('between two men') because it covers women as well.

This is a critical refinement of the earlier matn, showing how the legal consequence hinges on the nature of kitaba (divisible or not) and the effect of permission.

Key Terms
العبد المشترك (al-'abd al-mushtarak): A slave jointly owned by two or more persons.
تجزى الكتابة (tajazzi al-kitaba): The divisibility of the kitaba contract, meaning each share can be independently contracted and paid for.
الإذن (al-idhn): Permission from one co-owner to the other to contract the kitaba and receive payment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, when one co-owner permits the other to write a kitaba for his share and receive payment, the received money belongs to:
A) Both co-owners equally.
B) The contracting co-owner exclusively.
C) The slave.
D) The permitting co-owner.

Key Takeaway
The divisibility of kitaba determines whether payment belongs to the contracting co-owner alone or is shared with the permitting co-owner.

Kitaba of a Joint Slave: The Divisibility Dispute
Explains the ruling on joint slave kitaba with one partner's permission and the Imams' disagreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the divisibility of kitaba and apply them to determine the distribution of payments and emancipation in a joint slave kitaba scenario.

Core Idea
Imam Abu Hanifa holds kitaba divisible; the Sahibayn hold it indivisible, affecting payment ownership and emancipation.

This lesson examines an important internal disagreement within the Hanafi school regarding the kitaba (contract of manumission) of a jointly owned slave when one partner gives permission to the other to write a kitaba for his share. The core issue is whether the kitaba contract is divisible (tajzi'a) or not. Understanding this dispute is crucial for correctly applying the rules of kitaba in joint ownership cases.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and identify the core issue
Start by clearly describing the scenario: a slave jointly owned by two partners, one partner giving permission to the other to write a kitaba for his share. The central question is whether the kitaba is divisible – i.e., can it apply to only a partial share of the slave?
The permission is key; without it, the silent partner has the right to rescind the kitaba.
2
State Imam Abu Hanifa's position and his proof
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the kitaba is divisible. Therefore, the payment received by the writing partner belongs exclusively to him, and only his share is affected (emancipated upon full payment). His proof: the mukatab (slave under kitaba) owns half his earnings; the permission to receive payment on the share makes the payment the exclusive property of the receiver.
Imam's view is based on the principle that the slave's earnings are divided between the partners.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that the kitaba is indivisible. Therefore, the entire slave becomes a mukatab for both partners, and the payment is shared between them. Their proof: permission to write a kitaba for one's share implies permission for the whole, as the kitaba contract cannot be split; thus the slave is a mukatab for both by agency.
The Sahibayn analogize kitaba to other contracts like sale or emancipation, which are normally indivisible.
4
Determine the practical consequences (thamarah al-khilaf)
According to Imam, if the slave pays the full kitaba price, only the writing partner's share is freed, and the silent partner can take half of the payments received. According to the Sahibayn, full payment frees the entire slave, and the silent partner can reclaim from his partner or the slave if the partner is insolvent.
The difference affects the rights of both partners and the slave's status.
5
Note the tarjih if present
This text does not give a tarjih (preference) between the two positions. Later Hanafi works may prefer the Sahibayn's view or adopt a nuanced approach. The mufti should be aware of both views and the evidence for each.
The absence of tarjih indicates that both positions are considered valid within the school.

بعد الواحد قال رحمه الله : (عبد لهما إذن أحدهما لصاحبه أن يكاتب حصته بألف ويقبض بدل الكتابة فكاتب وقبض بعضه فعجز فالمقبوض للقابض) يعني إذا كان العبد بين اثنين إذن أحدهما لصاحبه إن يكاتب حظه . وتعبير أو تبرع بقضاء مهره وحصلت الفرقة من جهة المرأة حيث يرجع بالمهر والثمن لأن ذمة البائع والمرأة صلحت لوجوب الدين المتبرع عليها فأمكن الرجوع. ولو كان الشريك بالإذن مريضاً وأدى من كسبه قبله الثلث لأنه تبرع بعين ماله وفي الأول بالمنافع فالمتبرع بالمنافع يعتبر من جميع المال وبالعين من الثلث. وجه قولهما أن الإذن بكتابة نصيبه إذن بكتابة كله فإذا كاتبه صار كله مكاتباً نصيبه بالأصالة ونصيب شريكه بالوكالة فهو لأنه لم يخرج نصيبه من يده وبخلاف العتق وتعليق العتق بالشرط حيث لا يفسخ لأنه لا يقبل الفسخ. وفي العتابية : اعترض بأن الكتابة إما أن يعتبر فيها معنى المعاوضة أو معنى الإعتاق أو معنى تعليق العتق بأداء المال، ولو وجد شيء من ذلك من أحد الشريكين بغير إذن شريكه ليس للآخر ولاية الفسخ فمن أين ذلك في الكتابة؟ وأجيب بأن الكتابة ليست عيناً لكل واحد منهما وإنما يشتمل عليها فيجوز أن يكون فيها ولاية الفسخ لمعنى يوجبه وهو إلحاق الضرر، ولو أدى بدل الكتابة عتق نصيبه خاصة عند الإمام لما مر وللساكت أن يأخذ من الذي كاتبه نصف ما قبض لأنه كسب عبد مشترك بينهما ثم ينظر ؛ إن كاتب كله بألف لم يرجع على المكاتب بشيء مما أخذه منه شريكه لأنه مسلم له بدل نصيبه، وإن كاتب نصيبه فقط بألف رجع على المكاتب بما أخذه منه شريكه لأن الكل كان بدل نصيبه ولم يسلم له بعضه فيرجع عليه به وعندهما بالأداء عتق كله ورجع الساكت على شريكه إن كان موسراً وإلا فعلى العبد كما لو أعتقه وله أن يأخذ نصف ما بقي من الأكساب لأنه كسب عبد مشترك، ولو كاتبه الساكت بمائة دينار بعد الأول صار مكاتباً لهما . أما عند الإمام فظاهر لأنها تتجزأ، وأما عندهما فلأن الساكت كان له أن يفسخ فإذا كاتبه كان فسخاً منه في نصيبه وأيهما قبض شيئاً من يدل نصيبه لا يشاركه الآخر فيه وتعلق نصيب كل واحد منهما بجميع بدل الكتابة المسمى في كتابته، فإن أدى لهما معاً فالولاء لهما عندهم، وإن قدم أحدهما صار كمكاتبهما أعتقه أحدهما عتق نصيبه عند الإمام ويبقى نصيب صاحبه مكاتباً ولا ضمان ولا سعاية إلا أن يعجز المكاتب فيخير الساكت بين تضمين المعتق
Chapter on the Kitaba of the Joint Slave. It is valid. Since he completed the kitaba of a non-joint slave, he begins the kitaba of the joint slave because the original ruling is the absence of joint ownership; this is stated in Ghayat al-Bayan. Most commentators said: the mention of the kitaba of two after the kitaba of one is because two come after one. He (the author), may Allah have mercy on him, said: ('A slave owned by two, one of them gave permission to his partner to write a kitaba for his share for one thousand and to receive the kitaba payment, so he wrote the kitaba and received some of it, then the slave failed, so the received amount belongs to the one who received it.') Meaning if the slave is between two, one of them gave permission to his partner to write a kitaba for his share. The author's expression 'lihima' is more appropriate than the expression of the author of al-Hidayah who said 'between two men' because the dual form applies to both masculine and feminine, thus includes if they are two men, two women, or a man and a woman. In al-Inayah it is said: the benefit of permission is that he does not have the right of rescission as he would have if he did not give permission. In al-Asl and the majority of scholars did not stipulate for the validity of rescission a court order or consent, but the great scholar Najm al-Din al-Nasafi stipulated a court order or consent. This is the statement of Imam (Abu Hanifa). And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He is a mukatab for both of them and the received amount is between them. The basis is that kitaba is divisible according to Imam, and according to them it is not divisible as mentioned in the chapter on emancipation. In the commentary: the benefit of his permission to receive is that his right is cut off regarding what he received, and the receiver exclusively owns it because his permission to receive is permission for his slave to pay to him, except if he forbids him before payment, then his prohibition is valid because it is a gift that was not completed. The proof of Imam's statement is that the mukatab owns half of his earnings, so when he permitted the mukatab to spend it for his debt, his permission is valid and is completed by paying his debt with it, so the received amount belongs to the receiver. If the mukatab fails, the one who gave permission does not reclaim it even if his purpose (freedom) was not achieved because the one making a gift is the slave. If he reclaims, he reclaims from the slave, and the master does not owe a debt to his slave. This is unlike when a person donates payment of the price then it is reclaimed or destroyed before possession or the sale is rescinded, or donates payment of dower and separation occurs from the woman's side, where he reclaims the dower and price because the liability of the seller and woman became valid for the debt donated, so reclaim is possible. If the partner who gave permission was ill and payment was made from his earnings, it is effective from one-third because he donated from his actual property, while in the first case he donated from benefits; the donor of benefits is considered from the entire wealth, while the donor of actual property is considered from one-third. The proof of their (Sahibayn's) statement is that permission to write a kitaba for his share is permission to write a kitaba for the whole, so when he writes the kitaba, the whole becomes a mukatab: his share originally and his partner's share by agency, so he is a mukatab for both of them and the received amount is between them. He restricted it by saying 'permission' because if he wrote the kitaba without his partner's permission, his share becomes a mukatab and the silent partner has the right to rescind by consensus before the kitaba, to prevent harm to himself, unlike if he sold his share where he cannot rescind because there is no harm since his share does not leave his hand, and unlike emancipation and conditional emancipation where they cannot be rescinded because they do not accept rescission. In al-Atabiyyah, an objection is raised: kitaba either includes the meaning of exchange, emancipation, or conditional emancipation upon payment of money. If any of these occurs from one partner without the permission of the other, the other has no authority to rescind, so where does this come from in kitaba? The answer is that kitaba is not an identical thing for each of them but encompasses them, so it is possible that it includes the authority of rescission due to a reason that necessitates it, which is causing harm. If he pays the kitaba price, his share alone is freed according to Imam for the reason given, and the silent partner may take from the one who wrote the kitaba half of what he received because it is the earnings of a jointly owned slave between them. Then it is considered: if he wrote a kitaba for the whole for one thousand, he does not reclaim from the mukatab anything of what his partner took from him because it is surrendered to him as the price of his share. If he wrote a kitaba for his share only for one thousand, he reclaims from the mukatab what his partner took from him because the whole was the price of his share and part of it was not surrendered to him, so he reclaims it from him. According to them, upon payment the whole is freed, and the silent partner reclaims from his partner if he is wealthy; otherwise from the slave, as if he emancipated him. He may take half of the remaining earnings because it is earnings of a jointly owned slave. If the silent partner writes a kitaba for one hundred dinars after the first, he becomes a mukatab for both of them. According to Imam, this is clear because it is divisible. According to them, because the silent partner had the right to rescind, so when he writes the kitaba it is a rescission from him regarding his share. Whichever of them receives something from the kitaba price on behalf of his share, the other does not share it with him. The share of each of them is tied to the entire kitaba price specified in his kitaba. If he pays to both together, then the wala' is for both according to them. If he gives precedence to one, he becomes like their joint mukatab. If one of them emancipates him, his share is freed according to Imam, and the share of his partner remains as a mukatab. There is no guarantee or sa'y (earning) unless the mukatab fails, in which case the silent partner is given a choice between holding the one who emancipated liable
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the kitaba of a jointly owned slave when one partner gives permission to the other to write a kitaba for his share. The core issue is whether the kitaba contract is divisible (tajzi'a) or not. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that it is divisible, so the payment received by the partner who wrote the kitaba belongs exclusively to him, and only his share is affected. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that it is not divisible, so the entire slave becomes a mukatab for both partners, and the payment is shared between them. The commentary expands on the proofs for each position. Imam's proof: the mukatab owns half his earnings, so the permission to receive payment on his share is valid, making the received amount the sole property of the receiver. The Sahibayn's proof: permission to write a kitaba for one's share implies permission for the whole, as the kitaba is an indivisible contract; thus the slave becomes a mukatab for both partners by agency. The passage also discusses the silent partner's right to rescind when no permission is given, and it elaborates on the practical consequences: according to Imam, if the slave pays the full kitaba price, only the share of the writing partner is freed, and the silent partner may take half of the payments received. According to the Sahibayn, full payment frees the entire slave, and the silent partner can reclaim from his partner or the slave. The text also addresses scenarios of illness, multiple kitaba contracts, and the ruling on wala' (patronage) after emancipation.

Key Terms
الكتابة (al-kitaba): A contract between a master and his slave by which the slave agrees to pay a sum of money in installments in exchange for his freedom.
التجزئة (al-tajzi'a): Divisibility of the kitaba contract; Imam holds it is divisible, meaning the contract can apply to a share of the slave, while the Sahibayn hold it is indivisible and must apply to the entire slave.
الإذن (al-idhn): Permission given by one partner to the other to write a kitaba for his share.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if one partner gives permission to the other to write a kitaba for his share and the slave pays part of the price, what happens to the payment?
A) The payment is shared equally between both partners.
B) The payment belongs exclusively to the partner who received it.
C) The payment belongs to the slave.
D) The payment is given to the silent partner.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school is divided on the divisibility of kitaba, affecting the distribution of payments and emancipation of jointly owned slaves.

Kitabah of a Jointly Owned Slave with Permission and the Dispute on Earnings
Ruling on kitabah of a co-owned slave with permission, including difference between Imam and Sahibayn on earnings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ownership of earnings of a jointly owned slave when one partner permits kitabah, and explain the intra-madhhab dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
When one co-owner permits kitabah, Imam says earnings go to the permittor; Sahibayn say they are shared between both partners.

This lesson examines a nuanced issue in Hanafi fiqh concerning kitabah (a contract for a slave to earn freedom). When two partners co-own a slave and one permits the other to write kitabah, who owns the slave's earnings? Imam Abu Hanifa and his two main students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), differed on the interpretation of this permission. Understanding their proofs helps clarify the Hanafi framework for agency and property rights in co-ownership.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Issue
The central question: When one co-owner of a jointly owned slave permits kitabah for the entire slave (by allowing the partner to write the contract), who owns the earnings the slave makes before paying his freedom installments?
This is not a dispute on the validity of kitabah, but on the distribution of proceeds.
2
State Imam Abu Hanifa's Position and Proof
Imam holds that the earnings belong exclusively to the partner who gave permission. His proof: The permission for receipt is a direct grant to the slave to pay the permittor, so the payment becomes the permittor's property.
The key phrase: 'إذنه بالقبض إذن لعبده بالاداء إليه' (his permission for receipt is permission for his slave to pay him).
3
State the Sahibayn's Position and Proof
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) argue that earnings are shared equally between both co-owners. Their proof: Permission to write kitabah of one's share implies permission for the whole, making the slave mukatab for both partners, so earnings are owned jointly.
Key phrase: 'الإذن بكتابة نصيبه إذن بكتابة كله' (permission to write kitabah of his share is permission to write it for the whole).
4
Analyze the Practical Consequence (Thamarah al-Khilaf)
If the slave earns $1000, according to Imam, the permittor gets the entire amount. According to Sahibayn, each co-owner gets $500. This difference affects even cases where the permittor is terminally ill.
The passage also discusses a sub-case: if the permittor is sick, payment from earnings is limited to one-third of his wealth if considered a gift from property.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi (Relied-Upon Position)
Later Hanafi jurists preferred the view of the Sahibayn because it aligns better with the partnership nature of co-ownership. This is the operative position for fatwa.
Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah adopts the Sahibayn's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب كتابة العبد المشترك فيما قبضه ويختص به القابض لأن إذنه بالقبض إذن لعبده بالاداء إليه إلا إذا نهاه قبل الأداء فيصح نهيه لأنه تبرع لم يتم بعد اهـ. وجه قول الإمام أن المكاتب نصف كسبه له فإذا أذن للمكاتب أن يصرفه بدينه صح إذنه وتم بقضاء دينه به فكان المقبوض للقابض، فإن عجز المكاتب لا يرجع الآذن بذلك وإن لم يحصل مقصوده وهو الحرية لأن المتبرع عليه هو العبد، ولو رجع يرجع على العبد والمولى لا يستوجب على عبده ديناً بخلاف ما إذا تبرع شخص بقضاء الثمن ثم استحق أو هلك قبل القبض أو انفسخ البيع أو تبرع بقضاء مهره وحصلت الفرقة من جهة المرأة حيث يرجع بالمهر والثمن لأن ذمة البائع والمرأة صلحت لوجوب الدين المتبرع عليها فأمكن الرجوع. ولو كان الشريك بالإذن مريضاً وأدى من كسبه قبله الثلث لأنه تبرع بعين ماله وفي الأول بالمنافع فالمتبرع بالمنافع يعتبر من جميع المال وبالعين من الثلث. وجه قولهما أن الإذن بكتابة نصيبه إذن بكتابة كله فإذا كاتبه صار كله مكاتباً نصيبه بالأصالة ونصيب شريكه بالوكالة فهو مكاتب لهما والمقبوض بينهما
Chapter on the kitabah of the jointly owned slave: regarding what he receives, it is exclusively for the receiver because his permission for receipt is permission for his slave to pay to him, unless he forbade him before payment, then his prohibition is valid because it is a gratuitous contract not yet completed. The proof of Imam: the mukatab half of his earnings belongs to him; when he permits the mukatab to spend it for his debt, his permission is valid and is completed by paying his debt with it, so what is received belongs to the receiver. If the mukatab becomes unable, the permittor does not take back [the payment] even if his objective (freedom) is not achieved because the beneficiary is the slave. If he does take back, he takes from the slave, and the master cannot claim a debt from his slave. Unlike if a person voluntarily pays the price [of a sale] then the item is reclaimed or perished before receipt or the sale is rescinded, or if he voluntarily pays her dower and divorce occurs from the wife's side, then he can reclaim the dower and price because the seller's and woman's liability are valid for the debt incurred by the voluntary payment. If the partner who gave permission was sick and paid from his earnings, it is considered from the third of his wealth because he gives from his property, while in the first case it was from benefits; the one who gives benefits is considered from all wealth, and from property is from the third. The proof of the two (Sahibayn): permission to write kitabah of his share is permission to write kitabah of the whole, so when he writes it, the whole becomes mukatab, his share directly and his partner's share by agency, so he is mukatab for both, and what is received is between them.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage states a ruling on kitabah of a jointly owned slave when one partner gives permission. The commentator opens with the general rule: what the mukatab earns belongs exclusively to the one who permitted the receipt, because his permission is effectively a grant to his slave to pay him. He can revoke this before payment. Then Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is given: the mukatab owns half his earnings, so when the permitting partner authorizes him to spend it for his debt, the permission is effective and the payment is valid. The permittor cannot reclaim if the slave fails, even if freedom is not achieved, because the slave is the beneficiary. The Sahibayn's proof follows: the permission to write kitabah of one's share is permission for the whole kitabah, so the slave becomes mukatab for both partners, and earnings are shared. The passage also discusses the case where the permitting partner is terminally ill: payment from earnings is treated as a gift from all his wealth if from benefits, but from property it is limited to one-third.

Key Terms
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a kitabah contract to earn his freedom by paying installments.
إذن (idhn): Permission given by one co-owner to the other to write kitabah of his share.
كتابة (kitabah): A contract between a master and slave for the slave to earn and pay for freedom in installments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if one partner permits kitabah of his share of a jointly owned slave, who owns the slave's earnings before payment?
A) Both partners equally
B) The partner who gave permission
C) The slave himself
D) The silent partner

Key Takeaway
The ownership of earnings in kitabah of a co-owned slave hinges on how permission is interpreted: as a direct grant (Imam) or as agency (Sahibayn), with Sahibayn's view prevailing.

Kitabah Without Permission: Right to Annul and Liability
Ruling on kitabah without permission: annulment and liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the silent partner has the right to annul a kitabah made without permission, distinguish between Imam Abu Hanifa's and the Sahibayn's positions on the effect of payment, and apply the rule to determine liability.

Core Idea
Kitabah without permission is valid but gives the silent partner the right to annul due to harm.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the Hanafi ruling when one co-owner writes kitabah for a jointly owned slave without the other's consent. We will examine the right of the silent partner to annul the contract, the reasoning based on harm, and the divergent views of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the consequences of the slave's payment. By the end, you will understand the legal mechanism protecting the silent partner's interest.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the legal classification of a kitabah contract made by one partner without the other's permission. Is it void, valid, or subject to annulment?
The text states it is sahih (valid) but the silent partner has the right to annul (faskh) to prevent harm.
2
Analyze the right to annul (faskh)
Examine why the silent partner has this right. Compare with sale (where no annulment exists) and emancipation (where annulment is not possible). Understand the role of harm (idrar) as the basis.
The qiyas panel in the toolbox helps contrast kitabah with sale.
3
Examine the objection from al-Itabiyyah
Understand the objection that kitabah is composite of compensation and emancipation, neither of which allows annulment. How does the Hanafi response justify annulment based on the unique harm of kitabah?
The response affirms that kitabah is a distinct contract where harm justifies annulment.
4
Trace the effects of payment: Imam vs Sahibayn
Follow what happens when the slave pays the kitabah price. According to Imam, only the writer's share becomes free; according to the Sahibayn, the whole slave becomes free. Consider the implications for ownership and compensation.
The mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's view, but both are taught for understanding ikhtilaf.
5
Determine liabilities after payment
Who can sue whom? Under Imam, the silent partner takes half of the earnings from the writer. Under Sahibayn, the silent partner sues the writer if wealthy, else the slave. Also consider forced labor (si'ayah) if the slave becomes unable.
The text also covers the scenario where the silent partner later writes his own kitabah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قيد بقوله «إذن» لأنه لو كاتبه بغير إذن شريكه صار نصيبه مكاتباً وللساكت أن يفسخ بالإجماع قبل أن الكتابة دفعاً للضرر عن نفسه بخلاف ما إذا باع نصيبه حيث لا تفسخ لأنه لا ضرر فيه لأنه لم يؤد من بدل يخرج نصيبه من يده وبخلاف العتق وتعليق العتق بالشرط حيث لا يفسخ لأنه لا يقبل الفسخ. وفي العتابية : اعترض بأن الكتابة إما أن يعتبر فيها معنى المعاوضة أو معنى الإعتاق أو معنى تعليق العتق بأداء المال، ولو وجد شيء من ذلك من أحد الشريكين بغير إذن شريكه ليس للآخر ولاية الفسخ فمن أين ذلك في الكتابة؟ وأجيب بأن الكتابة ليست عيناً لكل واحد منهما وإنما يشتمل عليها فيجوز أن يكون فيها ولاية الفسخ لمعنى يوجبه وهو إلحاق الضرر، ولو أدى بدل الكتابة عتق نصيبه خاصة عند الإمام لما مر وللساكت أن يأخذ من الذي كاتبه نصف ما قبض لأنه كسب عبد مشترك بينهما ثم ينظر ؛ إن كاتب كله بألف لم يرجع على المكاتب بشيء مما أخذه منه شريكه لأنه مسلم له بدل نصيبه، وإن كاتب نصيبه فقط بألف رجع على المكاتب بما أخذه منه شريكه لأن الكل كان بدل نصيبه ولم يسلم له بعضه فيرجع عليه به وعندهما بالأداء عتق كله ورجع الساكت على شريكه إن كان موسراً وإلا فعلى العبد كما لو أعتقه وله أن يأخذ نصف ما بقي من الأكساب لأنه كسب عبد مشترك، ولو كاتبه الساكت بمائة دينار بعد الأول صار مكاتباً لهما . أما عند الإمام فظاهر لأنها تتجزى، وأما عندهما فلأن الساكت كان له أن يفسخ فإذا كاتبه كان فسخاً منه في نصيبه وأيهما قبض شيئاً من بدل نصيبه لا يشاركه الآخر فيه وتعلق نصيب كل واحد منهما بجميع بدل الكتابة المسمى في كتابته، فإن أدى لهما معاً فالولاء لهما عندهم، وإن قدم أحدهما صار كمكاتبهما أعتقه أحدهما عتق نصيبه عند الإمام ويبقى نصيب صاحبه مكاتباً ولا ضمان ولا سعاية إلا أن يعجز المكاتب فيخير الساكت بين تضمين المعتق
Qualified by the word 'permission': because if he wrote kitabah without his partner's permission, his share becomes mukatab, and the silent partner has the right to annul by consensus before the kitabah takes effect, to ward off harm from himself. Unlike if he sold his share, where there is no annulment because there is no harm—since no payment is made to remove his share from his hand. And unlike emancipation or conditional emancipation, where there is no annulment because they are not revocable. In al-Itabiyyah: an objection [is raised]: kitabah either involves compensation, emancipation, or conditional emancipation on payment; if any of these occurs from one partner without the other's permission, the other has no power to annul—so where does this right come from? The answer: kitabah is not identical to any of these alone; it combines them, so it is permissible to have the power of annulment for a reason that necessitates it, namely causing harm. If he paid the kitabah price, his share becomes free according to Imam; the silent partner may take from the one who wrote the kitabah half of what he received because it is earnings of a jointly owned slave. Then it is considered: if he wrote kitabah of the whole for a thousand [dirhams], he does not sue the mukatab for anything his partner took from him because he concedes the price of his share. If he wrote kitabah of his share only for a thousand, he sues the mukatab for what his partner took from him because the whole was the price of his share and part of it did not remain with him. According to the two (Sahibayn), upon payment the whole becomes free, and the silent partner sues his partner if he is wealthy, otherwise the slave—as if he emancipated him—and he may take half of the remaining earnings because it is earnings of a jointly owned slave. If the silent partner later writes kitabah for a hundred dinars after the first, he becomes mukatab for both. According to Imam, it is apparent because kitabah is divisible; according to them, because the silent partner had the right to annul, so when he writes kitabah it is an annulment of his share. Whichever one receives something from the price of his share, the other does not share it with him, and the share of each is attached to the entire kitabah price specified in his kitabah. If he pays both together, the wala is for both; if he pays one first, he becomes like their mukatab; if one emancipates him, his share becomes free according to Imam, and the other's share remains mukatab—no liability or forced labor unless the mukatab becomes unable; then the silent partner chooses between suing the emancipator
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage covers the case where one partner writes kitabah of a jointly owned slave without the other's permission. The ruling: the silent partner has the right to annul the kitabah to prevent harm, unlike in sale or emancipation. An objection from al-Itabiyyah questions this right, pointing out that kitabah is a composite contract; the answer is that the right to annul is granted due to the harm caused. Then the effects of payment are detailed: according to Imam, payment frees only the writer's share, and the silent partner can take half of what the writer received from the slave's earnings. If the writer wrote kitabah for the whole slave, he cannot reclaim from the mukatab; if only for his share, he can. According to Sahibayn, payment frees the whole slave, and the silent partner sues the writer if wealthy, otherwise the slave. The passage also covers the case where the silent partner later writes his own kitabah, and the rules of wala and liability upon inability.

Key Terms
فسخ (faskh): The right of the silent partner to annul the kitabah contract due to harm
تضمين (tadmeen): Suing for compensation, either the partner or the mukatab
سعاية (si'ayah): Forced labor for the mukatab to earn for the partner's share

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what happens if one partner writes kitabah without the other's permission and the slave pays the kitabah price?
A) The whole slave becomes free
B) Only the writer's share becomes free
C) The kitabah is void
D) The silent partner must also write kitabah

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a kitabah without consent is met with a right to annul, and the effects of payment depend on whether the imam or the sahibayn's view is followed.

Divisibility of Istilad in Jointly Owned Mukatabah
Ruling with proof on divisibility of istilad in mukatabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the divisibility of istilad in a jointly owned mukatabah and apply the ruling to determine the umm walad status and compensation owed.

Core Idea
Istilad is divisible in kitabah according to Imam Abu Hanifa; the first co-owner's child establishes umm walad status exclusively.

This passage from al-Kanz al-Daqa'iq presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a jointly owned slave woman who is made mukatabah and bears children from both co-owners. The core issue is whether the legal status of umm walad (being the mother of the master's child) can be divided among co-owners when the slave is under kitabah. Imam Abu Hanifa's view leads to different consequences for lineage and financial compensation compared to the Sahibayn. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply Hanafi principles of ownership and partial legal status.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the contract
There are two joint owners of a slave woman. They both write kitabah (a contract of manumission by payment) for her. She is thus partially free and partially owned.
2
Sequence of events
First, one co-owner has intercourse with her, she gives birth, and he claims the child. Then the second co-owner does the same. She later becomes unable to pay the kitabah (عجزت).
The order matters for determining whose child establishes umm walad status.
3
State Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling
Imam holds that istilad (creating an umm walad) is divisible. Thus the first co-owner's child makes her his umm walad exclusively. He must pay his partner half her value and half the dower (عقر). The second's child is his son, but he must pay the dower and the child's value.
Compensation is based on the value of the slave and the child, and the dower is a fixed amount for unlawful intercourse.
4
State the Sahibayn's ruling
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, istilad is indivisible. The first co-owner's child makes her his umm walad entirely, and she remains his mukatabah completely. He owes his partner half her value (Abu Yusuf) or the lesser of half her value and half the remaining kitabah price (Muhammad). The second child's lineage is not established.
The difference between the two Sahibayn is in the calculation of compensation.
5
Identify the basis of the ikhtilaf
The entire dispute hinges on whether istilad (the act of begetting a child that gives umm walad status) is considered divisible when the slave is jointly owned and under kitabah. Imam sees it as divisible; the Sahibayn see it as indivisible.
This affects not only status but also financial liabilities and lineage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله: (أمة بينهما كاتباها فوطئها أحدهما فولدت فادعاه ثم وطئ الآخر فولدت فادعاه فعجزت فهي أم ولد للأول ويغرم لشريكه نصف قيمتها ونصف عقرها وضمن شريكه عقرها وقيمة الولد وهو ابنه وهذا قول الإمام. وعندهما هي أم ولد للأول وهي مكاتبته كلها وعليه نصف قيمتها لشريكه عند الثاني وعند الثالث الأقل من نصف القيمة ومن نصف ما بقي من بدل الكتابة ولا يثبت نسب الولد الآخر من الآخر ولا يكون له الولد بالقيمة ويغرم العقر لها وهذا الاختلاف مبني على تجزئ الاستيلاد في المكاتبة فعنده يتجزئ،
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'A slave woman jointly owned, they both wrote kitabah for her. One had intercourse with her, she gave birth and he claimed the child. Then the other had intercourse, she gave birth and he claimed it. Then she became unable (to pay). She is an umm walad for the first, and he pays his partner half her value and half her dower (for intercourse). His partner is liable for her dower and the value of the child, and it is his son. This is the statement of Imam. According to the two (Sahibayn), she is umm walad for the first, and she is his mukatabah entirely, and he owes his partner half her value according to the second, and according to the third (Muhammad) the lesser of half the value and half the remaining kitabah price. The lineage of the other child is not established from the other, nor does he get the child for the value, and he pays the dower for her. This difference is based on the divisibility of istilad in the mukatabah: according to him (Imam), it is divisible.'
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This matn presents a specific case of a jointly owned slave woman who is made mukatabah. Both partners write kitabah for her. The first partner has intercourse, she bears a child he claims. Then the second partner also has intercourse, she bears another child he claims. She becomes unable to pay. Imam Abu Hanifa rules: she becomes umm walad exclusively for the first, because istilad (begetting a child) is divisible in mukatabah. Thus the first pays his partner half her value and half the dower (for the unlawful intercourse), while the second is liable for the dower and the value of the child (his son). According to Sahibayn, istilad is not divisible: the first gets her as umm walad entirely, but his share of the kitabah is unaffected. The second (Abu Yusuf) says he pays half her value; the third (Muhammad) says he pays the lesser of half the value or half the remaining kitabah price. The second child's lineage is not established. The entire difference hinges on whether istilad (impregnation leading to status of umm walad) can be divided in a mukatabah.

Key Terms
أم ولد (umm walad): A slave woman who bears a child to her master, gaining freedom upon his death
استيلاد (istilad): The act of impregnating a slave woman, making her umm walad
عقر (aqr): Dower or compensation paid for unlawful intercourse with a slave woman
مكاتبة (mukatabah): A contract of manumission by installment payments; the slave is partially owned until full payment

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what does the first co-owner pay to his partner in the jointly owned mukatabah case?
A) Half the slave's value and half the dower
B) Full value of the slave and dower
C) Half the remaining kitabah price
D) Nothing, because the second co-owner's intercourse was unlawful

Key Takeaway
The divisibility of istilad in kitabah determines whether umm walad status attaches exclusively to the first co-owner (Imam) or requires compensation adjustments (Sahibayn).

Dispute on the Status of a Child Purchased by a Makatib
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the kitabah status of a purchased child

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a child purchased by a makatib and identify the practical consequences of each view.

Core Idea
A purchased child does not enter the kitabah contract according to Abu Hanifa; the master may demand immediate payment or reclaim the child as a slave.

You already know that a child born to a makatib during the kitabah period automatically enters the contract. But what about a child the makatib purchases himself? The Hanafi imams disagreed on this point. In this lesson, we examine the reasoning of Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, and the practical difference it makes in the master's rights and the child's status.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position (Imam's view)
Identify the ruling given in the matn: if a makatib leaves a purchased child, the master may demand immediate payment of the kitabah price or take the child as a slave. Note that this is Imam Abu Hanifa's position.
The matn's absolute wording supports Imam's view.
2
Identify the opposing view of the Sahibayn
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the purchased child is treated like a child born during the kitabah: he strives for his payments on the original schedule and is not subject to immediate demand or re-enslavement.
The Sahibayn analogize the purchased child to a born child.
3
Analyze the reasoning of each side
Imam argues that deferment is established by contract condition and only applies to those who entered the contract; the purchased child was not a party. The Sahibayn argue that the child becomes like the makatib's own person, as evidenced by the master's ability to free him.
The passage includes responses to objections from other chapters.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response to the objection
An objector points to the rule that a makatib buying his father or son enters them into kitabah. The response distinguishes that this is a fresh kitabah, not extension. Also, immediate freeing upon payment is due to necessity, not extension.
The commentary uses al-Kafi to support this distinction.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
Under Imam's view, the master can demand full payment immediately or re-enslave the child if payment is not made. Under the Sahibayn, the child continues to pay installments and cannot be re-enslaved immediately.
The mufta bihi is Imam's view, as indicated by the matn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يعني أنه قد مر عن الحاضر أيضاً. وفي الولوالجية وإذا مات المكاتب عن ولد مولود في الكتابة وولد مشتري معها فعندهما يسعيان في نجوم الأم فما اتصل في يد كل واحد منهما بعد موت الأم فهو له خاصة، وعند الإمام المولود يسعى على نجوم الأم ويؤدي بدل الكتابة وهو المطالب ويسعى الولد المشتري ويأخذ من كسبه ويؤجره بأمر القاضي، وما فضل يكون ميراثاً الأم فيكون بينهما. وفي الأصل الولد المولود في الكتابة يسعى في ديون الأب. قال رحمه الله : (ولو ترك ولداً مشتري عجل البدل حالاً أو رد رقيقاً وظاهر إطلاق المتن أنه لا فرق في المشتري بين أن يكون ولد بعد الكتابة أو قبلها وسيأتي البيان، وهذا عند الإمام. وعندهما يسعى على نجومه كالمولود في الكتابة لأنه صار بمنزلته حتى جاز للمولى إعتاقه كما يجوز إعتاقه المكاتب بنفسه بخلاف سائر أكساب المكاتب فإنه لا يملك إعتاقه. وللإمام أن الأجل يثبت بالشرط في العقد فيثبت في حق من دخل تحت الكتابة والمشتري لم يدخل تحت العقد لأنه لم يضف إليه العقد ولم يسر حكمه إليه لكونه منفصلاً وقت الكتابة، وأورد في أول فصل المكاتب أن المكاتب إذا اشترى أباه أو ابنه دخل في كتابته، وأيضاً لو لم يسر حكمه إليه لما عتق عنده بأداء بدل الكتابة حالاً وأجيب أن المراد بدخول الولد المشتري في كتابه أبيه ليس السراية حكم عقد الكتابة الذي جرى بين المكاتب را ولاه إليه بل يجعل المكاتب مكاتباً لولده باشترائه اياه تحقيقاً للصلة وبأن عتق الولد المشتري عنده بأداء بدل الكتابة حالاً ليس لأجل السراية أيضاً بل لضرورة المكاتب إذا ذاك بمنزلة من مات عن وفاء، وقد أفصح عنه في الكافي حيث قال : وكان ينبغي أن يباع بعد موته لفوات المتبوع ولكن إذا عجل وأعطى من ساعته صار كأنه مات عن وفاء بخلاف المولود في الكتابة لأنه من مائه بعد الكتابة.
He means that it has already been mentioned from the present [scholar] as well. And in al-Walwalijiyya: If the makatib dies leaving a child born during the kitabah and a purchased child with her, then according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), both strive for the payments of the mother; whatever is earned in the hand of each after the mother's death is specifically his. According to Imam [Abu Hanifa]: the child born [during kitabah] strives for the payments of the mother and pays the kitabah payment, and he is the one demanded; and the purchased child strives and takes from his earnings, and he hires himself out by the judge's order, and whatever surplus remains becomes inheritance for the mother, so it is between them. And in al-Asl: the child born during kitabah strives for the debts of the father. He (the author) said: (If he leaves a purchased child, he hastens the payment immediately or returns him as a slave). And the apparent absolute wording of the matn indicates that there is no difference in the purchased child between being born after the kitabah or before it, and the explanation will come. And this is according to Imam. According to them (the two disciples), he strives for his payments like the child born during kitabah because he has become like him, to the extent that it is permissible for the master to manumit him just as it is permissible for the makatib to manumit him himself, unlike other earnings of the makatib, for he does not have the right to manumit [from them]. For Imam [the reasoning is] that the deferment is established by condition in the contract, so it is established for the one who enters under the kitabah, and the purchased child did not enter under the contract because the contract was not attached to him and its ruling did not extend to him because he was separate at the time of kitabah. And it was objected in the first chapter of al-Makatib that if the makatib buys his father or his son, he enters into his kitabah. Also, if its ruling did not extend to him, he would not be freed according to him by paying the kitabah payment immediately. He answered that the meaning of the entry of the purchased child into the kitabah of his father is not the extension of the ruling of the kitabah contract that occurred between the makatib and his master, but rather the makatib is made a makatib for his son by purchasing him, to achieve connection. And that the freeing of the purchased child according to him by paying the kitabah payment immediately is not because of extension either, but due to the necessity that the makatib at that time is like one who died with sufficient [estate]. And it was clarified in al-Kafi where he said: He should have been sold after his death due to the loss of the principal, but if he hastened and gave from his same hour, he becomes as if he died with sufficient [estate], unlike the child born during kitabah because he is from his [the makatib's] fluid after the kitabah.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the status of a child purchased by a makatib (a slave under a contract of manumission). The matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq states that if a makatib leaves a purchased child, the master may either demand immediate payment of the kitabah price or take the child back as a slave. The commentator, Zayla'i, explains that this ruling is according to Imam Abu Hanifa. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), the purchased child is treated like a child born during the kitabah: he continues to work and pay installments, and is not subject to immediate payment or re-enslavement. The Sahibayn argue that the purchased child becomes like the makatib's own person, so he can be freed by the master just as the makatib could free him from his own earnings. Imam Abu Hanifa's reasoning is that the deferment (ajal) in the kitabah contract is a condition that applies only to those who enter the contract; the purchased child was not a party to the contract at its inception, so no deferment applies to him. An objection is raised from an earlier chapter where a makatib who buys his father or son causes them to enter his kitabah. The response is that such entry is not due to extension of the original contract but rather a fresh kitabah created by the purchase to maintain familial ties. Similarly, if the child is freed by immediate payment, it is not because of extension but because the makatib at that point is analogous to one who died with sufficient estate. The passage cites al-Kafi to support this distinction.

Key Terms
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a contract of manumission (kitabah) with his master, agreeing to pay a sum in installments in exchange for freedom upon completion.
كتابة (kitabah): A contract between a master and a slave whereby the slave agrees to pay a specified amount in installments, and upon full payment becomes free.
مشتري (mushtari): A child purchased by the makatib; in this context, a child acquired by the makatib during the kitabah period.
بدل (badal): The payment (price) due under the kitabah contract; here, the master may demand immediate payment of the entire remaining sum.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what option does the master have if a makatib dies leaving a purchased child?
A) The purchased child automatically enters the kitabah and continues installments.
B) The master may demand immediate payment of the kitabah price or take the child as a slave.
C) The child is freed immediately regardless of payment.
D) The master must return the child to slavery without any option.

Key Takeaway
A child purchased by a makatib does not automatically enter the kitabah contract; according to the relied-upon Hanafi view, the master may demand immediate payment or re-enslave the child.

Purity of Master's Ownership After Mukatab's Inability
Ruling with proof on purity of master's ownership after 'ajz

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the purity of a master's ownership of a mukatab's earnings after 'ajz (inability) and explain the reasoning based on the prohibition of initial taking due to degradation.

Core Idea
Prohibition attaches to the initial taking due to degradation, not to ownership after a legitimate change of hands.

When a mukatab (slave under kitaba) becomes unable to pay his installments ('ajz), the contract is annulled and the slave returns to full slavery. At that point, the master gains ownership of the mukatab's earnings that were in his possession. But is that property considered pure (tayyib) for the master, or is it tainted by the earlier prohibition against taking the mukatab's earnings? This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq resolves the question by focusing on the underlying cause of the prohibition: the degradation (idhlal) involved in the act of taking, not the ownership itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the master's acquisition of the mukatab's earnings after 'ajz. The ruling according to the correct Hanafi view is that it is pure (tayyib) and lawful for the master to use.
The disputed point is the purity, not the permissibility of ownership itself.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
The evidence is an analogy (qiyas) with charity: a poor person who takes zakah (which was originally prohibited for the wealthy) may leave it to a wealthy heir, and it becomes pure for the heir because the heir did not perform the initial prohibited taking. Similarly, a poor person who later becomes wealthy may keep the zakah he took earlier because his taking was permissible at the time.
The key is the change of ownership and the absence of the degrading act from the current owner.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The analogy shows that the prohibition is attached to the act of taking due to degradation (idhlal), not to the property itself after it changes hands. The master never took the earnings during the kitaba (that would have been prohibited); he only acquires them after 'ajz through ownership transfer. Hence the prohibition does not carry over.
This distinguishes it from the case where a poor person gifts charity to a rich person: the rich person receives from the poor person, not from the original giver, but the taking from the poor person is still degrading for the rich person? Actually the text argues that the rich person's taking from the poor person also involves degradation. But the master's acquisition after 'ajz is not a 'taking' from the mukatab in the same sense.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Muhammad held that the master acquires the earnings as a fresh (ibtida'i) ownership, so it is pure. Imam Abu Yusuf held that the master had a type of ownership during the kitaba that is merely confirmed by 'ajz, so no new ownership arises, thus it remains impure.
The text states 'al-sahih' (the correct view) is that it is pure by consensus, siding with Muhammad.
5
Determine the tarjih
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that the master's ownership is pure. The authority is the consensus (ijma') mentioned in the text and the preference of later Hanafi scholars.
The practical consequence: if the master sells or uses the property, it is valid and lawful.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب المكاتب باب موت المكاتب وعجزه وموت المولى ١١٣ فعجز دفع أو فدى وكذا إن جنى مكاتب ولم يقض به فعجز فإن قضى به عليه في بده كان للمكاتب أن يمنع المولى من التصرف في ملكه ولم يكن للمولى أن يمنع المكاتب من التصرف وبالعجز ينعكس الحال وليس هذا إلا تبدل الملك للمولى ولئن كان فلا يسلم مثله بمنزلة تبدل العين فصار كالفقير يموت عن صدقة أخذها يطيب ذلك لوارثه الغني لما ذكرنا، وكذا إذا استغنى الفقير يطيب له ما أخذ من الزكاة وكذا ابن السبيل إذا وصل إلى بلده وفي مال من الصدقة لأن المحرم عليه ابتداء الأخذ لما فيه من الذل فلا يرخص من غير ضرورة. ولو أباح الفقير للغني أو الهاشمي عين ما أخذ من الزكاة لم يحل له لأن الملك لم يتبدل، ولك أن تقول المحرم ابتداء الأخذ إلى آخره. فعلى هذا لو أباح الفقير للغني أو الهاشمي ينبغي أن يطيب له لأنه لم يوجد منهما ابتداء الفعل المحرم المقترن بالإذلال. قلنا : إن لم يوجد منهما الأخذ من يد المتصدق وجد منهما الأخذ من يد الفقير فقد تحقق في حقهما سبب الخبث، ولك أن تقول ليس المحرم نفس الأخذ فقط بل نفس الأخذ المقرون بالإذلال أن لا يكون خبيثاً، ونظيره المشتري شراء فاسداً لا يطيب بالإباحة ولو ملكه يطيب، ولو عجز المكاتب قبل الأداء إلى المولى يطيب للمولى عند محمد لأن المولى يملك ما في يده ملكاً مبتدأ حتى تنتقض إجارته، وعند أبي يوسف لا يطيب له لأنه إذا عجز لا يملك المولى إكسابه ملكاً مبتدأ أو إنما له فيه نوع ملك فيتأكد بالعجز ولم يتجدد له ملك، ولهذا لا ينتقض إجارته بالعجز كما في العقد المأذون إذا حجر عليه ، والصحيح أنه يطيب له بالإجماع لما ذكرنا أن المحرم ابتداء الأخذ ولم يوجد من المولى الأخذ ا هـ.
Book of the Mukatab: Chapter on the death of the mukatab, his inability, and the death of the master. So if he becomes unable, he pays or ransoms. Similarly, if a mukatab commits a crime and the judge has not passed judgment on it, then he becomes unable... etc.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling when a mukatab becomes unable (ajz) and the purity (tayyib) of the master's ownership of the mukatab's earnings. The text begins by describing a scenario where the mukatab's property initially belongs to him, and the master is restricted from disposing of it. Upon 'ajz, ownership transfers to the master. The commentary compares this to a poor person who takes charity and then dies: the wealthy heir may use it because the taking was permissible for the poor person. The key principle is that the prohibition is on the initial taking due to degradation (dhull), not on subsequent ownership after the property changes hands. The passage then addresses an objection: if a poor person gifts the charity to a rich person or a Hashimi, why is it not allowed? The answer is that the rich person received it from the poor person, not from the original giver, so the degradation persists. A dispute between Muhammad and Abu Yusuf is presented: Muhammad holds that the master's ownership is fresh (ibtida') and thus pure; Abu Yusuf holds that the master had only a partial ownership that becomes confirmed but not renewed. The correct view (sahih) is that it is pure by consensus because the master did not perform the initial prohibited taking.

Key Terms
العجز (al-ʿajz): Inability of the mukatab to pay the kitaba installments, resulting in annulment of the contract.
الخبث (al-khubth): Legal impurity or prohibition affecting the lawfulness of property, here arising from degradation (dhull) in taking charity or master's earnings.
الإذلال (al-idhlāl): The humiliation or degradation associated with taking charity or master's earnings, which is the cause of prohibition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct Hanafi view, why is the master's ownership of the mukatab's earnings after 'ajz considered pure?
A) Because the master is the owner of the slave and all his property.
B) Because the prohibition on taking earnings is temporary and ends with 'ajz.
C) Because the master did not perform any initial act of taking that involves degradation.
D) Because the earnings are a gift from the mukatab to the master.

Key Takeaway
The purity of the master's ownership after 'ajz hinges on the absence of an initial degraded taking; the prohibition does not follow the property across a legitimate change of ownership.

Master's Option After 'Ajz When Slave Commits Jinaya Before Kitaba
Matn and sharh on master's option after slave's inability ('ajz) following pre-kitaba crime.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that the master has an option to pay the blood money (fida') or surrender the slave after the mukatab's 'ajz, and explain the reasoning (talil) comparing it to cases of freeing or selling the offending slave without knowledge.

Core Idea
The master's ignorance at kitaba gives an option, not liability; obstacle removed at 'ajz.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq and its commentary by Ibn Nujaym presents a case where a slave commits a crime before being written as a mukatab. The master, unaware of the crime, writes the kitaba. Later, the slave becomes unable ('ajz). The question: what is the master's obligation? The author clarifies that the master has an option: either surrender the slave to the victim or pay the blood money (arsh). The reasoning compares to other dispositions like freeing or selling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case
A slave commits a crime (jinaya) before the master writes kitaba; the master is ignorant of the crime.
2
Note the effect of kitaba
The kitaba contract prevents the master from surrendering the slave temporarily; the obstacle is on the verge of ceasing because the slave may later become unable.
3
Understand the rule for 'ajz
When the slave becomes unable to pay, the obstacle (kitaba) is removed, and the victim's right revives against the slave.
4
State the option
The master may choose either to pay the blood money (fida') or surrender the slave to the victim.
5
Compare to freeing/selling
If the master had freed or sold the slave ignorantly, he would owe the lesser of value or arsh immediately. The difference is the temporary nature of the obstacle, which allows the option after 'ajz.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فينبغي قال قال يصير عجز صار رحمه الله : (وإن جنى عبد فكاتبه سید جاهلاً بها فعجز دفع أو فدى) يعني المولي بالخيار إن شاء دفع العبد وإن شاء فداه بالأرش لأنه لو كاتبه وهو لا يعلم بالجناية لزمه قيمته لأنه لم يصر مختاراً للفداء بالمكاتبة من غير علم وقد امتنع الدفع بفعله من غير أن مختاراً للفداء فيجب عليه الأقل من قيمته ومن الأرش كما إذا أعتقه أو دبره أو استولد الأمة أو باعه بعد ما جنى من غير علم بها إلا أن المانع من الدفع على شرف الزوال فلم ينتقل حق ولي الجناية من العبد إلى القيمة، فإذا عجز زال المانع فيتخير بين الدفع والفداء على القاعدة ا هـ :
He (the author) said: (And if a slave commits a crime and his master writes him kitaba ignorant of it, then he becomes unable, he pays or ransoms.) Meaning: the master has the option, if he wishes he surrenders the slave, and if he wishes he ransoms him with the blood money...
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage presents a matn from Kanz al-Daqaiq with its sharh. The ruling: If a slave commits a crime (jinaya) before being written as a mukatab, and the master writes him as mukatab without knowing about the crime, then if the slave later becomes unable (ajz), the master has a choice: either surrender the slave to the victim's guardian or pay the blood money (arsh). The reason is that by writing the kitaba, the master did not deliberately choose to pay the blood money (fida) because he was ignorant. Therefore, the master is only liable for the lesser of the slave's value or the blood money, similar to cases where the master frees or sells an offending slave without knowledge. However, the obstacle to surrendering the slave (the kitaba) is temporary and likely to end (with 'ajz). So when 'ajz occurs, the obstacle is removed, and the master can either pay or surrender.

Key Terms
الفداء (al-fidā'): Payment of blood money (arsh) by the master to the victim instead of surrendering the slave.
الأرش (al-arsh): The compensation for injuries (blood money) proportional to the harm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
After the mukatab's 'ajz, what are the two options available to the master?
A) Keep the slave or free him.
B) Pay the slave's value or the blood money.
C) Surrender the slave or pay the blood money.
D) Cancel the kitaba or sell the slave.

Key Takeaway
The master's ignorance does not absolve him, but after the slave's inability, he has an option: surrender or pay the blood money, based on the temporary nature of the obstacle.

Mukatab's Jinaya Before Judgment and After 'Ajz
Matn and commentary on the same option when a mukatab commits a crime before judgment and then becomes unable.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the master's liability when a mukatab commits a crime before judgment and then becomes unable, and distinguish the ruling before and after 'ajz.

Core Idea
Before 'ajz, master pays lesser of value or arsh; after 'ajz, master has option to pay or surrender.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq extends the general rule of slave jinaya to a mukatab who commits a crime before a judge passes judgment and then becomes unable to fulfill his kitaba. The commentary clarifies the rationale based on the master's right to the mukatab's earnings and draws an analogy with mudabbar and umm walad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and timing
A mukatab commits a crime (jinaya) before a judge rules on it, then becomes unable (ajz) to pay his kitaba.
2
Ruling before 'ajz
The master must pay the lesser of the mukatab's value or the arsh (blood money). Reason: surrender is impossible because the mukatab has a stronger right to his earnings.
The obligation is limited to the lesser amount.
3
Ruling after 'ajz
The master has the option to pay the arsh or surrender the mukatab, just like a regular slave.
After 'ajz, the mukatab loses his right to earnings, so surrender becomes possible.
4
Multiple crimes
If multiple crimes are committed before judgment, the master owes only one value (the slave's value).
This is regardless of the number of crimes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وكذا إن جنى مكاتب ولم يقض به فعجز) حكمه كالأول لأنه لما وجناية القن يخير فيها المولى بين الدفع والفداء على ما عرف وقبل أن يعجز يجب الأقل من الأرش لأن دفعه متعذر وهو أحق بكسبه من المولى وموجب الجناية عند تعذر الدفع يجب على من يكون له الكسب، ألا ترى أن جناية المدبر وأم الولد توجب على المولى الأقل من قيمته ومن الأرش لما أنه أحق بكسبهما، ولو جنى جناية بعد الحكم عليه بالأولى فهي كالأولى. وإذا اجتمعت الجنايات في وقت قبل القضاء لم يلزمه إلا قيمة واحدة كذا في المبسوط. وفيه : وإذا جنى العبد المكاتب ثم عتق فهو على خياره، وإن عجز فالخيار للمولى، البحر الرائق / ج ۸/ ۸٤
He (the author) said: (And similarly, if a mukatab commits a crime and it has not been judged, then he becomes unable.) Its ruling is like the first case...
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage extends the previous ruling to a mukatab who commits a crime before a judge passes judgment and then becomes unable. The ruling is the same as the first case: the master has the option to pay or surrender. The reason is that before 'ajz, the master is only liable for the lesser of the slave's value or arsh because it is impossible to surrender the mukatab while he is earning his freedom. The master is entitled to the mukatab's earnings, so the liability attaches to him, similar to a mudabbar (slave promised freedom after master's death) or umm walad (slave mother of master's child). If multiple crimes are committed before judgment, only one value is owed.

Key Terms
المدبر (al-mudabbar): A slave who has been promised freedom upon the master's death (tadbir).
أم الولد (umm al-walad): A slave woman who has borne a child to her master, with special status under Hanafi law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Before the mukatab's 'ajz, what is the master's liability for the mukatab's crime?
A) He must pay the full blood money.
B) He must pay the lesser of the mukatab's value or the blood money.
C) He is not liable because the mukatab is free.
D) He must surrender the mukatab.

Key Takeaway
For a mukatab who commits a crime before judgment and then becomes unable, the master pays the lesser of value or arsh before 'ajz, and has the option of payment or surrender after 'ajz; multiple crimes before judgment only incur one value.

Judgment on Mukatab's Jinaya Then 'Ajz: Becomes Debt
Matn on the ruling when judgment is passed on a mukatab's crime before 'ajz, then it becomes a debt.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the effect of a judge's judgment on a mukatab's crime before 'ajz, and explain the qiyas that supports it.

Core Idea
A judge's judgment converts crime liability from the slave's person to a debt, enabling sale upon 'ajz.

This lesson examines a nuanced case involving a mukatab (slave under kitaba) who commits a crime and then becomes unable to pay. The central question is: once a judge has passed judgment on the liability, does that judgment crystallise the obligation into a debt collectible by selling the mukatab if he later becomes unable? The Hanafi school affirms this, based on a qiyas to a runaway usurped object and a refutation of opposing views.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the judge passing judgment on the liability of a mukatab's crime while he is still in kitaba. The ruling according to the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf later, Muhammad) is that it becomes a debt for which the mukatab is sold if he later becomes unable.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is qiyas jaliy (explicit analogy) to two cases: a runaway usurped object (maghsub abaq) and a sold runaway slave (mabi' abiq). In both, judgment transfers the right from the specific object to its value.
The text uses the phrase 'وهو نظير المغصوب إذا أبق'.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The effective cause (illa) is the uncertainty (taraddud) of the obstacle (kitaba). Unlike mudabbar/umm walad whose status is permanent, the kitaba can be dissolved by 'ajz, so the original obligation of surrender cannot be enforced directly; judgment is needed to crystallise the right into a value.
The text says 'المانع هنا متردد لاحتمال انفساخ الكتابة'.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Zufar and early Abu Yusuf held that the value is owed but the mukatab is not sold. Their reasoning: the kitaba was a valid obstacle at the time of the crime, so the situation is fixed like mudabbar or umm walad, where the master pays but the slave is not sold.
Abu Yusuf later retracted his initial view.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The three imams' view is the strong position (mufta bihi) because the kitaba is a revocable impediment, and judgment serves to convert the right from raqabah to value. The qiyas to runaway property is analogically sound and distinguishes the case from mudabbar.
The commentary says 'عند علمائنا الثلاثة'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (فإن قضى به عليه في كتابته فعجز فهو دين يباع فيه) يعني إذا قضى بموجب الجناية على المكاتب في حال كتابته وهو الأقل من قيمته ومن الأرش فهو دين عليه يباع فيه لأن الحق انتقل من الرقبة إلى القيمة بالقضاء، وهذا عند علمائنا الثلاثة. وقال زفر : تجب عليه قيمته ولا يباع وهو قول أبي يوسف أولاً لأن المانع من الدفع وقت الجناية موجود وهو الكتابة فلا تتغير كجناية المدبر وأم الولد. ولنا أن الأصل في جناية العبد الدفع وإنما يصار إلى القيمة عند تعذر الدفع والمانع هنا متردد لاحتمال انفساخ الكتابة فلا يثبت الانتقال عن الموجب الأصلي إلا بالقضاء والصلح عن الرضا وبالموت عن الوفاء، وهو نظير المغصوب إذا أبق لا يجب عليه القيمة إلا بالقضاء حتى لو رجع قبل القضاء يكون لمولاه، وإن رجع بعد القضاء يكون للغاصب، وكذا المبيع إذا أبق قبل القبض لا يبطل البيع إلا بالقضاء، وكذا إذا قتل لأن القيمة تقوم مقامه بخلاف المدبر وأم الولد لأنهما لا يقبلان الفسخ .
He (the author) said: (If judgment is passed against him during his kitaba, then he becomes unable, it is a debt for which he is sold.) Meaning: When the judge passes judgment for the liability of the crime against the mukatab while he is still in kitaba, which is the lesser of his value or the blood money, it becomes a debt on him for which he is sold, because the right transfers from the slave's person to the value by the judgment. This is according to our three imams. Zufar said: His value is owed and he is not sold; this is also Abu Yusuf's initial opinion, because the obstacle to surrender existed at the time of the crime, which is the kitaba, so it does not change, like the crime of a mudabbar or umm walad. Our proof: The original rule for a slave's crime is surrender; only when surrender is impossible do we resort to value. Here the obstacle (kitaba) is uncertain because it can be annulled (by 'ajz), so the transfer from the original obligation does not occur except by judgment, or by amicable settlement, or by death in satisfaction. This is analogous to a usurped object that runs away: value is not due except by judgment; if it returns before judgment, it goes to the owner; after judgment, to the usurper. Similarly, a sold runaway slave does not void the sale except by judgment. Thus, judgment crystallizes the transfer to value, unlike mudabbar and umm walad which are not subject to dissolution.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage addresses a case where a judge has already passed judgment on a mukatab's crime while he was still able to pay. The matn states that if the mukatab then becomes unable ('ajz), the liability becomes a debt (dayn) for which he is sold to satisfy. The commentary explains the reasoning: judgment transfers the right from the slave's person (raqabah) to a monetary value. This is the position of the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad). Zufar and Abu Yusuf's initial opinion held that the slave's value is owed but he is not sold, comparing to mudabbar and umm walad where the obligation is fixed on the master regardless of later events. The Hanafi response distinguishes: the kitaba can be broken by 'ajz, making the obstacle to surrender uncertain. Therefore, judgment is needed to convert the right to value, similar to a runaway usurped object or a sold runaway slave. In contrast, mudabbar and umm walad cannot be undone, so their case is different.

Key Terms
الرقبة (al-raqabah): The person of the slave, as opposed to his value. The right originally attaches to the slave's body.
القضاء (al-qaḍā'): The judge's judgment that crystallizes the liability into a monetary debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the effect of a judge's judgment on a mukatab's crime before 'ajz?
A) The liability transfers to the master permanently.
B) The liability remains attached to the slave's person and is not transferable.
C) The liability becomes a debt on the mukatab, and he is sold if he becomes unable.
D) The judgment is void because the mukatab is not fully liable.

Key Takeaway
A judge's judgment on a mukatab's crime converts the liability from the slave's person to a debt, enabling sale upon 'ajz, based on qiyas to runaway property.
