Kitaba Endures Beyond Master's Death
Matn with qiyas proof on the effect of master's death on kitaba.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the effect of the master's death on a kitaba contract and explain the qiyas proof using tadbir, umm walad, and debt.

Core Idea
The kitaba contract survives the master's death because it is the slave's right.

In this passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the author establishes a key principle: the death of the master does not annul the kitaba contract. This may seem counterintuitive because contracts are often personal to the parties. However, the Hanafi school treats the kitaba as a right belonging to the slave, not merely a bilateral contract that dissolves upon death. The proof uses clear qiyas to other well-established legal categories. Let's unpack this ruling and its reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The kitaba is not annulled when the master dies. It remains valid.
2
Understand the reasoning
Because it is the slave's right (haqq al-ʿabd) – it belongs to him, not to the master.
The right is established by the contract and continues.
3
Recognize the qiyas
Analogies drawn to tadbir (promise of freedom after death), umm walad (slave woman bearing master's child), and a debt owed to the deceased.
In each case, the right survives the death of the master/creditor.
4
Grasp the common element
The illa is that all are rights belonging to the slave or debtor that survive the master's death.
The kitaba installments are a right of the slave (debtor) and the term is his right, so it survives.
5
Note the cross-madhhab perspective
Some schools might consider kitaba as a contract that ends with either party's death, but Hanafi establishes the opposite.
This is an area of legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وإن مات السيد لم تنفسخ الكتابة لأنها حق العبد فلا تبطل بموت السيد كالتدبير وأم الولد والدين وكالأجل فيه إذا مات الطالب، ولأن الكتابة لا تقبل الانتقال إلى ملك الوارث فتبقى على حكم ملك المولى . قال رحمه الله : ويؤدي المال إلى الورثة على نجومه) لأن النجوم حقه وهو أجل لأنه حق المطلوب فلا يبطل بموت الطالب. هذا إذا كاتبه وهو صحيح، ولو كاتبه وهو مريض لا يصح تأجيله إلا من الثلث وقد ذكرناه والوارث ينوب مناب المورث ويقوم مقامه فيكون قبضه بمنزلة قبض المورث ويقع على ملكه ثم يصير الوارث قابضاً عن نفسه فيملكه بالإرث كما في الدين وفي المحيط : ولو أدى المكاتب بدل الكتابة إلى الورثة دون الوصي وعلى الميت دين يحيط به أو لا يحيط به لا يعتق لأن حق القبض للموصي للوارث لأن الوارث وإن ملك ما قبض إذا لم يكن الدين مستغرقاً وللوصي والغرماء أن يقبض ملكهم بقدر الدين فلم يدفع الحق له لمن له حق القبض فلا يبرأ عن بدل الكتابة كما لو دفع إلى أجنبي وإن أدى إلى الوصي عتق وإن لم يكن في التركة دين لأنه قائم مقام الميت، وإن لم يكن على الميت دين ودفع إلى الورثة وتقاسموا جاز لأن لهم حق القبض، وإن أدى إلى بعضهم لم يعتق ما لم يصل إلى الكل بخلاف الدفع إلى الوصي يوجب العتق وصل إلى الورثة حقهم أم لا، لأنه ثابت عن الميت بالتفويض، ولو أدى المكاتب إلى الغرماء وعليه دين محيط جاز وعتق لأنه دفع الحق إلى من له حق القبض، ولو أوصى المولى لإنسان بما على المكاتب فدفع المكاتب إليه يعتق لأنه دفع الحق إلى مستحقه.
He (the author) said: (If the master dies, the kitaba is not annulled because it is the right of the slave, so it is not invalidated by the master's death, like tadbir and umm walad and a debt, and like the term in it if the claimant dies. And because the kitaba cannot be transferred to the ownership of the heir, it remains under the rule of the master's ownership.) He said: (And he pays the money to the heirs according to its installments.), because the installments are his right, and it is a term that is the right of the debtor, so it is not invalidated by the death of the claimant.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage presents two matn statements: (1) The death of the master does not annul the kitaba contract. The reasoning is that the kitaba is a right belonging to the slave, similar to tadbir (promise of freedom after death) and umm walad, which survive the master. Analogously, a debt owed to the deceased remains due to the heirs, and the term (installments) is a right of the debtor (slave) that does not end when the creditor (master) dies. (2) The mukatab pays the kitaba money to the heirs according to the original installment schedule, because the installments are a right (of the slave) and an extension (ajal) that benefits the slave, so death of the master does not accelerate them. The commentary then discusses nuances: If the master was ill at the time of kitaba, the postponement (ajal) is only valid from one-third of the estate (as a bequest). It also details various scenarios of payment to heirs, executor, and creditors, explaining when the mukatab becomes free. Key point: payment must be made to the right party; otherwise, freedom is not achieved.

Key Terms
الكتابة (al-kitāba): A contract of manumission where the slave pays installments to the master and upon completion becomes free.
التدبير (al-tadbīr): A master's promise that a slave will be free upon the master's death.
أم الولد (umm al-walad): A female slave who bears a child to her master; she becomes free upon his death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary reason the kitaba contract is not annulled upon the master's death according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because the master's ownership continues after death.
B) Because it is a right of the slave that survives the master.
C) Because the contract is a form of will that takes effect after death.
D) Because the heirs are required to honor the contract.

Key Takeaway
The kitaba contract is not annulled by the master's death because it is a right of the slave, similar to other rights that survive death.

Payment of Kitaba Installments After Master's Death
Detailed scenarios on payment of kitaba installments after master's death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine the valid recipient of kitaba payments after the master's death and identify when the mukatab becomes free.

Core Idea
The mukatab must pay the installments to the rightful party; only the executor (wasi) or all heirs collectively can receive payment and effect freedom.

The second part of the passage addresses the practical issue of whom the mukatab pays after the master's death. The installments are still due according to the original schedule, but the recipient varies depending on the presence of an executor, debts, and whether all heirs consent. The commentary provides detailed scenarios to clarify when the payment results in freedom.

Guided Path
1
Default payment to heirs
The mukatab pays the heirs according to the original installment schedule.
The installments are a right of the slave (debtor) and do not accelerate upon death.
2
Role of the executor (wasi)
If there is an executor, payment to the executor effects freedom even if the heirs have not received their shares.
The executor stands in the place of the deceased (niyaba).
3
Impact of debts
If the master had debts, payment must be made to the executor or creditors; otherwise, the slave does not become free.
The right of the creditors takes precedence over the heirs.
4
Partial payment to individual heirs
If the mukatab pays only one heir without the others, he does not become free until the payment reaches all heirs collectively.
The right to collect is joint among heirs (in absence of executor).
5
Payment to a legatee
If the master bequeaths the kitaba debt to a specific person, payment to that person frees the mukatab.
The legatee becomes the rightful owner of the debt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وإن مات السيد لم تنفسخ الكتابة لأنها حق العبد فلا تبطل بموت السيد كالتدبير وأم الولد والدين وكالأجل فيه إذا مات الطالب، ولأن الكتابة لا تقبل الانتقال إلى ملك الوارث فتبقى على حكم ملك المولى . قال رحمه الله : ويؤدي المال إلى الورثة على نجومه) لأن النجوم حقه وهو أجل لأنه حق المطلوب فلا يبطل بموت الطالب. هذا إذا كاتبه وهو صحيح، ولو كاتبه وهو مريض لا يصح تأجيله إلا من الثلث وقد ذكرناه والوارث ينوب مناب المورث ويقوم مقامه فيكون قبضه بمنزلة قبض المورث ويقع على ملكه ثم يصير الوارث قابضاً عن نفسه فيملكه بالإرث كما في الدين وفي المحيط : ولو أدى المكاتب بدل الكتابة إلى الورثة دون الوصي وعلى الميت دين يحيط به أو لا يحيط به لا يعتق لأن حق القبض للموصي للوارث لأن الوارث وإن ملك ما قبض إذا لم يكن الدين مستغرقاً وللوصي والغرماء أن يقبض ملكهم بقدر الدين فلم يدفع الحق له لمن له حق القبض فلا يبرأ عن بدل الكتابة كما لو دفع إلى أجنبي وإن أدى إلى الوصي عتق وإن لم يكن في التركة دين لأنه قائم مقام الميت، وإن لم يكن على الميت دين ودفع إلى الورثة وتقاسموا جاز لأن لهم حق القبض، وإن أدى إلى بعضهم لم يعتق ما لم يصل إلى الكل بخلاف الدفع إلى الوصي يوجب العتق وصل إلى الورثة حقهم أم لا، لأنه ثابت عن الميت بالتفويض، ولو أدى المكاتب إلى الغرماء وعليه دين محيط جاز وعتق لأنه دفع الحق إلى من له حق القبض، ولو أوصى المولى لإنسان بما على المكاتب فدفع المكاتب إليه يعتق لأنه دفع الحق إلى مستحقه.
He (the author) said: (If the master dies, the kitaba is not annulled because it is the right of the slave, so it is not invalidated by the master's death, like tadbir and umm walad and a debt, and like the term in it if the claimant dies. And because the kitaba cannot be transferred to the ownership of the heir, it remains under the rule of the master's ownership.) He said: (And he pays the money to the heirs according to its installments.), because the installments are his right, and it is a term that is the right of the debtor, so it is not invalidated by the death of the claimant.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage presents two matn statements: (1) The death of the master does not annul the kitaba contract. The reasoning is that the kitaba is a right belonging to the slave, similar to tadbir (promise of freedom after death) and umm walad, which survive the master. Analogously, a debt owed to the deceased remains due to the heirs, and the term (installments) is a right of the debtor (slave) that does not end when the creditor (master) dies. (2) The mukatab pays the kitaba money to the heirs according to the original installment schedule, because the installments are a right (of the slave) and an extension (ajal) that benefits the slave, so death of the master does not accelerate them. Key Terms
الوصي (al-waṣiy): The executor appointed by the deceased to manage the estate.
الغرماء (al-ghuramā’): Creditors of the deceased who have a claim on the estate.
النجم (al-najm): The installment (time portion) of the kitaba payment.

Checkpoint
In the absence of an executor and debts, what is required for the mukatab to become free when paying the heirs?
A) Payment to any one heir.
B) Payment to all heirs collectively.
C) Payment to the eldest heir.
D) Payment to the executor appointed by the court.

Key Takeaway
The key to freedom after the master's death is paying the right person: the executor (if any), all heirs collectively, or the creditors if debts exist.

Manumission of Mukatab by All Heirs: Qiyas vs Istihsan
Matn and commentary on manumission by all heirs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on manumission of a mukatab by all heirs, explain the qiyas rationale, and identify istihsan as the basis for the operative ruling.

Core Idea
When all heirs free a mukatab, istihsan overrides qiyas and grants freedom without payment.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq presents a fascinating case where juristic preference (istihsan) overturns strict analogy (qiyas). The mukatab is a slave who has contracted to purchase his freedom in installments. If all heirs collectively manumit him, does he become free? The passage shows how Hanafi usul resolves this by preferring equity over rigid logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
The matn states: 'If they free him, he becomes free for nothing.' Identify the ruling: the mukatab is freed without payment (majjānan) when all heirs manumit him.
2
State the qiyas (analogy) ruling
The commentary notes: by qiyas, he would not become free. Understand why: the heirs do not own the mukatab; they only have a right to collect the kitaba payments. Manumission requires ownership, which they lack.
Qiyas is based on the principle that only the owner can free a slave.
3
Identify the basis of istihsan
The istihsan overrides qiyas. The reasoning (not fully quoted) likely considers that collective manumission fulfills the purpose of kitaba (freedom) and the heirs' consent effectively cancels the debt. This is an act of goodwill that the Law encourages.
Istihsan is a Hanafi source of law that prefers a more equitable outcome over strict analogy.
4
Understand the thamarah (practical result)
The practical consequence: the mukatab becomes free immediately, and the remaining kitaba debt is waived. This differs from if only one heir freed him (which would not be effective).
5
Relate to Hanafi usul
This case exemplifies the Hanafi principle that istihsan can be used when qiyas leads to hardship. It also shows that the combined action of all heirs is treated as equivalent to the owner's act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وإن حرروه عتق مجاناً) يعني لو أعتقه جميع الورثة عتق والقياس أن لا يعتق لأنهم لم يملكوه. وجه الاستحسان أن لا
He (the author) said: (And if they free him, he becomes free for nothing.) Meaning: If all the heirs free him, he becomes free. By qiyas, he would not become free because they did not own him. The reason for istihsan: because...
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This is a partial passage. The matn states that if all the heirs collectively manumit the mukatab, he becomes free without having to pay the kitaba (majjānan). The commentary begins by noting that by qiyas (analogy) he would not be free because the heirs do not own the mukatab (they only have the right to collect payments). However, by istihsan (juristic preference), he is freed. The reasoning would likely be that freeing the mukatab is an act of goodwill that fulfills the purpose of kitaba, and the heirs' consent effectively cancels the remaining debt. The passage is cut off but conveys the ruling.

Key Terms
الاستحسان (al-istiḥsān): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas to achieve equity.
المكاتب (al-mukātab): A slave who has made a contract (kitaba) with his master to purchase his freedom by paying installments.
الورثة (al-warathah): The heirs of the deceased master; they succeed to the right to collect the kitaba payments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, what happens if all the heirs of a deceased master jointly free the mukatab?
A) The mukatab remains enslaved and must continue paying the kitaba.
B) The mukatab becomes free but must pay the remaining kitaba to the heirs.
C) The mukatab becomes free without any payment.
D) The manumission is invalid because the heirs do not own the mukatab.

Key Takeaway
When all heirs collectively manumit a mukatab, istihsan overrides qiyas and he becomes free without paying the remaining kitaba.

Ruling on a Mukatab's Liability for a Crime During Kitabah
Ruling and dispute on the mukatab's liability for jinaayah: debt or sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a mukatab's liability for a crime during kitabah and explain the qiyas-based proof that distinguishes it from the case of a mudabbar and umm walad.

Core Idea
A mukatab's crime becomes a debt after judgment, allowing his sale due to the uncertain impediment of kitabah.

The Hanafi school addresses a nuanced scenario involving a mukatab (a slave under a contract of kitabah) who commits a crime. The key issue is whether the liability for the crime is automatically determined or requires a judicial judgment. This lesson unpacks the ruling of the three Hanafi imams, contrasts it with the view of Zufar and the earlier Abu Yusuf, and examines the qiyas reasoning that settles the dispute.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify the act (mukatab's crime) and the ruling: the liability becomes a debt (the lesser of his value or blood-money) and he can be sold to pay it.
The ruling applies only after a judgment is passed.
2
Identify the opposing view
Zufar and the earlier Abu Yusuf hold that the full value is due immediately and the mukatab cannot be sold.
They analogize with mudabbar and umm walad.
3
Follow the Hanafi proof
The original rule for a slave's crime is handing over the slave; value is only recourse when handing over is impossible. The impediment (kitabah) is uncertain because it can be annulled.
Thus, transition to value only occurs by judgment or mutual consent.
4
Examine the qiyas analogies
The Hanafi argument compares the case to a usurped slave who runs away and a sold slave who runs away before delivery: value is not due until a judgment.
These analogies show the importance of a judicial decision.
5
Determine the practical consequence
Under the Hanafi view, the debt can be collected by selling the mukatab; under the opposing view, the full value must be paid and sale is impossible.
The mufta bihi is the Hanafi position for practical viability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (فإن قضى به عليه في كتابته فعجز فهو دين يباع فيه) يعني إذا قضى بموجب الجناية على المكاتب في حال كتابته وهو الأقل من قيمته ومن الأرش فهو دين عليه يباع فيه لأن الحق انتقل من الرقبة إلى القيمة بالقضاء، وهذا عند علمائنا الثلاثة. وقال زفر : تجب عليه قيمته ولا يباع وهو قول أبي يوسف أولاً لأن المانع من الدفع وقت الجناية موجود وهو الكتابة فلا تتغير كجناية المدبر وأم الولد. ولنا أن الأصل في جناية العبد الدفع وإنما يصار إلى القيمة عند تعذر الدفع والمانع هنا متردد لاحتمال انفساخ الكتابة فلا يثبت الانتقال عن الموجب الأصلي إلا بالقضاء والصلح عن الرضا وبالموت عن الوفاء، وهو نظير المغصوب إذا أبق لا يجب عليه القيمة إلا بالقضاء حتى لو رجع قبل القضاء يكون لمولاه، وإن رجع بعد القضاء يكون للغاصب، وكذا المبيع إذا أبق قبل القبض لا يبطل البيع إلا بالقضاء، وكذا إذا قتل لأن القيمة تقوم مقامه بخلاف المدبر وأم الولد لأنهما لا يقبلان الفسخ .
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (If a judgment is passed against him while he is a mukatab, and he becomes unable to pay, then it is a debt for which he can be sold). Meaning: when a judgment is passed for the consequence of the crime (jinaayah) against the mukatab while he is in the state of kitabah, and it is the lesser of his value and the blood-money, then it is a debt upon him for which he can be sold, because the right has transferred from the slave's person (raqabah) to the value (qimah) by the judgment. This is according to our three scholars. Zufar said: His value is due and he cannot be sold, and this was the earlier opinion of Abu Yusuf, because the impediment to handing over (the slave) at the time of the crime exists, which is the kitabah, so it does not change, like the case of a mudabbar and umm walad. Our argument: The original principle in the crime of a slave is the handing over (of the slave himself), and recourse is made to the value only when handing over is impossible. The impediment here is uncertain due to the possibility of the annulment of the kitabah, so the transition from the original obligation is not established except by a judicial decision, or by a mutual settlement with consent, or by death as fulfillment. This is analogous to the case of a usurped (maghsoub) slave who runs away: the value is not obligatory except by a judicial decision; if he returns before the judgment, he is for his master; if he returns after the judgment, he is for the usurper. Similarly, if a sold slave runs away before delivery, the sale is not void except by a judicial decision. Likewise, if it is killed, because the value stands in its place. This is unlike the mudabbar and umm walad, because they cannot be annulled.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling of the Hanafi school regarding a mukatab who commits a crime during the period of kitabah. The author first states the matn: if a judgment is passed against the mukatab for the crime and then he becomes unable to pay (i.e., he cannot pay the kitabah), the amount becomes a debt for which he can be sold to pay it. The commentary explains that the judgment refers to the liability for the crime, where the liability is the lesser of the slave's value and the blood-money (arsh). This is the position of the three scholars (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad). Zufar and the earlier opinion of Abu Yusuf hold that the full value is due and the mukatab cannot be sold, drawing an analogy with a mudabbar (a slave promised freedom upon the master's death) or an umm walad (a slave mother of the master's child), where the kitabah (or similar status) prevents the transfer of the slave. The Hanafi response argues that the original rule for a slave's crime is handing over the slave himself; recourse to value is only when handing over is impossible. Here, the impediment (kitabah) is uncertain because the kitabah could be annulled (if the mukatab becomes unable to pay), so the transition to the value does not occur except by a judicial decision. They support this with analogies from other areas of fiqh: a usurped slave who runs away is only liable for the value after a judgment; a sold slave who runs away before delivery does not void the sale except by judgment. Thus, the mukatab's liability is established only by judgment, making it a debt, and he can be sold to satisfy it.

Key Terms
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a kitabah contract with his master to earn and pay a fixed sum for his freedom.
جناية (jinaayah): A crime or injury caused by the mukatab that incurs a financial liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the liability of a mukatab who commits a crime during kitabah?
A) The full value of the mukatab is due immediately.
B) The lesser of his value or the blood-money is due as a debt, and he can be sold to pay it.
C) The master must pay the blood-money.
D) The mukatab is exempt from liability because of the kitabah.

Key Takeaway
The mukatab's crime becomes a debt after judgment, allowing his sale, because the kitabah is an uncertain impediment unlike mudabbar and umm walad.

Effect of Master's Death on Kitabah and Payment to Heirs
Ruling with proof on kitabah post-master death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the kitabah contract continues after the master's death and apply the rules for who should receive the kitabah payments in various scenarios.

Core Idea
Kitabah survives the master's death; the slave pays heirs on installments, but proper recipient depends on debts, executor, or bequest.

When a master who contracted kitabah with a slave dies, one might assume the contract ends. However, Hanafi fiqh holds that the kitabah continues because it is a right of the slave, analogous to tadbir, umm walad, and debts. This lesson explores the proof for this ruling and the detailed fiqh of who receives the payments—heirs, executor, or creditors—and the consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Main Ruling
The matn states: 'If the master dies, the kitabah is not dissolved.' This is the central ruling. Understand that the contract remains valid and the slave continues to pay.
2
Understand the Proof (Qiyas)
The commentary gives analogies: tadbir, umm walad, and debts are not extinguished by death. Also, the term (installments) is a right of the obligated party (slave), so it survives the creditor (master). Recognize that this is a qiyas (analogical reasoning) based on these established cases.
The kitabah cannot transfer to the heir's ownership, so it remains under the master's ownership, with the heir standing in the master's place.
3
Note the Condition of Master's Health
If the master was healthy when making the kitabah, it continues as normal. If he was sick, the deferment is only valid from one-third of the estate—a protective measure for other heirs' shares.
This sub-rule prevents the sick master from burdening the estate beyond one-third.
4
Determine Who Has the Right to Receive Payment
The heir stands in the master's place, so they are the default recipients. However, if there is an executor (wasi), the executor is the proper recipient because they represent the deceased. Creditors also have rights if the estate has debts.
The passage details several scenarios to clarify who must be paid for the mukatab to be freed.
5
Apply the Scenario-Based Rulings
Work through each situation: (a) Payment to heirs without executor and no debt → valid only if heirs divide among themselves. (b) Payment to executor → frees the mukatab regardless. (c) Payment to some heirs only → not freed until all receive. (d) Payment to creditors when debt is encompassing → valid. (e) Bequest of the kitabah to a third party → payment to that party frees the slave.
The key principle: payment must reach the one with the right to receive (mustahiqq).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وإن مات السيد لم تنفسخ الكتابة لأنها حق العبد فلا تبطل بموت السيد كالتدبير وأم الولد والدين وكالأجل فيه إذا مات الطالب، ولأن الكتابة لا تقبل الانتقال إلى ملك الوارث فتبقى على حكم ملك المولى . قال رحمه الله : ويؤدي المال إلى الورثة على نجومه) لأن النجوم حقه لأنه أجل وهو حق المطلوب فلا يبطل بموت الطالب. هذا إذا كاتبه وهو صحيح، ولو كاتبه وهو مريض لا يصح تأجيله إلا من الثلث وقد ذكرناه والوارث ينوب مناب المورث ويقوم مقامه فيكون قبضه بمنزلة قبض المورث ويقع على ملكه ثم يصير الوارث قابضاً عن نفسه فيملكه بالإرث كما في الدين وفي المحيط : ولو أدى المكاتب بدل الكتابة إلى الورثة دون الوصي وعلى الميت دين يحيط به أو لا يحيط به لا يعتق لأن حق القبض للموصي للوارث لأن الوارث وإن ملك ما قبض إذا لم يكن الدين مستغرقاً وللوصي والغرماء أن يقبض ملكهم بقدر الدين فلم يدفع الحق له لمن له حق القبض فلا يبرأ عن بدل الكتابة كما لو دفع إلى أجنبي وإن أدى إلى الوصي عتق وإن لم يكن في التركة دين لأنه قائم مقام الميت، وإن لم يكن على الميت دين ودفع إلى الورثة وتقاسموا جاز لأن لهم حق القبض، وإن أدى إلى بعضهم لم يعتق ما لم يصل إلى الكل بخلاف الدفع إلى الوصي يوجب العتق وصل إلى الورثة حقهم أم لا، لأنه ثابت عن الميت بالتفويض، ولو أدى المكاتب إلى الغرماء وعليه دين محيط جاز وعتق لأنه دفع الحق إلى من له حق القبض، ولو أوصى المولى لإنسان بما على المكاتب فدفع المكاتب إليه يعتق لأنه دفع الحق إلى مستحقه.
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (If the master dies, the kitabah is not dissolved) because it is the right of the slave, so it is not invalidated by the death of the master, like the tadbir and umm walad and a debt, and like the term when the creditor dies. And because the kitabah cannot be transferred to the ownership of the heir, so it remains under the ownership of the master. He said: And he pays the money to the heirs according to its installments) because the installments are his right, because it is a term, and the term is the right of the obligated party, so it is not invalidated by the death of the creditor. This applies if the master made the kitabah while he was healthy. If he made it while he was sick, the deferment is not valid except from one-third, as we have mentioned. The heir stands in the place of the testator and takes his position, so his receipt is like the receipt of the testator, and it falls on his ownership, then the heir becomes a receiver on his own behalf and owns it by inheritance, like in a debt. In al-Muhit: If the mukatab pays the kitabah price to the heirs without the executor and the deceased has a debt all-encompassing or not, he is not freed, because the right to receive is for the executor for the heir, because the heir, even though he owns what he received if the debt is not all-encompassing, yet the executor and the creditors may receive their ownership to the extent of the debt. So he did not pay the right to the one who has the right to receive, so he is not absolved from the kitabah price, just as if he paid to a stranger. If he pays to the executor, he becomes free even if there is no debt in the estate, because he stands in place of the deceased. If there is no debt on the deceased and he pays to the heirs and they divide it, it is permissible because they have the right to receive. If he pays to some of them, he is not freed until it reaches all of them, unlike payment to the executor which necessitates freedom regardless of whether it reaches the heirs' right or not, because it is established from the deceased by delegation. If the mukatab pays to the creditors while there is an encompassing debt, it is permissible and he becomes free, because he paid the right to the one who has the right to receive. If the master bequeaths to someone what the mukatab owes, and the mukatab pays it to him, he becomes free, because he paid the right to its due recipient.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage deals with the situation after the master's death. The matn states that the kitabah does not dissolve upon the master's death. The commentary gives reasons: it is the slave's right, similar to tadbir, umm walad, and debts, which are not extinguished by the death of the party. Also, the kitabah cannot transfer to the heir's ownership, so it remains under the master's ownership, and the heir takes the master's position. The payment is made to the heirs according to the installments. The commentary then discusses various scenarios: if the master was sick when he made the kitabah, the deferment is only valid from one-third of his estate. It then details who has the right to receive payment: if there is an executor, he should receive; if the mukatab pays directly to the heirs without the executor, he is not freed unless the deceased had no debts or the heirs divide it. Payment to the executor frees the mukatab regardless. Payment to creditors is valid if there is an encompassing debt. Bequest of the kitabah debt to someone also requires payment to that person.

Key Terms
تدبير (tadbir): A master's declaration that a slave is free upon the master's death.
نجوم (nujoom): The installments of the kitabah payment.
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave under a kitabah contract.
وصي (wasi): Executor of a will; one appointed to manage the deceased's affairs.
غرماء (ghurama): Creditors of the deceased.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens when a mukatab pays the full kitabah amount to the master's executor?
A) The slave is freed regardless of whether the executor distributes to the heirs.
B) The slave is not freed until the executor pays the heirs.
C) The slave is freed only if there are no debts.
D) The slave remains a slave because payment should go to the heirs directly.

Key Takeaway
The kitabah contract survives the master's death, and the slave's freedom depends on paying the proper recipient: heirs (if no debt/executor), executor (always valid), creditors (when debts encompass), or legatee (if bequeathed).

Freeing the Mukatab by the Heirs: Condition of Collective Action and Istihsan Proof
Ruling with proof: istihsan over qiyas for freeing mukatab by heirs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on freeing a mukatab by the heirs and explain why istihsan overrides qiyas in making it valid.

Core Idea
Freeing a mukatab by the heirs is valid by istihsan as a release of the kitabah debt, but only if all heirs act together in one sitting.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains when the manumission of a mukatab by his heirs is effective. While qiyas would deny validity because the heirs do not own the slave, the Hanafi school adopts istihsan, treating the act as a release of the kitabah debt. The ruling also imposes a strict condition that the freeing must be done collectively and in a single sitting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the freeing of a mukatab by the heirs. The ruling: if all heirs free him together, he becomes free without paying any remaining kitabah.
This is the matn's claim.
2
Understand the qiyas objection
By qiyas, the heirs do not own the mukatab (they only inheriting the right to the kitabah payments), so their manumission should be invalid.
This is the apparent analogy.
3
Apply istihsan as the Hanafi dalil
Istihsan reinterprets the act as a release (ibra') of the kitabah debt, which the heirs do own. Since the debt is considered satisfied, the mukatab's liability ends and he becomes free.
This is the Hanafi preferred method.
4
Note the condition for validity
The freeing must be done by all heirs in one sitting (majlis). If only some free him, it does not take effect.
There is a narration from Hisham allowing later freeing if the first does not retract, but the relied-upon position requires immediate collective action.
5
Apply the ruling to further cases
If one heir accepts the entire payment without permission, the mukatab is not freed unless the others authorize. If an heir gives his share in the mukatab's person as a gift, it does not free him, but if the mukatab later becomes unable to pay, the heir's share returns as part of his value.
These are extensions of the same principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وإن حرروه عتق مجاناً) يعني لو أعتقه. جميع الورثة عتق والقياس أن لا يعتق لأنهم لم يملكوه. وجه الاستحسان أن لا يجعل إبراء عن بدل الكتابة لأنه حقهم وقد جرى فيه الإرث فيكون الإعتاق منهم إبراء وإقراراً بالاستيفاء فلم يبق عليه دين فيعتق لبراءة ذمته كما إذا أبرأه المولى عن بدل الكتابة، ويشترط أن يعتقوه في مجلس واحد حتى إذا أعتقه بعضهم في مجلس لم يعتق، وقيل يعتق إذا أعتقه الباقون ما لم يرجع الأول وهو رواية هشام عن محمد قال رحمه الله : (وإن حرره بعض لم ينفذ عتقه) يعني لو أعتقه بعض الورثة لا يعتق منه شيء لأنه لم يملكه ولا عتق فيما لم يملك ولا يملك أن يجعل إبراء واستيفاء لأن إبراء البعض واستيفاءه لا عتقه لتعذر يوجب ثبوت العتق من جهته ولا يبرأ من الدين أيضاً لأن البراءة لم تثبت الاقتضاء، فإذا بطل المقتضي بطل المقتضي، ولو قبض واحد نصيب الكل بغير أمرهم لا يعتق إلا إذا أجازوا قبضه أو قبض ما أمرهم وفي المحيط : لو وهب أحدهم للمكاتب نصيبه في رقبته جاز ولا يعتق لأنه لو أدى نصيبه لا يعتق فكذا إذا أبرأه عنه بالهبة فإن عجز رد رقيقاً فنصيب الواهب في رقبته ثابت لأنه عاد قناً فانفساخ الكتابة فصار كله راثاً لهم من المولى ألا ترى [ميرا؟] أنه إذا وهبه المولى بعض الكتابة ثم عجز صار كله رقيقا للمولى فكذا هنا والله تعالى أعلم بالصواب وإليه المرجع والمآب.
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (If they free him, he becomes free without paying). Meaning: if all the heirs free him, he becomes free. The analogy (qiyas) would be that he should not become free because they do not own him. The istihsan (preference) is that it is considered an iqta' (release) of the kitabah price, because it is their right and it has been subject to inheritance. Thus their freeing is a release (ibra') and an acknowledgment of receipt, so no debt remains upon him, so he becomes free due to the clearing of his liability, just as if the master had released him from the kitabah price. It is required that they free him in one sitting; if some free him in a sitting, he does not become free. It is said that he becomes free if the remaining ones free him as long as the first does not retract, and this is a narration of Hisham from Muhammad. He said: (If one of them frees him, his freeing does not take effect). Meaning: if some of the heirs free him, none of him is freed, because he did not own him, and there is no freeing in what is not owned. And he cannot make it a release and receipt because the release of a part and its receipt is not enough to establish the freeing from his side, nor is he released from the debt either, because the release is not established by the requirement. So when the requirement is invalidated, the required is invalidated. If one of them receives the entire share without their permission, he does not become free unless they authorize his receipt, or he receives what they command. In al-Muhit: If one of them gives the mukatab his share in his slavery (i.e., in his person), it is valid, but he does not become free, because if he paid his share, he would not become free, so likewise if he releases him from it through a gift. Then if he becomes unable (to pay), he returns as a slave, so the share of the giver is still in his slavery, because he returned as a slave due to the annulment of the kitabah, so he becomes all of them inheriting from the master? Do you not see that if the master gave him a part of the kitabah and then he became unable, he becomes wholly a slave for the master? So here too. And Allah knows best what is correct, and to Him is the return and refuge.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage addresses what happens when the heirs free the mukatab. The matn says: if they free him, he becomes free without paying. The commentary explains that this is based on istihsan, because by analogy (qiyas) the heirs did not own the slave (since the kitabah was a right against the slave, not ownership of his person), so their manumission should not be valid. However, istihsan considers it as an iqta' (release) of the kitabah debt, because the right to the kitabah payment has been inherited by them. So their act is interpreted as a release (ibra') and an acknowledgment that the debt has been satisfied, so the mukatab's liability is cleared and he becomes free. A condition is that they must free him in one sitting; otherwise it is not effective. There is a narration from Hisham from Muhammad that if some free him and then the rest free him later, he becomes free as long as the first does not retract. The matn also states that if only some of the heirs free him, it does not take effect, because they do not own the slave, and a partial release cannot free him. The commentary further discusses the case where one heir accepts the full payment without permission, and the case where an heir gives the mukatab his share in the slave's person as a gift; this does not free the mukatab, but if he later becomes unable to pay, the heir's share returns to being part of the slave.

Key Terms
إبراء (ibra'): Release from a debt; here the freeing of the mukatab by the heirs is considered a release of the kitabah debt.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference used to override qiyas; here, the freeing of the mukatab by heirs is upheld despite the qiyas that they don't own him.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a necessary condition for the freeing of a mukatab by his heirs to be valid according to the relied-upon Hanafi position?
A) Any one heir can free him.
B) All heirs must free him together in a single sitting.
C) He must pay the remaining kitabah first.
D) The heirs must first obtain the mukatab's consent.

Key Takeaway
The manumission of a mukatab by his heirs is valid through istihsan as a release of the debt, but only if all heirs act collectively in one sitting.

8 min
Ruling on Manumission of Mukatab by Heirs
Explaining the ruling when heirs manumit the mukatab after master's death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid manumission of a mukātab by heirs and explain the ruling on partial manumission.

Core Idea
Partial manumission of a mukātab by one heir is ineffective; full freedom requires all heirs acting in one session.

When a master dies leaving a mukātab slave, the right of kitābah passes to the heirs. If they collectively manumit him, he becomes free. However, the law is strict: partial manumission by some heirs is not only incomplete—it is entirely void. This lesson unpacks the condition of unanimity and the single session requirement, and addresses a minority view within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? The manumission of a mukātab by the heirs after the master's death. The primary ruling: if all heirs manumit, the mukātab becomes free; if only some, the manumission is ineffective.
2
Locate the dalīl
The commentary treats the heirs' manumission as a discharge (ibrā') from the kitābah debt, analogous to the master's own discharge. This is based on the principle that the heirs inherit the right of kitābah.
The proof is a qiyās jaliyy: as the master's discharge frees the mukātab, so does the heirs' collective discharge.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalālah
The heirs' manumission is considered an acknowledgment that the kitābah debt is satisfied. Consequently, no debt remains, and the mukātab's liability is cleared, leading to freedom.
4
Note the condition of a single session
All heirs must manumit in one gathering (majlis). If some manumit in one session and others later, the manumission is not valid. This condition is explicit in the text.
5
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilāf
There is a narration from Hishām from Muhammad that if the first manumitter does not revoke and the remaining heirs later manumit, the mukātab becomes free. However, the relied-upon (muftā bihī) position is that partial manumission is entirely ineffective.
The standard position is that manumission must be complete in one session.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب المكاتب / باب موت المكاتب وعجزه وموت المولى على نجومه وإن حرروه عتق مجاناً وإن حرره بعض لم ينفذ عتقه . يجعل إبراء عن بدل الكتابة لأنه حقهم وقد جرى فيه الإرث فيكون الإعتاق منهم إبراء وإقراراً بالاستيفاء فلم يبق عليه دين فيعتق لبراءة ذمته كما إذا أبرأه المولى عن بدل الكتابة، ويشترط أن يعتقوه في مجلس واحد حتى إذا أعتقه بعضهم في مجلس لم يعتق، وقيل يعتق إذا أعتقه الباقون ما لم يرجع الأول وهو رواية هشام عن محمد قال رحمه الله : (وإن حرره بعض لم ينفذ عتقه) يعني لو أعتقه بعض الورثة لا يعتق منه شيء لأنه لم يملكه ولا عتق فيما لم يملك ولا يملك أن يجعل إبراء واستيفاء لأن إبراء البعض واستيفاءه لا عتقه لتعذر يوجب ثبوت العتق من جهته ولا يبرأ من الدين أيضاً لأن البراءة لم تثبت الاقتضاء، فإذا بطل المقتضي بظل المقتضي، ولو قبض واحد نصيب الكل بغير أمرهم لا يعتق إلا إذا أجازوا قبضه أو قبض ما أمرهم وفي المحيط : لو وهب أحدهم للمكاتب نصيبه في رقبته جاز ولا يعتق لأنه لو أدى نصيبه لا يعتق فكذا إذا أبرأه عنه بالهبة فإن عجز رد رقيقاً فنصيب الواهب في رقبته ثابت لأنه عاد قناً فانفساخ الكتابة فصار كله راثاً لهم من المولى ألا ترى میرا أنه إذا وهبه المولى بعض الكتابة ثم عجز صار كله رقيقا للمولى فكذا هنا والله تعالى أعلم بالصواب وإليه المرجع والمآب.
Book of Mukatab / Section on Death of Mukatab and His Inability and Death of the Master. Upon his installments, if they manumit him, he is free gratis. If some of them manumit him, his manumission is not effective. It is made a discharge from the payment of kitabah because it is their right and inheritance has occurred in it, so the manumission from them is a discharge and an acknowledgment of receipt, so no debt remains on him, so he becomes free due to the innocence of his liability, just as if the master had discharged him from the kitabah payment. And it is a condition that they manumit him in one gathering, such that if some of them manumit him in a gathering, he is not free. And it is said he becomes free if the rest manumit him as long as the first does not revoke, and that is the narration of Hisham from Muhammad. He (the author) said: 'And if some manumit him, his manumission is not effective.' Meaning if some of the heirs manumit him, nothing of him becomes free because he did not own him, and there is no manumission in what he does not own, and he cannot make it a discharge and receipt because the discharge and receipt of some without manumission does not necessitate the establishment of manumission from his side, and he is also not discharged from the debt because the discharge was not proven to necessitate. So when the necessitator is invalidated, the necessitated remains. And if one person collects the share of all without their permission, he does not become free unless they authorize his collection or he collects what they ordered. In al-Muhit: If one of them gives his share in his servitude as a gift to the mukatab, it is valid and he does not become free because if he paid his share, he would not become free, so likewise if he discharges him from it by gift. Then if he becomes unable, he returns as a slave, so the share of the donor in his servitude is established because he returned to being a slave due to annulment of the kitabah, so he becomes entirely inherited by them from the master. Do you not see that if the master gives some of the kitabah to him then he becomes unable, he becomes entirely a slave to the master, so likewise here. And Allah knows best the truth, and to Him is the return and the refuge.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a ruling from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding the manumission of a mukatab by the heirs of the deceased master. The author explains the ruling and conditions. The matn states: 'Upon his installments, if they manumit him, he is free gratis. If some of them manumit him, his manumission is not effective.' The commentary elaborates that when all heirs collectively manumit the mukatab, they are considered to have discharged him from the kitabah debt, because the right of kitabah belongs to them and is inherited. Their manumission is treated as a discharge and an acknowledgment that the debt has been satisfied, so the mukatab's liability is cleared, and he becomes free. However, a key condition is that all heirs must manumit him in one sitting (majlis). If some manumit in one sitting but not others, the manumission is incomplete. There is a narration from Hisham ibn Amr al-Darir from Muhammad al-Shaybani that if the first manumitter does not revoke, and the rest later manumit, the mukatab becomes free. But the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that partial manumission by some heirs is ineffective entirely, as the author states: 'If some manumit him, his manumission is not effective.' The commentary explains that the partial manumitter does not own the mukatab fully (since ownership is shared), and one cannot free what one does not own. Also, the partial manumitter cannot turn his act into a discharge or receipt because that would require the full right. The passage also discusses a scenario where one heir collects all the kitabah installments without authorization: the mukatab does not become free unless other heirs ratify. Another scenario from al-Muhit: if one heir gives his share in the servitude as a gift (hiba) to the mukatab, it is valid, but the mukatab does not become free because even if he paid that share, he would not be free (since other shares remain). If he later becomes unable to pay, he returns to servitude, and the share of the donor returns to being part of the servitude because the kitabah is annulled. The commentary uses an analogy: if the master himself gives a portion of the kitabah to the mukatab and he later fails, he becomes entirely a slave again. The ruling is based on the Hanafi principle that the mukatab's freedom is contingent on full payment or discharge by all owners in one session.

Key Terms
مكاتب (mukātab): A slave who has entered a contract (kitābah) to earn freedom by paying installments.
إبراء (ibrāʾ): A legal discharge or release from a debt, here from the kitābah payment.
عتق (ʿitq): Manumission; the act of freeing a slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What condition must be met for the manumission of a mukātab by the heirs of the deceased master to be valid?
A) They must manumit him individually.
B) They must manumit him in one sitting.
C) The mukātab must agree.
D) They must manumit him before his death.

Key Takeaway
Manumission of a mukātab by heirs is valid only when all heirs act together in a single session; any partial manumission is legally void.

The Hanafi Definition of Wala' (Clientage)
Defining the concept of wala' and outlining topics covered in the book

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of wala' in Hanafi fiqh, identify its cause and proof, and distinguish between walāʾ al-ʿitq and muwālāh.

Core Idea
Wala' is a legal bond of mutual help and inheritance, caused by manumission from one's own ownership, proven by the Prophet’s hadith.

The concept of wala' (clientage) is a unique feature of Islamic inheritance law that arises from manumission. Understanding its definition, cause, and proof is essential for correctly applying the rules of inheritance. This lesson unpacks the introductory passage of the Book of Wala' from a Hanafi commentary, revealing the legal structure behind this bond.

Guided Path
1
Enumerate the Eight Aspects
The commentator lists eight aspects: etymology, proof, cause, linguistic meaning, juristic meaning, pillar, condition, and ruling. Recognize that wala' is treated systematically as a legal institution.
These aspects form the framework for the entire book.
2
Analyze the Derivation and Proof
Wala' derives from closeness or assistance. Its primary proof is the hadith 'al-wala' li-man a'taq' (wala' is for the one who frees). This hadith establishes the principle.
The hadith is a sound (sahih) tradition and is the core textual evidence.
3
Identify the Cause according to the Hanafi School
The cause (sabab) is manumission from one's own ownership. The commentator specifies 'al-asahh' (the most correct) view, emphasizing that the manumittor must have owned the slave at the time of freeing.
This is a nuanced point: the cause is not just any manumission, but manumission by the owner.
4
Distinguish Linguistic and Juristic Meanings
Linguistically, wala' means mutual help or closeness. Juristically, it means mutual help established either by manumission (ʿitq) or by contract (muwālāh). This dual avenue is a Hanafi feature.
The contract of muwalah is a secondary cause for those who cannot be freed directly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الولاء أورد كتاب الولاء عقب المكاتب لأن الولاء من آثار المكاتب لزوال ملك الرقبة عند أداء بدل الكتابة وهو وإن كان من آثار العتق إلا أن موجبات ترتيب الكتب السابقة ساقت المكاتب إلى هذا الموضع فوجب تأخير كتاب الولاء عن كتاب المكاتب لئلا يتقدم الأثر على المؤثر. والكلام فيه من وجوه الأول في اشتقاقه والثاني في بيان دليله، والثالث في سببه، والرابع في معناه لغة والخامس في معناه عند الفقهاء والسادس في ركنه، والسابع في شرطه، والثامن في حكمه. أما الأول فهو مشتق من الولاء وهو القرب وهو حصول الثاني عقيب الأول من غير فصل، أو من الموالاة يقال ولي الشيء إذا حصل بعده من غير فصل، من الولاية بالفتح وهو النصرة والمحبة ودليله قوله «الولاء لمن أعتق»(1) وقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام الولاء لحمة كلحمة النسب (2). وسببه الإعتاق لأن المولى أنعم على عبده بالإعتاق قال الشارح والأصح أن سببه العتق على ملكه لأنه يضاف إليه والإضافة دليل الاختصاص، ولأن من ورث قريبه عتق عليه وولاؤه له ولا إعتاق من جهته. وأما معناه لغة وهو عبارة عن المعاونة والنصرة أو عبارة عن المواصلة والمصادقة الولي وسمي ولياً لتناصره وتعاونه لحبيبه وصديقه. وعند الفقهاء عبارة عن التناصر سواء كان بالإعتاق أو بعقد الموالاة ولهذا قال في المبسوط والمطلوب بكل منهما التناصر ؛ كذا في النهاية. وأورد عليه بأن المذكور في المبسوط يدل على كون التناصر غيرهما إلا أنفسهما إذ لا يخفى على الفطن . وهو مفاعلة
Book of Wala'. He placed the Book of Wala' after the Book of Mukatab because wala' is among the effects of the mukatab due to the removal of ownership of the slave's person upon payment of the kitabah. And although it is among the effects of manumission, the reasons for ordering the previous books led the mukatab to this place, so it became necessary to delay the Book of Wala' after the Book of Mukatab so that the effect does not precede the cause. The discussion on it is from eight aspects: first: its etymology; second: exposition of its proof; third: its cause; fourth: its linguistic meaning; fifth: its meaning according to jurists; sixth: its pillar; seventh: its condition; eighth: its ruling. As for the first, it is derived from 'wala' meaning closeness, which is the occurrence of the second immediately after the first without interval, or from 'muwalah', it is said 'waliya' something if it occurs after it without interval, from 'wilayah' (with fatha) meaning help and love. And its proof is his saying: 'Wala' belongs to the one who frees' and his saying peace be upon him: 'Wala' is like flesh to flesh of lineage.' Its cause is manumission because the master bestowed upon his slave by manumission. The commentator said: the most correct is that its cause is manumission from one's own ownership because it is attributed to him and attribution indicates specificity, and because one who inherited his relative and then had to free him, his wala' belongs to him even though there is no manumission from his side. As for its linguistic meaning, it means assistance and help, or continuous connection and friendship. A friend (wali) is called wali because of mutual help and assistance for his beloved and friend. According to jurists, it means mutual help, whether by manumission or by contract of muwalah. For this reason it is said in al-Mabsut: 'The objective in both is mutual help.' Similarly in al-Nihayah. It was objected that what is mentioned in al-Mabsut indicates that mutual help is something other than them except themselves, as is not hidden from the intelligent. And it is a verbal noun of the form mufa'alah.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage introduces the Book of Wala' (Clientage) in the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The commentator first explains why this book comes after the Book of Mukatab: because wala' is a consequence of freedom attained through kitabah (contract of manumission). Although wala' is also a consequence of ordinary manumission, the flow of topics places it here to avoid the effect preceding the cause. Then, he outlines eight aspects of the discussion: etymology, proof, cause, linguistic meaning, juristic meaning, pillar, condition, and ruling. He explains that 'wala' linguistically derives from closeness or assistance. The proof is the well-known hadith 'Wala' is for the one who frees' and another hadith comparing it to flesh of lineage. The cause of wala' is manumission from one's own ownership, meaning that the freeing person must have owned the slave at the time of manumission. This is the preferred view (al-asahh) according to the commentator. The linguistic meaning includes assistance and friendship. In juristic terminology, wala' is mutual help that arises from either manumission or a specific contract (muwalah). The commentator cites al-Mabsut and al-Nihayah to support this. The passage ends with a brief objection about the precise definition, but it is not elaborated.

Key Terms
ولاء (walāʾ): A legal relationship of mutual help and inheritance arising from manumission or contract, giving the manumittor a right of inheritance from the freed slave.
موالاة (muwālāh): A contract of clientage between a free person and another, creating a mutual right of inheritance, distinct from walāʾ al-ʿitq (clientage by manumission).
عتق (ʿitq): Manumission; the act of freeing a slave, which is the primary cause of walāʾ.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, from which two sources does wala' derive its meaning of mutual help?
A) Linguistic derivation and the hadith.
B) The linguists and the jurists.
C) Manumission and contract.
D) The Quran and the Sunnah.

Key Takeaway
Wala' is a relationship of mutual help and inheritance, established by manumission from one's own ownership, and proven by the hadith 'al-wala' li-man a'taq'.

Definition and Proof of Wala' (Patronage)
Introduces wala' with its derivation, proof, and cause.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of wala' in Hanafi fiqh, cite its primary textual proof (the hadith 'al-wala' liman a'taq'), and explain its cause (emancipation of one's own slave).

Core Idea
Wala' is a legal bond of mutual support, proven by the hadith 'al-wala' liman a'taq', caused by freeing a slave one owns.

This lesson introduces the Hanafi concept of wala' (patronage). You will learn its linguistic derivation, the prophetic proof that establishes it, and its cause: emancipating a slave whom you own. Understanding this foundation is essential for grasping the inheritance and blood money rulings that follow.

Guided Path
1
Identify the eight aspects of discussion
The passage outlines eight aspects; we focus on aspects one to three: derivation, proof, and cause.
2
Trace the derivation of wala'
It comes from 'al-wala'' (closeness) or 'al-muwalah' (mutual help). Also from 'al-wilayah' (help and love).
The multiple derivations reinforce the bond of support.
3
State the proof
The primary proof is the hadith 'al-wala' liman a'taq' (patronage belongs to the one who frees), and another hadith likening wala' to the bond of lineage.
These are ahad hadith but widely accepted.
4
Explain the cause
The cause (sabab) is emancipation. The commentator specifies that the correct view is freeing one's own slave, because attribution indicates specification.
This excludes cases where wala' arises from inheritance of a relative who becomes free.

(۳۳ (۲) رواه الدارمي في كتاب الفرائض باب ٥٣ كتاب الولاء ۱۱۷ الولاء لمن أعتق ولو بتدبير وكتابة واستيلاد وملك قريب وشرط السائبة لغو ولو أعتق أن المطلوب بالشيء لا يكون نفسه بل يكون أمراً مغايراً له قال في العناية : وهو في عرف الفقهاء عبارة عن تناصر يوجب الإرث والعقل ا هـ . وأما ركنه فقوله أعتقته أو ملك القريب أو عقدت الموالاة، ويشترط كون المعتق أهلاً للولاء وهو أن يكون أهلاً للإرث وهو كونه حراً مسلماً وأولاده يكونوا أهلاً بالعصوبة لا بالقرابة وحكمه أن يعقل الجناية حال حياة معتقه والإرث منه بعد مماته. قال رحمه الله : (الولاء لمن أعتق ولو بتدبير وكتابة واستيلاد وملك قريب) لما روينا وهو بعمومه يتناول الكل لأن الرقيق هالك حكماً ألا ترى أنه لا يثبت في حقه كثير من الأحكام التي تختص بالأحياء نحو القضاء والشهادة والملك في الأموال وكثير من العبادات فكان الإعتاق احياء له لثبوت أحكام الأحياء به كالأحياء بالإيلاد فيرث به كما يرث الأب ولده ولهذا سمي ولاء نعمة لقوله تعالى وإذ تقول للذي أنعم الله عليه بالهدي وأنعمت عليه ﴾ [الأحزاب: ٣٧] بالإعتاق والمرأة في هذا كالرجل. وقوله «الولاء لمن أعتق صادق بما إذا أعتق في دار الإسلام أو في دار الحرب وخلي سبيله في دار الحرب أو لم يخل وليس كذلك لأنه إذا أعتق في دار الحرب وخلاه لم يكن له عليه ولاء حتى إذا خرجا إلينا مسلمين لا يرثه ولم يكن له عليه ولاء وعند أبي يوسف يرثه ويكون عليه له الولاء، فلو قال مسلماً ولو رقيقاً كافراً في دارنا لكان أحسن ولو أدى المكاتب بعد موت المولى فعتق فولاؤه للمولى فيكون لعصبته الذكور. وقوله لمن أعتق» يعني ولو حكماً فدخل العبد الموصي بعتقه وبشرائه وأعتقه الوصي بعد موته فولاؤه لعصبة المولى، وكذا مدبروه وأمهات أولاده بعد موته ويكون ولاؤهم له وفي شرح الطحاوي: إذا أمر غيره بإعتاق عبد فأعتق في حال حياته أو بعد وفاته يكون عن الآمر والولاء له ولو قال لغيره أعتق عبدك عني على ألف درهم فأعتق فالعتق يكون عن الآمر استحساناً والولاء له. ولو قال أعتق عبدك عني ولم يذكر البدل فأعتق عتق عن المأمور والولاء له في قولهما، وفي قول أبي يوسف عن الآمر والولاء له ولو قال أعتق عبدك على ألف درهم ولم يقل عني فأعتق فإنه يتوقف على قبول العيد، فإن قبل في المجلس الذي علم به لزمه المال وإلا فلا والولاء يورث ا هـ. وشمل قوله لمن أعتق الذمي لأن الذمي أهلاً للولاء كالمسلم. وفي المحيط : حربي أعتق عبده فلا يخلو إما أن أعتقه في دار الحرب أو في دار الإسلام، فإن أعتقه في الحرب وكان العبد مسلماً فولاؤه له لأنه لا يسترق وإن كان كافراً فلا ولاء له عليه لأن دار عند الولاء نتيجة العتق وإعتاق الحربي عبده المسلم يصح بالإجماع وعبده الكافر لا يصح . الإمام ومحمد إذا لم يخل سبيله، وإن خلى سبيله صح العتق لكنه لم يتم العتق في حق زوال الرق وإن صح في حق إزالة الملك لأن كون الحربي في داره سبب لرقه فإذا أعتق الحربي عبده الكافر في دار الإسلام صح عتقه، وكل معتق جرى عليه الرق بعد العتق انتقض به ولاؤه.
The book of wala' is placed after the book of the mukatab because wala' is among the effects of the mukatab due to the removal of ownership of the person upon payment of the kitaba. Although it is an effect of emancipation, the reasons for arranging the previous books led the mukatab to this position, so it was necessary to delay the book of wala' after the book of the mukatab so that the effect does not precede the cause. The discussion is in eight aspects: first, its derivation; second, its proof; third, its cause; fourth, its linguistic meaning; fifth, its meaning according to the jurists; sixth, its pillar; seventh, its condition; eighth, its ruling. As for the first, it is derived from al-wala' which means closeness, i.e., the occurrence of the second immediately after the first without interval, or from al-muwalah: one says waliya al-shay' when it occurs after it without interval, or from al-wilayah (with fatha) meaning help and love. Its proof is his statement: 'Wala' belongs to the one who frees' and his statement, peace be upon him: 'Wala' is like the bond of lineage.' Its cause is emancipation because the master bestowed favor on his slave by freeing him. The commentator said: the correct view is that its cause is freeing a slave whom one owns, because it is attributed to him and attribution indicates specification, and because whoever inherits his relative and that relative becomes free by virtue of being owned, the wala' goes to him even though he did not perform the freeing. As for its linguistic meaning, it is assistance and help, or continuous connection and friendship. The wali is named wali for mutual support and help for his beloved and friend. According to the jurists, it is mutual support, whether by emancipation or by a contract of muwalah. Hence it is said in al-Mabsut: the objective in both is mutual support. So in al-Nihayah. And it was objected that what is mentioned in al-Mabsut indicates that mutual support is something other than them except themselves, as is not hidden from the intelligent. It is mufa'alah. The hadith is narrated by al-Bukhari, Muslim, etc. The second hadith is narrated by al-Darimi. The book of wala' page 117: 'Wala' belongs to the one who frees, even if by tadbir, kitaba, istilad, or owning a relative, and the condition of the sa'ibah is void, even if he frees...' The objective of a thing is not the thing itself but something other than it. He said in al-Inayah: in the jurists' custom it is mutual support that necessitates inheritance and liability for blood money. End. As for its pillar, it is his saying 'I freed him' or 'I owned a relative' or 'I contracted muwalah'. It is conditioned that the one who frees be qualified for wala', meaning qualified to inherit, i.e., free and Muslim, and his children are qualified by agnatic relationship not by kinship. Its ruling is that he bears blood money during the life of his emancipator and inherits from him after his death. He said: (Wala' belongs to the one who frees, even if by tadbir, kitaba, istilad, or owning a relative) due to what we narrated, and its generality covers all because the slave is legally dead; do you not see that many rulings specific to the living are not established for him, such as judgeship, testimony, ownership of property, and many acts of worship. So emancipation is a revival for him through the establishment of rulings of the living, like giving life through fathering a child, so he inherits by it just as a father inherits from his child. Hence it is called wala' of grace due to His statement: 'And when you said to the one upon whom Allah had bestowed favor and upon whom you had bestowed favor' (Ahzab: 37) by emancipation. The woman is like the man in this. His statement 'Wala' belongs to the one who frees' applies when he frees in Dar al-Islam or in Dar al-Harb and he let him go in Dar al-Harb or did not let him go, but it is not so because if he frees in Dar al-Harb and let him go, there is no wala' over him, so that if they both come out to us as Muslims, he does not inherit from him and there is no wala' over him. According to Abu Yusuf, he inherits from him and has wala' over him. It would have been better if he said 'Muslim, even if a slave, a disbeliever in our land.' If the mukatab pays after the death of the master and becomes free, his wala' belongs to the master, thus to his male agnates. His statement 'to the one who frees' means even if by legal implication, so it includes the slave who was willed to be freed and purchased and the executor freed him after his death, his wala' goes to the agnates of the master. Likewise, his mudabbars and ummahat al-awlad after his death, their wala' belongs to him. In Sharh al-Tahawi: If he ordered someone else to free a slave and he freed during his lifetime or after his death, it is on behalf of the orderer and the wala' is his. If he said to another: 'Free your slave for me for one thousand dirhams' and he freed, the emancipation is on behalf of the orderer by istihsan and the wala' is his. If he said: 'Free your slave for me' without mentioning compensation, and he freed, it is on behalf of the one ordered and the wala' is his according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), but in the view of Abu Yusuf it is on behalf of the orderer and the wala' is his. If he said: 'Free your slave for one thousand dirhams' and did not say 'for me', then he freed, it is suspended on the acceptance of the slave; if he accepts in the gathering where he learned of it, the money is binding, otherwise not, and the wala' is inherited. End. His statement 'to the one who frees' includes the dhimmi because the dhimmi is qualified for wala' like the Muslim. In al-Muhit: A harbi freed his slave; it is either that he freed him in Dar al-Harb or in Dar al-Islam. If he freed him in Dar al-Harb and the slave was Muslim, his wala' is for him because he cannot be enslaved; if he was a disbeliever, there is no wala' for him over him because...    Dar... according to... wala' is the result of emancipation, and the freeing of the Muslim slave by a harbi is valid by consensus, while freeing his disbelieving slave is not valid. Imam (Abu Hanifa) and Muhammad (say): if he did not let him go, but if he let him go, the emancipation is valid but it is not complete regarding the removal of slavery, although it is valid regarding the removal of ownership because the harbi being in his land is a cause of his enslavement. If the harbi frees his disbelieving slave in Dar al-Islam, his emancipation is valid, and whoever is freed then becomes enslaved again, his wala' is nullified.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Wala' (Patronage) in al-Bahr al-Raiq. The author first explains why this book follows the Book of the Mukatab: wala' is an effect of the mukatab's situation. He then outlines eight aspects of discussion: derivation, proof, cause, linguistic meaning, technical meaning, pillar, condition, and ruling. The derivation is from closeness or help. The proof is the famous hadith 'Wala' belongs to the one who frees' and another hadith likening wala' to lineage. The cause is freeing a slave one owns; the correct view according to the commentator is that it is specifically freeing one's own slave. Linguistically, wala' means assistance; technically among Hanafi jurists, it is mutual support that leads to inheritance and liability for blood money. The pillar is the utterance of freeing. The condition is that the emancipator be qualified to inherit, i.e., free and Muslim. The ruling includes the emancipator bearing blood money for the freed slave during his lifetime and inheriting from him after death. The matn states that wala' belongs to the one who frees, even if by tadbir, kitaba, istilad, or owning a relative who becomes free. The commentator explains that the slave is legally dead, so emancipation is like giving life, hence the inheriting relationship. He then discusses various scenarios: freeing in Dar al-Islam vs. Dar al-Harb, and notes an intra-Hanafi dispute where Abu Yusuf differs regarding a slave freed in Dar al-Harb and let go. The passage also covers cases of ordering another to free, and includes a discussion on the harbi freeing his slave. Throughout, the emphasis is that wala' follows emancipation in all its forms, and it is a right that cannot be nullified by conditions like making the freed slave a sa'ibah.

Key Terms
الولاء (al-wala'): A legal relationship between the emancipator and the freed slave that results in inheritance rights and liability for blood money.
المعتق (al-mu'tiq): The person who frees the slave, i.e., the emancipator.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary textual proof for the establishment of wala' according to the passage?
A) Quranic verse from Surah al-Ahzab
B) Ijma' of the Companions
C) Hadith 'al-wala' liman a'taq'
D) Qiyas on lineage

Key Takeaway
Wala' is a fixed legal right proven by the hadith 'al-wala' liman a'taq', caused by freeing one's own slave.

intermediate
8 min
Meaning, Pillar, and Conditions of Wala'
Covers linguistic and technical meaning, pillar, and conditions of wala'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the technical meaning of wala' among Hanafi jurists, identify its pillar (the utterance of freeing), and list the conditions for a valid wala' (emancipator must be free and Muslim).

Core Idea
Wala' technically means mutual support causing inheritance and blood money; its pillar is the declaration of freeing, and its condition is that the emancipator be qualified to inherit.

Having learned the proof of wala', we now delve into its precise technical definition, its pillar (rukn), and its conditions. The Hanafi jurists define wala' as a relationship of mutual support that results in inheritance and liability for blood money. The pillar is the utterance 'I freed you' or similar. The key condition is that the emancipator must be eligible to inherit — meaning he must be free and Muslim.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish linguistic from technical meaning
Linguistically, wala' means assistance or continuous friendship. Technically, it is mutual support (tanasur) that leads to inheritance and liability for blood money.
The technical meaning is narrower and legally operative.
2
Explain the objection and its resolution
An objection is raised that the definition in al-Mabsut implies mutual support is something other than the parties themselves. The response clarifies that the term 'tanasur' is used metaphorically for the legal bond.
This shows the precision of Hanafi technical definitions.
3
Identify the pillar (rukn)
The pillar is the emancipator's statement, such as 'I freed him' or 'I contracted muwalah'. This is a verbal declaration.
In Hanafi fiqh, the rukn of a contract is the offer and acceptance; here it is the declaration of freeing.
4
List the conditions (shurut)
The condition is that the emancipator be qualified for wala', meaning he must be free and Muslim. His children must be agnatic heirs (not through kinship).
A non-Muslim cannot inherit from a Muslim, so wala' is not established for a non-Muslim emancipator if the freed slave is Muslim.

أورد كتاب الولاء عقب المكاتب لأن الولاء من آثار المكاتب لزوال ملك الرقبة عند أداء بدل الكتابة وهو وإن كان من آثار العتق إلا أن موجبات ترتيب الكتب السابقة ساقت المكاتب إلى هذا الموضع فوجب تأخير كتاب الولاء عن كتاب المكاتب لئلا يتقدم الأثر على المؤثر. والكلام فيه من وجوه الأول في اشتقاقه والثاني في بيان دليله، والثالث في سببه، والرابع في معناه لغة والخامس في معناه عند الفقهاء والسادس في ركنه، والسابع في شرطه، والثامن في حكمه. أما الأول فهو مشتق من الولاء وهو القرب وهو حصول الثاني عقيب الأول من غير فصل، أو من الموالاة يقال ولي الشيء إذا حصل بعده من غير فصل، من الولاية بالفتح وهو النصرة والمحبة ودليله قوله «الولاء لمن أعتق»(۱) وقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام الولاء لحمة كلحمة النسب (۲) . وسببه الإعتاق لأن المولى أنعم على عبده بالإعتاق قال الشارح والأصح أن سببه العتق على ملكه لأنه يضاف إليه والإضافة دليل الاختصاص، ولأن من ورث قريبه عتق عليه وولاؤه له ولا إعتاق من جهته. وأما معناه لغة وهو عبارة عن المعاونة والنصرة أو عبارة عن المواصلة والمصادقة الولي وسمي ولياً لتناصره وتعاونه لحبيبه وصديقه. وعند الفقهاء عبارة عن التناصر سواء كان بالإعتاق أو بعقد الموالاة ولهذا قال في المبسوط والمطلوب بكل منهما التناصر ؛ كذا في النهاية. وأورد عليه بأن المذكور في المبسوط يدل على كون التناصر غيرهما إلا أنفسهما إذ لا يخفى على الفطن . وهو مفاعلة (۱) رواه البخاري في كتاب الصلاة، باب ۷۰ . كتاب الفرائض باب ۱۹ ، ۲۰ ، ۲۲ . مسلم في كتاب العتق باب ٥، ٦، ٨. أبو داود في كتاب الفرائض باب ۱۲ النسائي في كتاب الزكاة باب ۹۹. الموطأ في كتاب الطلاق حديث ٢٥ كتاب العتق حديث ۱۷ ۱۹ . أحمد في مسنده (۱/ ۲۸۱، ۳۲۱) (٦/ . (۳۳ (۲) رواه الدارمي في كتاب الفرائض باب ٥٣ كتاب الولاء ۱۱۷ الولاء لمن أعتق ولو بتدبير وكتابة واستيلاد وملك قريب وشرط السائبة لغو ولو أعتق أن المطلوب بالشيء لا يكون نفسه بل يكون أمراً مغايراً له قال في العناية : وهو في عرف الفقهاء عبارة عن تناصر يوجب الإرث والعقل ا هـ . وأما ركنه فقوله أعتقته أو ملك القريب أو عقدت الموالاة، ويشترط كون المعتق أهلاً للولاء وهو أن يكون أهلاً للإرث وهو كونه حراً مسلماً وأولاده يكونوا أهلاً بالعصوبة لا بالقرابة وحكمه أن يعقل الجناية حال حياة معتقه والإرث منه بعد مماته. قال رحمه الله : (الولاء لمن أعتق ولو بتدبير وكتابة واستيلاد وملك قريب) لما روينا وهو بعمومه يتناول الكل لأن الرقيق هالك حكماً ألا ترى أنه لا يثبت في حقه كثير من الأحكام التي تختص بالأحياء نحو القضاء والشهادة والملك في الأموال وكثير من العبادات فكان الإعتاق احياء له لثبوت أحكام الأحياء به كالأحياء بالإيلاد فيرث به كما يرث الأب ولده ولهذا سمي ولاء نعمة لقوله تعالى وإذ تقول للذي أنعم الله عليه بالهدي وأنعمت عليه ﴾ [الأحزاب: ٣٧] بالإعتاق والمرأة في هذا كالرجل. وقوله «الولاء لمن أعتق صادق بما إذا أعتق في دار الإسلام أو في دار الحرب وخلي سبيله في دار الحرب أو لم يخل وليس كذلك لأنه إذا أعتق في دار الحرب وخلاه لم يكن له عليه ولاء حتى إذا خرجا إلينا مسلمين لا يرثه ولم يكن له عليه ولاء وعند أبي يوسف يرثه ويكون عليه له الولاء، فلو قال مسلماً ولو رقيقاً كافراً في دارنا لكان أحسن ولو أدى المكاتب بعد موت المولى فعتق فولاؤه للمولى فيكون لعصبته الذكور. وقوله لمن أعتق» يعني ولو حكماً فدخل العبد الموصي بعتقه وبشرائه وأعتقه الوصي بعد موته فولاؤه لعصبة المولى، وكذا مدبروه وأمهات أولاده بعد موته ويكون ولاؤهم له وفي شرح الطحاوي: إذا أمر غيره بإعتاق عبد فأعتق في حال حياته أو بعد وفاته يكون عن الآمر والولاء له ولو قال لغيره أعتق عبدك عني على ألف درهم فأعتق فالعتق يكون عن الآمر استحساناً والولاء له. ولو قال أعتق عبدك عني ولم يذكر البدل فأعتق عتق عن المأمور والولاء له في قولهما، وفي قول أبي يوسف عن الآمر والولاء له ولو قال أعتق عبدك على ألف درهم ولم يقل عني فأعتق فإنه يتوقف على قبول العيد، فإن قبل في المجلس الذي علم به لزمه المال وإلا فلا والولاء يورث ا هـ. وشمل قوله لمن أعتق الذمي لأن الذمي أهلاً للولاء كالمسلم. وفي المحيط : حربي أعتق عبده فلا يخلو إما أن أعتقه في دار الحرب أو في دار الإسلام، فإن أعتقه في الحرب وكان العبد مسلماً فولاؤه له لأنه لا يسترق وإن كان كافراً فلا ولاء له عليه لأن دار عند الولاء نتيجة العتق وإعتاق الحربي عبده المسلم يصح بالإجماع وعبده الكافر لا يصح . الإمام ومحمد إذا لم يخل سبيله، وإن خلى سبيله صح العتق لكنه لم يتم العتق في حق زوال الرق وإن صح في حق إزالة الملك لأن كون الحربي في داره سبب لرقه فإذا أعتق الحربي عبده الكافر في دار الإسلام صح عتقه، وكل معتق جرى عليه الرق بعد العتق انتقض به ولاؤه.

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Wala' (Patronage) in al-Bahr al-Raiq. The author first explains why this book follows the Book of the Mukatab: wala' is an effect of the mukatab's situation. He then outlines eight aspects of discussion: derivation, proof, cause, linguistic meaning, technical meaning, pillar, condition, and ruling. The derivation is from closeness or help. The proof is the famous hadith 'Wala' belongs to the one who frees' and another hadith likening wala' to lineage. The cause is freeing a slave one owns; the correct view according to the commentator is that it is specifically freeing one's own slave. Linguistically, wala' means assistance; technically among Hanafi jurists, it is mutual support that leads to inheritance and liability for blood money. The pillar is the utterance of freeing. The condition is that the emancipator be qualified to inherit, i.e., free and Muslim. The ruling includes the emancipator bearing blood money for the freed slave during his lifetime and inheriting from him after death. The matn states that wala' belongs to the one who frees, even if by tadbir, kitaba, istilad, or owning a relative who becomes free. The commentator explains that the slave is legally dead, so emancipation is like giving life, hence the inheriting relationship. He then discusses various scenarios: freeing in Dar al-Islam vs. Dar al-Harb, and notes an intra-Hanafi dispute where Abu Yusuf differs regarding a slave freed in Dar al-Harb and let go. The passage also covers cases of ordering another to free, and includes a discussion on the harbi freeing his slave. Throughout, the emphasis is that wala' follows emancipation in all its forms, and it is a right that cannot be nullified by conditions like making the freed slave a sa'ibah.

Key Terms
التناصر (al-tanasur): Mutual support and helping, used metaphorically for the legal bond of wala'.
الركن (al-rukn): The pillar or essential element of wala', which is the verbal declaration of freeing.
الشرط (al-shart): Condition that the emancipator be free and Muslim, i.e., qualified to inherit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the condition (shart) for the validity of wala'?
A) The emancipator must be wealthy.
B) The emancipator must be free and Muslim.
C) The slave must consent to the emancipation.
D) The emancipation must be in Dar al-Islam.

Key Takeaway
The pillar of wala' is the verbal declaration, and the key condition is that the emancipator be free and Muslim to be eligible to inherit.

Ruling of Wala' and the Dar al-Harb Dispute
Ruling of wala' and intra-Hanafi dispute on freeing in Dar al-Harb.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of wala' (inheritance and 'aql) and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding wala' for a slave freed in Dar al-Harb and let go.

Core Idea
Wala' obligates the emancipator to pay blood money and inherit; but if a harbi frees a slave in Dar al-Harb and lets him go, no wala' according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, contrary to Abu Yusuf.

This lesson covers the practical ruling of wala': the patron is liable for blood money and inherits from the freed slave. It also examines a significant intra-Hanafi dispute about whether wala' is established when a harbi frees his slave in Dar al-Harb and releases him. The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) say no, while Abu Yusuf disagrees. Understanding this dispute highlights how the legal consequence (thamarah) differs.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling of wala'
The ruling (hukm) is that the emancipator is liable for blood money (ya'qilu al-jinayah) during his life and inherits from the freed slave after his death.
This is the legal effect of the bond of wala'.
2
Present the disputed scenario
A harbi (non-Muslim from enemy territory) frees his disbelieving slave in Dar al-Harb and releases him (khalla sabeelehi).
The slave is a disbeliever, so enslavement is permissible.
3
Compare the positions
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: no wala' is established because the emancipation is incomplete regarding the removal of slavery. Abu Yusuf: wala' is established because the emancipation is valid.
The difference hinges on whether the freeing is complete in Dar al-Harb.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if the freed slave dies, according to the majority, the harbi does not inherit; according to Abu Yusuf, he does.
This affects inheritance planning and blood money liability.
5
Note the tarjih
The text leans towards the majority view by saying 'laysa kathalika' (it is not so).
The mufta bihi (relied-upon view) is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
