(۳۳ (۲) رواه الدارمي في كتاب الفرائض باب ٥٣ كتاب الولاء ۱۱۷ الولاء لمن أعتق ولو بتدبير وكتابة واستيلاد وملك قريب وشرط السائبة لغو ولو أعتق أن المطلوب بالشيء لا يكون نفسه بل يكون أمراً مغايراً له قال في العناية : وهو في عرف الفقهاء عبارة عن تناصر يوجب الإرث والعقل ا هـ . وأما ركنه فقوله أعتقته أو ملك القريب أو عقدت الموالاة، ويشترط كون المعتق أهلاً للولاء وهو أن يكون أهلاً للإرث وهو كونه حراً مسلماً وأولاده يكونوا أهلاً بالعصوبة لا بالقرابة وحكمه أن يعقل الجناية حال حياة معتقه والإرث منه بعد مماته. قال رحمه الله : (الولاء لمن أعتق ولو بتدبير وكتابة واستيلاد وملك قريب) لما روينا وهو بعمومه يتناول الكل لأن الرقيق هالك حكماً ألا ترى أنه لا يثبت في حقه كثير من الأحكام التي تختص بالأحياء نحو القضاء والشهادة والملك في الأموال وكثير من العبادات فكان الإعتاق احياء له لثبوت أحكام الأحياء به كالأحياء بالإيلاد فيرث به كما يرث الأب ولده ولهذا سمي ولاء نعمة لقوله تعالى وإذ تقول للذي أنعم الله عليه بالهدي وأنعمت عليه ﴾ [الأحزاب: ٣٧] بالإعتاق والمرأة في هذا كالرجل. وقوله «الولاء لمن أعتق صادق بما إذا أعتق في دار الإسلام أو في دار الحرب وخلي سبيله في دار الحرب أو لم يخل وليس كذلك لأنه إذا أعتق في دار الحرب وخلاه لم يكن له عليه ولاء حتى إذا خرجا إلينا مسلمين لا يرثه ولم يكن له عليه ولاء وعند أبي يوسف يرثه ويكون عليه له الولاء، فلو قال مسلماً ولو رقيقاً كافراً في دارنا لكان أحسن ولو أدى المكاتب بعد موت المولى فعتق فولاؤه للمولى فيكون لعصبته الذكور. وقوله لمن أعتق» يعني ولو حكماً فدخل العبد الموصي بعتقه وبشرائه وأعتقه الوصي بعد موته فولاؤه لعصبة المولى، وكذا مدبروه وأمهات أولاده بعد موته ويكون ولاؤهم له وفي شرح الطحاوي: إذا أمر غيره بإعتاق عبد فأعتق في حال حياته أو بعد وفاته يكون عن الآمر والولاء له ولو قال لغيره أعتق عبدك عني على ألف درهم فأعتق فالعتق يكون عن الآمر استحساناً والولاء له. ولو قال أعتق عبدك عني ولم يذكر البدل فأعتق عتق عن المأمور والولاء له في قولهما، وفي قول أبي يوسف عن الآمر والولاء له ولو قال أعتق عبدك على ألف درهم ولم يقل عني فأعتق فإنه يتوقف على قبول العيد، فإن قبل في المجلس الذي علم به لزمه المال وإلا فلا والولاء يورث ا هـ. وشمل قوله لمن أعتق الذمي لأن الذمي أهلاً للولاء كالمسلم. وفي المحيط : حربي أعتق عبده فلا يخلو إما أن أعتقه في دار الحرب أو في دار الإسلام، فإن أعتقه في الحرب وكان العبد مسلماً فولاؤه له لأنه لا يسترق وإن كان كافراً فلا ولاء له عليه لأن دار عند الولاء نتيجة العتق وإعتاق الحربي عبده المسلم يصح بالإجماع وعبده الكافر لا يصح . الإمام ومحمد إذا لم يخل سبيله، وإن خلى سبيله صح العتق لكنه لم يتم العتق في حق زوال الرق وإن صح في حق إزالة الملك لأن كون الحربي في داره سبب لرقه فإذا أعتق الحربي عبده الكافر في دار الإسلام صح عتقه، وكل معتق جرى عليه الرق بعد العتق انتقض به ولاؤه.
The book of wala' is placed after the book of the mukatab because wala' is among the effects of the mukatab due to the removal of ownership of the person upon payment of the kitaba. Although it is an effect of emancipation, the reasons for arranging the previous books led the mukatab to this position, so it was necessary to delay the book of wala' after the book of the mukatab so that the effect does not precede the cause. The discussion is in eight aspects: first, its derivation; second, its proof; third, its cause; fourth, its linguistic meaning; fifth, its meaning according to the jurists; sixth, its pillar; seventh, its condition; eighth, its ruling. As for the first, it is derived from al-wala' which means closeness, i.e., the occurrence of the second immediately after the first without interval, or from al-muwalah: one says waliya al-shay' when it occurs after it without interval, or from al-wilayah (with fatha) meaning help and love. Its proof is his statement: 'Wala' belongs to the one who frees' and his statement, peace be upon him: 'Wala' is like the bond of lineage.' Its cause is emancipation because the master bestowed favor on his slave by freeing him. The commentator said: the correct view is that its cause is freeing a slave whom one owns, because it is attributed to him and attribution indicates specification, and because whoever inherits his relative and that relative becomes free by virtue of being owned, the wala' goes to him even though he did not perform the freeing. As for its linguistic meaning, it is assistance and help, or continuous connection and friendship. The wali is named wali for mutual support and help for his beloved and friend. According to the jurists, it is mutual support, whether by emancipation or by a contract of muwalah. Hence it is said in al-Mabsut: the objective in both is mutual support. So in al-Nihayah. And it was objected that what is mentioned in al-Mabsut indicates that mutual support is something other than them except themselves, as is not hidden from the intelligent. It is mufa'alah. The hadith is narrated by al-Bukhari, Muslim, etc. The second hadith is narrated by al-Darimi. The book of wala' page 117: 'Wala' belongs to the one who frees, even if by tadbir, kitaba, istilad, or owning a relative, and the condition of the sa'ibah is void, even if he frees...' The objective of a thing is not the thing itself but something other than it. He said in al-Inayah: in the jurists' custom it is mutual support that necessitates inheritance and liability for blood money. End. As for its pillar, it is his saying 'I freed him' or 'I owned a relative' or 'I contracted muwalah'. It is conditioned that the one who frees be qualified for wala', meaning qualified to inherit, i.e., free and Muslim, and his children are qualified by agnatic relationship not by kinship. Its ruling is that he bears blood money during the life of his emancipator and inherits from him after his death. He said: (Wala' belongs to the one who frees, even if by tadbir, kitaba, istilad, or owning a relative) due to what we narrated, and its generality covers all because the slave is legally dead; do you not see that many rulings specific to the living are not established for him, such as judgeship, testimony, ownership of property, and many acts of worship. So emancipation is a revival for him through the establishment of rulings of the living, like giving life through fathering a child, so he inherits by it just as a father inherits from his child. Hence it is called wala' of grace due to His statement: 'And when you said to the one upon whom Allah had bestowed favor and upon whom you had bestowed favor' (Ahzab: 37) by emancipation. The woman is like the man in this. His statement 'Wala' belongs to the one who frees' applies when he frees in Dar al-Islam or in Dar al-Harb and he let him go in Dar al-Harb or did not let him go, but it is not so because if he frees in Dar al-Harb and let him go, there is no wala' over him, so that if they both come out to us as Muslims, he does not inherit from him and there is no wala' over him. According to Abu Yusuf, he inherits from him and has wala' over him. It would have been better if he said 'Muslim, even if a slave, a disbeliever in our land.' If the mukatab pays after the death of the master and becomes free, his wala' belongs to the master, thus to his male agnates. His statement 'to the one who frees' means even if by legal implication, so it includes the slave who was willed to be freed and purchased and the executor freed him after his death, his wala' goes to the agnates of the master. Likewise, his mudabbars and ummahat al-awlad after his death, their wala' belongs to him. In Sharh al-Tahawi: If he ordered someone else to free a slave and he freed during his lifetime or after his death, it is on behalf of the orderer and the wala' is his. If he said to another: 'Free your slave for me for one thousand dirhams' and he freed, the emancipation is on behalf of the orderer by istihsan and the wala' is his. If he said: 'Free your slave for me' without mentioning compensation, and he freed, it is on behalf of the one ordered and the wala' is his according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), but in the view of Abu Yusuf it is on behalf of the orderer and the wala' is his. If he said: 'Free your slave for one thousand dirhams' and did not say 'for me', then he freed, it is suspended on the acceptance of the slave; if he accepts in the gathering where he learned of it, the money is binding, otherwise not, and the wala' is inherited. End. His statement 'to the one who frees' includes the dhimmi because the dhimmi is qualified for wala' like the Muslim. In al-Muhit: A harbi freed his slave; it is either that he freed him in Dar al-Harb or in Dar al-Islam. If he freed him in Dar al-Harb and the slave was Muslim, his wala' is for him because he cannot be enslaved; if he was a disbeliever, there is no wala' for him over him because...    Dar... according to... wala' is the result of emancipation, and the freeing of the Muslim slave by a harbi is valid by consensus, while freeing his disbelieving slave is not valid. Imam (Abu Hanifa) and Muhammad (say): if he did not let him go, but if he let him go, the emancipation is valid but it is not complete regarding the removal of slavery, although it is valid regarding the removal of ownership because the harbi being in his land is a cause of his enslavement. If the harbi frees his disbelieving slave in Dar al-Islam, his emancipation is valid, and whoever is freed then becomes enslaved again, his wala' is nullified.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Wala' (Patronage) in al-Bahr al-Raiq. The author first explains why this book follows the Book of the Mukatab: wala' is an effect of the mukatab's situation. He then outlines eight aspects of discussion: derivation, proof, cause, linguistic meaning, technical meaning, pillar, condition, and ruling. The derivation is from closeness or help. The proof is the famous hadith 'Wala' belongs to the one who frees' and another hadith likening wala' to lineage. The cause is freeing a slave one owns; the correct view according to the commentator is that it is specifically freeing one's own slave. Linguistically, wala' means assistance; technically among Hanafi jurists, it is mutual support that leads to inheritance and liability for blood money. The pillar is the utterance of freeing. The condition is that the emancipator be qualified to inherit, i.e., free and Muslim. The ruling includes the emancipator bearing blood money for the freed slave during his lifetime and inheriting from him after death. The matn states that wala' belongs to the one who frees, even if by tadbir, kitaba, istilad, or owning a relative who becomes free. The commentator explains that the slave is legally dead, so emancipation is like giving life, hence the inheriting relationship. He then discusses various scenarios: freeing in Dar al-Islam vs. Dar al-Harb, and notes an intra-Hanafi dispute where Abu Yusuf differs regarding a slave freed in Dar al-Harb and let go. The passage also covers cases of ordering another to free, and includes a discussion on the harbi freeing his slave. Throughout, the emphasis is that wala' follows emancipation in all its forms, and it is a right that cannot be nullified by conditions like making the freed slave a sa'ibah.

Key Terms
دار الحرب (dar al-harb): Territory under non-Muslim rule where the legal effects of Islamic law are not fully applied.
السائبة (al-sa'ibah): A slave freed without any claim of wala' (pre-Islamic practice).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), what is the ruling on wala' if a harbi frees his disbelieving slave in Dar al-Harb and lets him go?
A) Wala' is established regardless.
B) Wala' is established only if the slave becomes Muslim later.
C) No wala' is established.
D) Wala' is established only if the harbi also becomes Muslim.

Key Takeaway
The ruling of wala' is inheritance and blood money liability, but an exception exists for freeing in Dar al-Harb with release, where the majority says no wala'.

Wala Belongs to the Manumitter: Foundational Ruling and Conditions
States the foundational rule of wala and expands on its applications and conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the hadith that establishes wala', explain the conditions for the manumitter, and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute concerning a harbi's slave in Dar al-Harb.

Core Idea
Wala' is an exclusive right of the manumitter that cannot be transferred or waived.

In this lesson, we explore the foundational ruling of wala' (patronage) in Hanafi fiqh. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq comments on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, establishing that wala' belongs to the person who frees a slave, based on the Prophet's hadith. We will learn the conditions for the manumitter, the various forms of manumission that trigger wala', and an important intra-Hanafi disagreement regarding slaveries in Dar al-Harb.

Guided Path
1
Identify the foundational dalil
Locate the hadith 'al-wala li man a'taq' in the passage and note its authority as a sunnah ahad with clear meaning (dalala qat'iyya).
2
Define wala' and its elements
From the commentary, extract the definition of wala' as mutual support entailing inheritance and blood-money. Identify its pillar (the utterance of manumission) and the condition that the manumitter be free and Muslim.
3
List the forms of manumission
The passage states that wala' applies to tadbir, kitaba, istilad, and owning a relative. Note how each form leads to wala'.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Focus on the case of a harbi freeing a disbelieving slave in Dar al-Harb. Understand why Abu Hanifa and Muhammad deny wala' while Abu Yusuf affirms it, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf.
5
Examine proxy manumissions
Review the scenarios where one person orders another to manumit a slave. Determine who the wala' belongs to in each case according to the relied-upon position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الولاء
الولاء لمن أعتق ولو بتدبير وكتابة واستيلاد وملك قريب وشرط السائبة لغو ولو أعتق
أن المطلوب بالشيء لا يكون نفسه بل يكون أمراً مغايراً له قال في العناية : وهو في عرف الفقهاء عبارة عن تناصر يوجب الإرث والعقل ا هـ . وأما ركنه فقوله أعتقته أو ملك القريب أو عقدت الموالاة، ويشترط كون المعتق أهلاً للولاء وهو أن يكون أهلاً للإرث وهو كونه حراً مسلماً وأولاده يكونوا أهلاً بالعصوبة لا بالقرابة وحكمه أن يعقل الجناية حال حياة معتقه والإرث منه بعد مماته. قال رحمه الله : (الولاء لمن أعتق ولو بتدبير وكتابة واستيلاد وملك قريب) لما روينا وهو بعمومه يتناول الكل لأن الرقيق هالك حكماً ألا ترى أنه لا يثبت في حقه كثير من الأحكام التي تختص بالأحياء نحو القضاء والشهادة والملك في الأموال وكثير من العبادات فكان الإعتاق احياء له لثبوت أحكام الأحياء به كالأحياء بالإيلاد فيرث به كما يرث الأب ولده ولهذا سمي ولاء نعمة لقوله تعالى ﴿ وإذ تقول للذي أنعم الله عليه بالهدي وأنعمت عليه ﴾ [الأحزاب: ٣٧] بالإعتاق والمرأة في هذا كالرجل. وقوله «الولاء لمن أعتق صادق بما إذا أعتق في دار الإسلام أو في دار الحرب وخلي سبيله في دار الحرب أو لم يخل وليس كذلك لأنه إذا أعتق في دار الحرب وخلاه لم يكن له عليه ولاء حتى إذا خرجا إلينا مسلمين لا يرثه ولم يكن له عليه ولاء وعند أبي يوسف يرثه ويكون عليه له الولاء، فلو قال مسلماً ولو رقيقاً كافراً في دارنا لكان أحسن ولو أدى المكاتب بعد موت المولى فعتق فولاؤه للمولى فيكون لعصبته الذكور. وقوله لمن أعتق» يعني ولو حكماً فدخل العبد الموصي بعتقه وبشرائه وأعتقه الوصي بعد موته فولاؤه لعصبة المولى، وكذا مدبروه وأمهات أولاده بعد موته ويكون ولاؤهم له وفي شرح الطحاوي: إذا أمر غيره بإعتاق عبد فأعتق في حال حياته أو بعد وفاته يكون عن الآمر والولاء له ولو قال لغيره أعتق عبدك عني على ألف درهم فأعتق فالعتق يكون عن الآمر استحساناً والولاء له. ولو قال أعتق عبدك عني ولم يذكر البدل فأعتق عتق عن المأمور والولاء له في قولهما، وفي قول أبي يوسف عن الآمر والولاء له ولو قال أعتق عبدك على ألف درهم ولم يقل عني فأعتق فإنه يتوقف على قبول العيد، فإن قبل في المجلس الذي علم به لزمه المال وإلا فلا والولاء يورث ا هـ. وشمل قوله لمن أعتق الذمي لأن الذمي أهلاً للولاء كالمسلم. وفي المحيط : حربي أعتق عبده فلا يخلو إما أن أعتقه في دار الحرب أو في دار الإسلام، فإن أعتقه في الحرب وكان العبد مسلماً فولاؤه له لأنه لا يسترق وإن كان كافراً فلا ولاء له عليه لأن دار عند الولاء نتيجة العتق وإعتاق الحربي عبده المسلم يصح بالإجماع وعبده الكافر لا يصح . الإمام ومحمد إذا لم يخل سبيله، وإن خلى سبيله صح العتق لكنه لم يتم العتق في حق زوال الرق وإن صح في حق إزالة الملك لأن كون الحربي في داره سبب لرقه فإذا أعتق الحربي عبده الكافر في دار الإسلام صح عتقه، وكل معتق جرى عليه الرق بعد العتق انتقض به ولاؤه.
The book of Wala. Wala belongs to the one who frees, even if by tadbir, kitaba, istilad, or owning a relative, and the condition of sa'ibah is void. And if he frees... That which is sought by something is not itself but is something different from it. He said in al-'Inayah: It is in the terminology of the jurists an expression for mutual support that necessitates inheritance and blood-money. Its pillar is his saying: I freed him, or I owned the relative, or I contracted wala'. And it is stipulated that the manumitter be qualified for wala', that is, qualified for inheritance, which is being free and Muslim. His children are qualified by 'usubah, not by kinship. Its ruling is that he is responsible for blood-money during the life of his manumitter and inherits from him after his death. He (the author) said: Wala belongs to the one who frees, even if by tadbir, kitaba, istilad, or owning a relative. Based on what we narrated, and it includes everything by its generality, because the slave is legally dead. Do you not see that many rulings specific to the living do not apply to him, such as judiciary, testimony, ownership of property, and many acts of worship? So manumission brings him to life because rulings of the living are established through it, just as bringing to life through istilad. Thus, he inherits through it just as a father inherits from his child. Hence it is called wala' ni'mah (patronage of grace) due to the verse: 'And when you said to the one on whom Allah bestowed favor and you bestowed favor' [al-Ahzab 33:37] by manumission. A woman is like a man in this. His saying 'Wala belongs to the one who frees' applies whether one frees in Dar al-Islam or in Dar al-Harb and releases him in Dar al-Harb or not. But it is not like that. Because if he frees in Dar al-Harb and leaves him, no wala is established until they come out to us as Muslims; he does not inherit from him and no wala is established. According to Abu Yusuf, he inherits and wala is established for him. So if he said 'Muslim, even if a slave, a disbeliever in our abode' it would be better. If the mukatib pays after the death of the master and becomes free, his wala is for the master, then for his male agnates. His saying 'to the one who frees' means even if by legal fiction, so it includes the slave who is bequeathed or purchased and freed by the executor after his death; his wala is for the master's agnates. Likewise, his mudabbar and umm walad after his death, their wala is for him. In Sharh al-Tahawi: If one orders another to free a slave and he frees during his life or after his death, it is on behalf of the commander and wala is for him. If he says to another: Free your slave on my behalf for a thousand dirhams, and he frees, the manumission is on behalf of the commander by istihsan and wala is for him. If he says: Free your slave on my behalf without mentioning payment, and he frees, it is on behalf of the commander according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and according to Abu Yusuf it is on behalf of the commander and wala is for him. If he says: Free your slave for a thousand dirhams without saying 'on my behalf', and he frees, then it depends on acceptance by the slave. If he accepts in the session he learns of it, the money is due; otherwise not, and wala is inherited. His saying 'to the one who frees' includes the dhimmi, because the dhimmi is qualified for wala like the Muslim. In al-Muhit: A harbi frees his slave. Either he frees him in Dar al-Harb or in Dar al-Islam. If he frees him in Dar al-Harb and the slave is Muslim, his wala is for him because he cannot be enslaved. If he is disbeliever, no wala is established for him, because the abode is... Wala is the result of manumission. Manumission by a harbi of his Muslim slave is valid by ijma', but of his disbelieving slave is not valid. Imam (Abu Hanifa) and Muhammad: If he does not release him. If he releases him, the manumission is valid but not completed with regard to removal of slavery, though it is valid with regard to removal of ownership, because the harbi's being in his abode is a cause of enslavement. So if the harbi frees his disbelieving slave in Dar al-Islam, his manumission is valid. Every manumitter who experiences slavery after manumission has his wala invalidated.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It begins the chapter on Wala, defining it as a legal bond of mutual support that entails inheritance and responsibility for blood-money (al-'aql). The author explains that the pillar (rukn) of wala is the act of manumission, and the condition is that the manumitter must be eligible for wala: free and Muslim. He then cites the hadith 'al-wala li man a'taq' (Wala belongs to the one who frees) as the foundational proof. The commentary expands on the ruling by stating that it applies to all forms of manumission: direct, tadbir (declaration upon death), kitaba (contract of manumission), istilad (bearing a child to the master), and even ownership of a relative. It then discusses special scenarios: manumission in Dar al-Harb, where the school holds that wala is not established for a harbi's disbelieving slave unless the slave is Muslim. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf holds that wala is established even for a disbelieving slave. The passage also covers cases of manumission by proxy, manumission on behalf of another, and the rulings for dhimmis and harbis. The overall message is that wala is a legal consequence of manumission that cannot be separated from it.

Key Terms
الولاء (al-wala'): A legal bond of mutual support between the manumitter and the freed slave, entitling the manumitter to inherit from the freed slave and be responsible for his blood-money.
المعتق (al-mu'tiq): The one who frees a slave, becoming the patron (mawla) of the freed slave.
التدبير (al-tadbir): A declaration by the master that a slave will be free upon the master's death.
الكتابة (al-kitaba): A contract between master and slave whereby the slave is to pay a sum of money and become free.
الاستيلاد (al-istilad): The master's act of begetting a child from his female slave, making her an umm walad who becomes free upon the master's death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited in the passage, who does the wala of a freed slave belong to?
A) The state
B) The manumitter
C) The freed slave's family
D) The mosque

Key Takeaway
Wala' is an exclusive right of the manumitter that cannot be transferred or waived, established by a clear hadith and applied to all forms of manumission.

The Condition of Sa'ibah is Void
Ruling statement: condition of sa'ibah is void.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the condition of sa'ibah, explain why it is void, and apply the principle to analogous cases where a condition contradicts Shari'ah.

Core Idea
The condition that a freed slave be a sa'ibah is void; the manumitter retains wala and inheritance.

In pre-Islamic Arabia, some masters freed slaves with the condition that the slave had no further ties—no patronage (wala) and no inheritance. This practice, known as sa'ibah, was later questioned in Islamic law. The author of the matn addresses it directly: any such condition is legally void. In this lesson, we examine the ruling and its rationale, rooted in the principle that conditions contradicting Shari'ah are without effect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Identify the act: stipulating that the freed slave be a sa'ibah (no wala). The ruling: the condition is void (laghw) and the manumission itself is valid, with wala established for the manumitter.
The term 'sa'ibah' refers to a freed slave cut off from patronage.
2
Understand the legal principle
The condition is void because it contradicts the Shari'ah ruling that wala belongs to the manumitter (based on the hadith 'al-wala' li man a'taqa'). Any condition that contradicts a clear Shari'ah ruling is invalid.
This is analogous to the rule that one cannot stipulate that a son not inherit from his father.
3
Apply the analogy with lineage
The commentary draws an analogy: just as a father cannot stipulate that his son will not inherit from him, a manumitter cannot stipulate that he will not inherit from the freed slave. The wala relationship is treated like lineage for inheritance purposes.
This analogy (qiyas) reinforces that the condition is without legal effect.
4
Confirm the practical consequence
The manumitter inherits from the freed slave despite the condition. The condition does not affect the validity of the manumission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وشرط السائبة لغو) يعني لو أعتق المولى عبده وشرط أن لا يرثه كان الشرط لغواً لكونه مخالفاً لحكم الشرع فيرثه كما في النسب إذا شرط أن لا يرثه .
He (the author) said: 'And the condition of being a sa'ibah is void.' That is, if the master frees his slave and stipulates that he will not inherit from him, the condition is void because it contradicts the ruling of Shari'ah. So he inherits from him, just as in lineage, if one stipulates that he will not inherit from him.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This is a concise ruling from the matn explained by the commentator. The term 'sa'ibah' refers to a freed slave who is cut off from any patronage (wala). The author of the matn states that if a manumitter stipulates that the freed slave will be a sa'ibah (i.e., no wala will exist), that stipulation is legally void. The reason is that it contradicts the explicit ruling of the Shari'ah that wala belongs to the manumitter. The commentary draws an analogy with lineage: just as a father cannot stipulate that his son will not inherit from him, a manumitter cannot stipulate that he will not inherit from the freed slave. The wala remains intact, and the manumitter inherits from the freed slave as normal.

Key Terms
السائبة (al-sa'ibah): A freed slave who is set free without any patronage (wala) to the manumitter; the practice of making a slave sa'ibah was from pre-Islam.
لغو (laghw): Legally void; something that does not take effect in the eyes of the law.
الولاء (al-wala'): Patronage; the legal relationship between the manumitter and the freed slave, which includes the right of inheritance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a manumitter stipulates that the freed slave will be a sa'ibah with no patronage, what is the ruling?
A) The stipulation is valid and wala is lost
B) The stipulation is void and wala remains with the manumitter
C) The freed slave may choose a patron
D) The manumitter loses the right to inherit but retains other rights

Key Takeaway
The condition of sa'ibah is void because it contradicts the Shari'ah ruling that wala belongs to the manumitter; the manumitter retains inheritance rights.

Wala of a Child Born to a Freed Pregnant Woman: Permanence and Transfer
Ruling on the wala of a child born to a freed slave woman and its potential transfer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on the wala of a child born to a freed pregnant slave woman and explain when the wala may transfer to the father's manumitter.

Core Idea
The wala of a child freed with its mother remains with her manumitter, but transfers to the father's patrons if he is later freed.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a subtle issue in the fiqh of wala (patronage). When a pregnant slave woman is freed, her child is also freed, and the wala belongs to the mother's manumitter. But what if the father, who was a slave at the time of birth, is later freed? Does the wala transfer to the father's patrons? The text resolves this by drawing on a hadith that likens wala to lineage, and clarifies the timeline using the six-month minimum gestation period. Understanding this rule is crucial for correctly assigning the rights of inheritance and other legal consequences tied to wala.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling and its exception
The text states that if a pregnant slave woman is freed, the wala of the fetus does not transfer from the mother's patrons ever—but then adds that if the father (the slave husband) is later freed, the wala is drawn to his patrons. Identify this as the default rule and the exception.
2
Trace the legal basis for the default rule
The child is freed because it is part of the mother; the manumission is intended for the whole, so the child is freed intentionally. This is supported by the hadith 'al-wala li man a'taq' (patronage belongs to the one who frees). The child's wala stays with the mother's manumitter because it was the mother's manumission that caused the child's freedom.
The text also addresses an apparent contradiction about whether the child is freed intentionally or as a consequence.
3
Understand the timeline: the six-month rule
The fetus is considered to have existed at the time of manumission if the mother gives birth within six months. If born after more than six months, it is not deemed to have been freed with the mother, but the wala still goes to her manumitter because the child follows her in legal attributes. This step clarifies how to determine the child's status.
4
Analyze the transfer upon father's manumission
When the father (who was a slave at the child's birth) is freed, the wala transfers to his patrons. The basis is the hadith 'al-wala luhmah kaluhmat al-nasab' (wala is a bond like the bond of lineage), and lineage is to the fathers. Since the impediment of the father's slavery is removed, it becomes possible to attribute the child's wala to him, just as lineage transfers when an impediment is removed (e.g., in cases of li'an).
This is an example of Hanafi istihsan based on analogy.
5
Apply to a practical dispute
The text cites a case from al-Tatarakhaniyyah: if the mother and father disagree on the timing of the birth (whether it was within six months of her freeing), the husband's statement is given precedence. This shows how the six-month rule is applied in practice when evidence conflicts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( ولو أعتق حاملاً من زوجها القن لا ينتقل ولاء الحمل عن موالي الأم أبداً) لأن الجنين عتق بعتق أمه وعتق أمه مقصود فكذا هو يعتق مقصوداً لأنه هو جزء الأم والمولى أوقع الإعتاق على جميع أجزائها، وأورد أن هذا مخالف لما ذكر في كتاب الإعتاق فإنهم هناك قالوا : وإن أعتق حاملاً عتق حملها تبعاً لها إذ هو متصل بها، فأوردوا أنه يعتق تبعاً لا قصداً وهذا منافٍ لما ذكروه ،هنا، والأصل في هذا قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «الولاء لمن أعتق» وإنما يعرف كون الحمل موجوداً عند العتق بأن تلده لأقل . من ستة أشهر من وقت العتق، وكذا إذا ولدت ولدين أحدهما لأقل من ستة أشهر والآخر لأكثر منه وبينهما أقل من ستة أشهر لأنا تيقنا أن الأول كان موجوداً عند العتق فإذا تناول الإعتاق الأول تناول الآخر ضرورة وصار معتقاً لهما، والولاء لا ينتقل من المعتق . وقوله من زوجها القن» مثال، وكذا لو كان زوجها مكاتباً أو مديراً. وقوله من زوجها صادق بحال قيام النكاح أو بعده وما بعد النكاح لا يتأتى فيه هذا التفصيل فكان عليه أن يقول ولو أعتق حاملاً من زوجها القن حال قيامه وجاءت به لأقل من ستة أشهر . قال رحمه الله : (فإن ولدت بعد عتقها لأكثر من ستة أشهر فولاؤه لمولى الأم لأن الولد جزؤها فيتبعها في الصفات الشرعية ألا ترى أنه يتبعها في الحرية وغيرها فكذا الولاء عند تعذر جعله تبعاً للأب لرقه. وفي التتارخانية : ولدت فقالت المرأة ولدت بعد عتقي بخمسة أشهر وولاؤه لموالي الأم وقال الزوج بعد عتقك بستة أشهر فولاؤه لموالي فالقول قول الزوج ا هـ . قال رحمه الله: (فإن أعتق العبد) وهو الأب (جرّ ولاء ابنه المواليه لأن موالي الأم لم يعتق الولد ههنا لحدوثه بعد إعتاقها، وإنما نسب إليه تبعاً للإمام لتعذر نسبته إلى الأب فإذا أعتق الأب أمكن نسبته إليه فجعله تبعاً له أولى تبعاً للأم لأن الولاء كالنسب قال عليه الصلاة والسلام الولاء لحمة كلحمة النسب والنسب إلى الآباء فكذا الولاء ينتقل إلى موالي الأب إذا زال المانع كولد الملاعنة يثبت نسبه من قوم الأم، فإذا أكذب نفسه ينتقل إلى الأب لزوال المانع. وفي الكافي : قلتم الولاء كالنسب من جعله
He (the author) said: 'And if he frees a pregnant [slave] from her husband who is a slave (qinn), the wala of the fetus does not transfer from the mother's patrons ever.' Because the fetus is freed by the freeing of its mother, and the freeing of the mother is intended, so likewise he is freed intentionally because he is a part of the mother, and the patron has placed the freeing on all her parts. And it was objected that this contradicts what was mentioned in the Book of Manumission, where they said: 'If he frees a pregnant [slave], her fetus is freed as a consequence of her, since it is attached to her.' So they said it is freed as a consequence, not intentionally, and this contradicts what they mentioned here. The basis for this is his statement (peace be upon him): 'Al-wala li man a'taq'. And the knowledge of the existence of the fetus at the time of freeing is by her giving birth at least six months from the time of freeing. Likewise, if she gives birth to two children: one at less than six months and the other at more than six months, and between them less than six months, then we are certain that the first existed at the time of freeing. So if the freeing applies to the first, it applies to the second out of necessity, and both become freed. And wala does not transfer from the manumitter. His saying 'from her husband who is a slave (qinn)' is an example; likewise if her husband is a mukatib or mudabbar. His saying 'from her husband' applies to the state of marriage being ongoing or after it? But after marriage there is no room for this detail. So he should have said: 'If he frees a pregnant [slave] from her husband who is a slave (qinn) during the marriage and she brings it at less than six months.' He (the author) said: 'If she gives birth after her freeing at more than six months, then his wala is for the mother's patron because the child is a part of her and follows her in legal attributes. Do you not see that it follows her in freedom and other things? Similarly, wala follows when it is not possible to make it follow the father due to his slavery.' In al-Tatarakhaniyyah: She gives birth and says, 'I gave birth after my freeing by five months, and his wala is for the mother's patrons,' and the husband says, 'after your freeing by six months, so his wala is for my patrons.' The statement is the statement of the husband. He (the author) said: 'If the slave (the father) is freed, he draws the wala of his son to his patrons.' Because the mother's patrons did not free the child here, as he came into existence after her freeing. He was attributed to her patron due to the inability to attribute him to his father. But when the father is freed, attribution to him becomes possible, so making him follow the father is better than following the mother, because wala is like lineage. He (peace be upon him) said: 'Wala is a bond like the bond of lineage, and lineage is to the fathers.' So likewise wala transfers to the father's patrons when the impediment is removed, just like the child of a woman married by li'an: his lineage is established from the mother's people, but if he (the father) denies himself (after admitting?), it transfers to the father when the impediment is removed. In al-Kafi: You said that wala is like lineage, from him...
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage deals with the wala of a child born to a freed slave woman. The key principle is that if the mother is freed while pregnant, the child is freed with her, and the wala of the child remains with the mother's manumitter permanently, even if the father is a slave (qinn). The text then discusses how to determine if the fetus existed at the time of manumission: if the mother gives birth within six months of the freeing, the fetus is deemed to have been present. If more than six months, the child is born after the freeing and the wala still goes to the mother's manumitter, but the commentary notes an exception: if the father is later freed, the wala transfers to the father's manumitter. This is based on the analogy that wala is like lineage, which follows the father. The passage also includes a practical case from al-Tatarakhaniyyah on disputed statements. Overall, the lesson emphasizes the permanence of wala but the possibility of transfer when the father's impediment (slavery) is removed.

Key Terms
الحمل (al-haml): The fetus in the womb of a slave woman.
القن (al-qinn): A full male slave who is not a mukatib, mudabbar, or umm walad's child.
موالي الأم (mawali al-umm): The patrons (manumitters) of the mother, i.e., the person who freed her and his agnates.
جرّ الولاء (jarr al-wala'): The pulling or transfer of wala from the mother's patrons to the father's patrons when the father is freed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a pregnant slave woman is freed and gives birth to a child after seven months, who holds the wala of the child?
A) The mother's manumitter
B) The father's manumitter, if the father is free
C) The child chooses
D) No wala exists

Key Takeaway
The wala of a child freed with its mother remains with her manumitter, but transfers to the father's patrons if the father is later freed, because wala is like lineage.

Wala' of Child when Non-Arab Marries a Freed Slave
Explains the wala' of a child when a non-Arab marries a freed slave and the dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relied-upon Hanafi position on the wala' of a child of a non-Arab father and a freed slave mother, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
The wala' of manumission is stronger than the father's lineage when the father is a non-Arab.

This lesson examines a specific case in Hanafi fiqh: when a non-Arab (ajami) Muslim marries a woman who is a freed slave (mu'tiqa), to whom does the wala' of their child belong? The school's leading authorities — Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani — differed on this question. Understanding this dispute reveals how the Hanafi school balances the strength of manumission-based wala' against lineage-based rights, particularly when the father is not of Arab descent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their statuses
Recognize that the father is a non-Arab Muslim who has a father in Islam, and the mother is a freed slave. This specific combination triggers the dispute.
2
State the relied-upon ruling (mufta bihi)
According to the text, the correct view (al-ash) is that the child's wala' goes to the mother's patrons (mawali al-umm).
This is the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
3
Understand Abu Yusuf's opposing position
Abu Yusuf holds that the wala' goes to the father's patrons because he considers lineage dominant over manumission wala' in this context.
The scholars disagreed on what Abu Yusuf's exact view was; some said he agreed with Abu Hanifa on certain points.
4
Analyze the thamarah (practical consequence)
The fruit of the disagreement appears when the child dies leaving certain relatives: under Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, inheritance goes to the mother's manumitter; under Abu Yusuf, it goes to the child's uterine relatives.
The example from Sharh al-Tahawi illustrates a scenario where wala' and 'aql are separated.
5
Apply a fortiori logic (qiyas al-awla)
If the wala' goes to the mother's patrons when the non-Arab has a father in Islam, then it is even more clearly so when he has no father in Islam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن كان أعجمياً مسألة وهي المتن قال إن كان العجمي له أب في الإسلام فعند أبي يوسف ولاء الولد لموالي الأب واختلف المشايخ على قولهما قيل ولاؤه لموالي الأب عندهم جميعاً. وقيل لمولى الأم وهو الأصح ولا يجر الجد الولاء ا هـ . قيد بكونها معتقة لأن العجمي لو تزوج بعربية فولدت له ولداً فإنه ينسب إلى قوم أبيه دون أمه . وقيدنا بكون الزوج عجمي فإن العربي إذا تزوج معتقة فإن ولده منها ينسب إلى قومه دونها. وقيد القدوري بمعتقة العرب وأطلق المصنف وهو الصواب لأن ولاء العتق قوي معتبر شرعاً فلا يختلف بين أن يكون من العرب أو من العجم. ولو كانا معتقين أو عجميين أو عربيين فالولد تابعاً للأب بالإجماع. وثمرة الخلاف على ما ذكر المصنف تظهر فيما إذا مات الولد وترك عمته أو غيرها من ذوي الأرحام ومعتق أمه أو عصبة معتقها كان المال لمعتق أمه أو عصبتها عندهما، وعند أبي يوسف يكون لذوي الأرحام لأن حكمه حكم أبيه . وفي شرح الطحاوي : امرأة من بني همدان تزوجت برجل من بني أسد فولد منها فأعتقت عبداً فالولاء يثبت منها وولدها يكون تبعاً للأب من بني أسد، فإذا ماتت ثم مات فميراثه لابن المعتقة وهو من بني جنى جناية تكون على عاقلتها من بني همدان فالميراث لبني أسد والعقل على بني همدان، ويجوز مثل هذا أن يكون الضمان على الغير والميراث للغير ألا ترى أن رجلين مثل الخال وابن العم فنفقته على الخال وميراثه لابن العم ا هـ . وإذا علم أن العجمي الذي له أب في الإسلام ولاؤه لموالي الأم علم بطريق الأولى إذا لم يكن له أب بالأولى.
And if he is a non-Arab, it is a case, and it is the text: he said that if the non-Arab has a father in Islam, then according to Abu Yusuf the wala' of the child goes to the patrons of the father. The scholars disagreed on their statement: it was said that his wala' goes to the patrons of the father according to all of them, and it was said to the patron of the mother, and that is the correct view, and the grandfather does not draw the wala'. End. It is restricted to her being a freed slave, because if a non-Arab marries an Arab woman and she gives birth to a child for him, then he is attributed to his father's people, not his mother. And we restricted it to the husband being a non-Arab, because if an Arab marries a freed slave, then his child from her is attributed to his people, not to her. And al-Quduri restricted it to a freed slave of the Arabs, and the author made it absolute, and that is correct because the wala' of manumission is strong and legally recognized, so it does not differ whether (the freed slave) is from the Arabs or from the non-Arabs. And if both were freed slaves, or non-Arabs, or Arabs, then the child follows the father by consensus. And the fruit of the disagreement, according to what the author mentioned, appears when the child dies leaving his paternal aunt or others from the uterine relatives and the manumitter of his mother or the 'asaba of her manumitter; the wealth goes to the manumitter of his mother or her 'asaba according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), and according to Abu Yusuf it goes to the uterine relatives because his ruling is like the ruling of his father. And in Sharh al-Tahawi: A woman from Banu Hamdan married a man from Banu Asad, and she gave birth to a child from him, then she manumitted a slave; the wala' is established from her, and her child follows the father from Banu Asad. When she dies, then he dies, his inheritance goes to the son of the freed slave, and he is from Banu Jana; if a crime is committed, its 'aql is on her 'aqila from Banu Hamdan. So the inheritance is for Banu Asad and the 'aql is on Banu Hamdan. And it is permissible that the guarantee be on someone else and the inheritance for someone else; do you not see that two men like the maternal uncle and the cousin: his maintenance is on the maternal uncle and his inheritance is for the cousin. End. And if it is known that the non-Arab who has a father in Islam, his wala' is to the patrons of the mother, then it is known a fortiori if he has no father, a fortiori.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the wala' (clientage) of a child born to a non-Arab ('ajami) father who has a father in Islam (i.e., is a Muslim) and a mother who is a freed slave (mu'tiqa). The passage first states the case and then explains the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. According to the relied-upon position (as stated in the text), the child's wala' goes to the patrons (mawali) of the mother. This is because the mother's wala' by manumission is strong and takes precedence over the father's lineage, especially since the father is a non-Arab. The text then discusses the practical consequence (thamarah) of this difference: if the child dies leaving only uterine relatives and the mother's manumitter or his 'asaba, the inheritance goes to the mother's manumitter according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, but to the uterine relatives according to Abu Yusuf. The passage also provides an example from Sharh al-Tahawi illustrating how the wala' and 'aql (blood money responsibility) can be separated between different groups. Finally, a fortiori logic is applied: if the non-Arab has a father in Islam and yet the wala' goes to the mother's patrons, then when he has no father in Islam, it is even more clearly so.

Key Terms
العجمي (al-'ajami): A non-Arab, specifically a person not of Arab descent.
الولاء (al-wala'): The legal relationship of clientage established through manumission, entailing inheritance rights.
المعتقة (al-mu'tiqa): A freed slave woman; the female manumitter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, if a non-Arab Muslim man marries a freed slave woman and they have a child, to whom does the child's wala' belong?
A) The father's patrons
B) The mother's patrons
C) The father's 'asaba relatives
D) The mother's 'asaba relatives

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, when a non-Arab marries a freed slave, the child's wala' belongs to the mother's patrons because the wala' of manumission is stronger than the father's lineage.

Priority of the Manumitter Over Uterine Relatives and Related Testimony Cases
States rule, provides evidence, then tests with cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the manumitter's inheritance priority, explain the evidence from hadith, and apply the rule to resolve conflicting testimony cases.

Core Idea
The manumitter inherits after the 'asaba but before uterine relatives, as established by hadith.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling that the manumitter (mu'tiq) is given precedence over uterine relatives (dhawi al-arham) but is placed after the blood 'asaba. After stating the rule and its evidence, the text presents numerous practical cases illustrating how inheritance is decided when there are conflicting testimonies about manumission and heirship. Understanding this rule is crucial for correctly determining the order of inheritance in the absence of blood 'asaba.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hierarchy of heirs
State the order: blood 'asaba (e.g., sons, fathers) come first, then the manumitter, then uterine relatives. The manumitter is the last of the 'asaba.
The manumitter is not an absolute 'asaba; he only inherits when no blood 'asaba exists.
2
Examine the evidence
Analyze the two proofs: the hadith 'If he dies and leaves no heir, you are his 'asaba' and the hadith of Hamza where the manumitter's daughter received half after the prescribed share.
The phrase 'you are his 'asaba' indicates the manumitter steps into the role of an 'asaba, not a uterine relative.
3
Analyze the dispute with Ibn Mas'ud
Ibn Mas'ud argued from Quran 8:75 that all blood relatives (including uterine) take priority. The Hanafi response distinguishes 'asaba from dhawi al-arham, and the hadith specifies the exception.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf resolved by the strong hadith evidence.
4
Apply the rule to testimony cases
Work through the cases from al-Muhit: conflicting claims between Muslim and dhimmi, requirements for testimony, multiple claimants, etc. Determine how the principle is used to decide inheritance.
Key is the equality of evidence and the need for specific testimony wording.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (والمعتق مقدم على ذوي الأرحام ومؤخر عن العصبة النسبية) وكذا هو مقدم على الرد على ذوي السهام وهو آخر العصبات وهو قول علي رضي الله عنه وبه أخذ علماء الأمصار، وكان ابن مسعود يقول بأنه مؤخر عن ذوي الأرحام بقوله تعالى وأولوا الأرحام بعضهم أولى ببعض في كتاب الله [الأنفال : ٧٥] وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام للمعتق في معتقه وإن مات ولم يدع وارثاً كنت أنت عصبته ولنا ما روينا من حديث حمزة أنه جعل لها النصف الباقي بعد فرض بنت معتقها حين مات عنها فعلم بقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام ولم يدع وارثاً يعني وارثاً هو عصبته. وفي المحيط : أقام مسلم بينة عادلة أنه أعتقه وأنه مات مسلماً لا وارث له غيره فأقام الذمي شاهدين مسلمين أنه أعتقه وأنه مات كافراً لا وارث له غيره فللمسلم نصف الميراث ونصف الميراث لأقرب الناس من المسلمين إلى الذمي لاستوائهما في الحجة، ولو شهدا أن الميت مولى فلان عتاقة لم يجز القضاء حتى يقولوا إن هذا الحي أعتق هذا الميت وهو يملكه وهو وارثه لا يعلم له وارثاً غيره. مات رجل وأخذ آخر ماله وادعى أنه وارثه لم يؤخذ منه المال لأنه يده ثابتة على المال، فإن خاصمه انسان طلب منه البينة لأنه يدعي استحقاق ما في يده . أن أباه أعتقه فشهد ابنا أخيه لم تقبل لأنها شهادة للجد . ادعى رجلان ولاءه بالعتق فأقاما البينة جعل الميراث بينهما لاستوائهما في الحجة، ولو قضى القاضي لأحدهما بالولاء والإرث ثم شهد آخران لآخر بمثله لا تقبل إلا أن يشهدا أنه اشتراه من الأول قبل أن يعتقه فيبطل القضاء للأول . أقام أحدهما البينة على ولاء العتاقة والآخر على أنه حر الأصل أسلم على يده ووالاه والغلام يدعيه فهو أولى. ادعى رجل أن أباه أعتق فلاناً الميت وآخر أن أباه أعتقه وأقرت بينة المیت به فالإقرار باطل والشهادة جائزة ، ولو شهد للآخر ابن وبنتان فالولاء بينهما . ادعى آخر أنه أعتق الميت وأقام البينة من في يده المال البينة على مثل ذلك فالمال والولاء بينهما .
He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: (The manumitter is given precedence over uterine relatives and is placed after the blood 'asaba.) And likewise he is given precedence over the return (of surplus) to the entitled shares, and he is the last of the 'asaba. This is the statement of 'Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, and the scholars of the regions adopted it. Ibn Mas'ud used to say that he is delayed after the uterine relatives by His statement, 'But those of kinship are more entitled to one another in the decree of Allah' [al-Anfal 75], and he, peace be upon him, said to the manumitter regarding his freed slave: 'If he dies and leaves no heir, then you are his 'asaba.' And we have what we narrated from the hadith of Hamza that he gave her the remaining half after the prescribed share of the daughter of her manumitter when he died, so it is known by his statement, peace be upon him, 'and he leaves no heir' meaning an heir who is his 'asaba. And in al-Muhit: A Muslim established just evidence that he manumitted him and that he died as a Muslim with no heir other than him, then the dhimmi brought two Muslim witnesses that he manumitted him and that he died as a disbeliever with no heir other than him; then the Muslim gets half the inheritance and the other half goes to the nearest person among the Muslims to the dhimmi due to the equality of their evidence. And if they testify that the deceased is the freed slave of so-and-so by manumission, the judgment is not permitted until they say: 'This living person manumitted this deceased while he owned him and he is his heir, and he knows of no other heir for him.' A man died and another took his property and claimed that he is his heir; the property is not taken from him because his hand is established on the property. If someone disputes with him, he demands evidence from him because he claims entitlement to what is in his hand. If his father manumitted him and the two sons of his brother testify, it is not accepted because it is testimony for the grandfather. Two men claimed his wala' by manumission and they brought evidence; the inheritance is divided between them due to the equality of their evidence. If the judge judged for one of them with the wala' and inheritance, then two others testify for another with similar, it is not accepted unless they testify that he bought him from the first before he manumitted him, thereby nullifying the judgment for the first. One of them presented evidence of manumission wala', and the other presented that he is free by origin who became Muslim at his hand and made a pact of clientage, and the slave claims him; then the first is more entitled. A man claimed that his father manumitted so-and-so the deceased, and another that his father manumitted him, and the witnesses of the deceased acknowledged it; then the acknowledgment is invalid but the testimony is valid. If the other was witnessed by a son and two daughters, then the wala' is between them. Another claimed that he manumitted the deceased and brought evidence, and the one in whose hand the property is brought similar evidence; then the property and the wala' are between them.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It first states the rule: the manumitter (mu'tiq) is preferred over uterine relatives (dhawi al-arham) but is placed after the blood 'asaba (nasabiyya). This means that the mu'tiq inherits as an 'asaba after all partial agnates, and even after the return (radd) to the entitled shares. The text attributes this view to 'Ali ibn Abi Talib and the majority of scholars. Ibn Mas'ud disagreed, saying the mu'tiq should be after uterine relatives, citing Quran 8:75. The author rebuts this with two proofs: first, a hadith where the Prophet said to a manumitter, 'If he dies and leaves no heir, you are his 'asaba,' meaning an heir from the 'asaba, not uterine relatives. Second, the hadith of Hamza where the Prophet gave the remaining half to the manumitter's daughter after the prescribed share of the manumitter's daughter, showing the manumitter's entitlement is through 'asaba, not after all relatives. The text then gives a series of cases from al-Muhit: conflicting evidence between a Muslim and a dhimmi, requirements for testimony in manumission cases, claims of inheritance, testimony of relatives, and multiple claimants. These illustrate the practical application of the rules. The commentary emphasizes that the mu'tiq is a last resort heir: he only inherits when there is no blood 'asaba, and not after uterine relatives.

Key Terms
المعتق (al-mu'tiq): The manumitter; the person who frees a slave.
ذوو الأرحام (dhawi al-arham): Uterine relatives; blood relatives who are not 'asaba (e.g., maternal uncles, aunts).
العصبة النسبية (al-'asaba al-nasabiyya): The agnatic relatives by blood who inherit as 'asaba (e.g., sons, fathers, brothers).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, where does the manumitter (mu'tiq) stand in the order of inheritance?
A) After all blood relatives, including uterine
B) Before all blood relatives
C) After the 'asaba but before uterine relatives
D) After the uterine relatives but before the 'asaba

Key Takeaway
The manumitter inherits after the blood 'asaba but before uterine relatives, based on the hadith making him an 'asaba in their absence.

Inheritance through Wala' When the Manumitter Dies After the Freed Slave
Explains inheritance rules when the manumitter dies after the freed slave, including priority of asaba and specific cases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for wala' inheritance when the mu'tiq dies after the mawla, and apply it to determine the heir among the mawla's 'asaba.

Core Idea
Wala' inheritance reverts to the freed slave's closest agnatic heir, not the manumitter's own family.

When a manumitter (mu'tiq) dies after the freed slave (mawla), the estate that passes through wala' must be distributed based on the freed slave's agnatic relations. This lesson unpacks the general rule, its basis in substitution (khilafa), and several specific applications, including a well-known dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. We will also examine the famous incident of Ali and al-Zubayr before Caliph Uthman, which serves as a key proof text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
State clearly that when the mu'tiq dies after the mawla, the wala' inheritance goes to the nearest 'asaba (agnatic heir) of the mawla.
The text begins: 'فميراثه لأقرب عصبة المولى'
2
Understand the legal basis (khilafa)
Explain why the rule is as such: wala' substitutes (khilafa) for the mawla's own 'asaba. The mu'tiq steps into the shoes of the mawla's agnates, so the nearest among them inherits.
This principle distinguishes wala' from blood inheritance.
3
Apply the rule to examples
Work through the father/son and grandfather/brother cases given in the text. Determine who inherits in each scenario based on proximity in 'asaba.
Father vs son: son inherits. Grandfather vs brother: grandfather inherits.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi disagreement
Identify that Abu Yusuf holds a different view in the father/son case, giving the father one-sixth. Understand his reasoning and the majority response.
Abu Yusuf analogizes to regular inheritance; the majority holds that wala' is not the same.
5
Consider edge cases and practical implications
Review the case of the daughter of the mawla (zahir al-riwaya says nothing; later scholars differ), the inheritance of dhimmis, and the distribution among multiple grandchildren.
These show the rule's boundaries and the role of fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (فإن مات المولى ثم المعتق فميراثه لأقرب عصبة المولى) لأن الولاء يجر الإرث وإنما يثبت للعصبة بطريق الخلافة فيقدم الأقرب فالأقرب حتى لو ترك أباً مولاه وابن مولاه كان الولاء للابن، ولو ترك جد مولاه وأخا مولاه كان الولاء للجد لأنه أقرب في العصبة. وفي الأول خلاف أبي يوسف فإنه يعطي الأب السدس والباقي للابن، والثاني خلاف من يرى توريث الإخوة مع الجد، وكذا الولاء لابن المعتقة دون أخيها وعقل جنايتها على أخيها لأنه من قوم أبيها لما روي أن علي بن أبي طالب والزبير بن العوام اختصما إلى عثمان في معتق صفية بنت عبد المطلب حين مات فقال علي : مولى عمتي فأنا أحق بإرثه لأني أعقل عنها. وقال الزبير : هو مولى أمي فأنا أرثها فكذا أرث معتقها. فقضى عثمان بالإرث للزبير وبالعقل على علي. ولو ترك المعتق ابن مولاه وابن ابن مولاه كان الولاء للابن دون ابن الابن لما روي عن عمر وعلي وابن مسعود أنهم قالوا الولاء للكبير أي لا كبر الأولاد. والمراد أقربهم نسباً لا أكبرهم سناً . ولو مات المعتق ولم يترك إلا ابنة المعتق فلا شيء لبنت المعتق في ظاهر الرواية عن أصحابنا ويوضع ماله في بيت المال وبعض المشايخ كانوا يفتون بالدفع إليها بطريق الإرث بل لأنها أقرب الناس إلى الميت وليس في زماننا بيت مال منتظم. ولو دفع إلى السلطان أو القاضي لا يصرفه إلى المستحق ظاهراً، وكذا ما فضل عن فرض الزوجين يرد عليهما، وكذا ولد الابن والبنت من الرضاع يصرف إليهما إذا لم يكن هناك أقرب منهما؛ ذكر هذه المسائل في النهاية. والذميون يتوارثون كالمسلمين لأنه أحد أسباب الإرث. وفي المحيط : مات المعتق عن ابنين فمات أحدهما عن ابن والآخر عن ابنين ثم مات المعتق فالميراث على عدد رؤوسهم لأنهم سواء في كونهم عصبة الميت، ولو أعتقت المرأة ثم ماتت عن زوج عبد وابن وبنت ثم مات المعتق فميراثه لابن المعتقة لأنه عصبتها لا غير،
He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: (If the freed slave dies then the manumitter dies, then his inheritance goes to the nearest 'asaba of the freed slave) because wala' draws inheritance, and it is only established for the 'asaba by way of substitution; so the nearest is given precedence, then the next. Even if he leaves a father of his freed slave and a son of his freed slave, the wala' goes to the son. If he leaves a grandfather of his freed slave and a brother of his freed slave, the wala' goes to the grandfather because he is nearer in 'asaba. In the first there is a disagreement of Abu Yusuf, for he gives the father one-sixth and the remainder to the son. The second is a disagreement of those who consider brothers to inherit with the grandfather. Likewise, the wala' goes to the son of the freed slave woman, not to her brother, and the 'aql for her crime is on her brother, because he is from her father's people, based on what is narrated that 'Ali ibn Abi Talib and al-Zubayr ibn al-'Awwam disputed before 'Uthman regarding a freed slave of Safiyya bint 'Abd al-Muttalib when he died. 'Ali said: 'He is the freed slave of my aunt, so I am more entitled to his inheritance because I bear the 'aql for her.' Al-Zubayr said: 'He is the freed slave of my mother, so I inherit from her, and likewise I inherit her freed slave.' 'Uthman judged that the inheritance goes to al-Zubayr and the 'aql is on 'Ali. If the manumitter leaves a son of his freed slave and a son's son of his freed slave, the wala' goes to the son, not to the son's son, based on what is narrated from 'Umar, 'Ali, and Ibn Mas'ud that they said: 'Wala' is for the elder,' meaning the older in age? No, the intended meaning is the nearer in lineage, not the older in age. If the manumitter dies and leaves only a daughter of the freed slave, then there is nothing for the daughter of the freed slave in the apparent transmission from our companions, and his wealth is placed in the treasury. Some scholars used to give a fatwa to give it to her by way of inheritance, because she is the nearest person to the deceased, and in our time there is no organized treasury. If it is given to the ruler or judge, he does not spend it to the deserving apparently. Likewise, what remains after the prescribed shares of the spouses is returned to them. Likewise, the child of a son or daughter through suckling is given to them if there is no one nearer than them. These issues are mentioned in al-Nihaya. And the dhimmis inherit from each other like Muslims because it is one of the causes of inheritance. In al-Muhit: The manumitter died leaving two sons; one of them died leaving a son, and the other died leaving two sons; then the manumitter dies; the inheritance is distributed according to the number of heads because they are equal in being 'asaba of the deceased. If a woman manumitted someone, then she dies leaving a slave husband, a son, and a daughter; then the manumitter dies; his inheritance goes to the son of the freed slave woman because he is her 'asaba, no one else.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, explaining the order of inheritance when the mu'tiq (manumitter) dies after the mawla (freed slave). The general rule: the inheritance of the mu'tiq (through wala') goes to the nearest 'asaba of the mawla, because wala' transfers inheritance to the 'asaba by way of substitution (khilafa). The text gives examples: if the mawla left a father and a son, the son gets the wala' inheritance because he is nearer in 'asaba; if a grandfather and a brother, the grandfather takes precedence. Abu Yusuf disagrees on the father-son case, giving the father one-sixth and the son the remainder, similar to inheritance rules. On the grandfather-brother case, it is a well-known dispute between those who make brothers co-inherit with the grandfather. The text then mentions the famous case of 'Ali and al-Zubayr before 'Uthman concerning the wala' of a freed slave of Safiyya. 'Uthman gave the inheritance to al-Zubayr (as he was the son of the manumitter) and the 'aql (responsibility for blood money) to 'Ali (who was the nephew of the manumitter), illustrating that wala' and 'aql can be separated. Next, the rule that the nearer in lineage (aqrab nasaban) inherits, not the older in age. The passage then addresses edge cases: if the mu'tiq dies leaving only a daughter of the mawla, the apparent transmission (zahir al-riwaya) says she gets nothing; the wealth goes to the treasury (bayt al-mal). Some later scholars (mutakhkhirin) gave fatawa to give it to her because she is the nearest and in our times there is no regular treasury. The text also covers the inheritance of dhimmis through wala' and a case from al-Muhit about multiple grandchildren inheriting per capita. Finally, a case where a woman manumits and then dies leaving a slave husband, son, and daughter: the mu'tiq's inheritance goes to the son (of the freed slave) because he is her 'asaba.

Key Terms
المولى (al-mawla): The freed slave; the person who has been manumitted.
العصبة (al-'asaba): Agnatic heirs who inherit the remainder after fixed shares.
الخلافة (al-khilafa): Substitution; the mu'tiq stands in the place of the freed slave's 'asaba.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a freed slave dies, then his manumitter dies later, who inherits the manumitter's estate (from the wala')?
A) The manumitter's own children
B) The nearest 'asaba of the freed slave
C) The manumitter's spouse
D) The state treasury

Key Takeaway
Wala' inheritance always goes to the nearest agnatic heir of the freed slave, not to the manumitter's own family.

Conditions and Ruling of Wala' al-Muwalah
Explaining the conditions and legal ruling of wala' al-muwalah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three general conditions for the validity of wala' al-muwalah and state its legal ruling (sahih) as per the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Wala' al-muwalah is valid with three conditions: unknown lineage, no prior wala', and not being an Arab.

This lesson examines the contractual form of patronage known as wala' al-muwalah, which allows a non-Arab convert with unknown lineage to enter into a pact with a patron for inheritance and blood money. The Hanafi school upholds its validity under specific conditions, while other schools reject it. We will explore these conditions and the dual role of inheritance and 'aql as both prerequisites and legal outcomes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its category
Recognise that wala' al-muwalah is a contract of patronage established by mutual agreement after conversion to Islam. Its validity depends on specific conditions.
This is a voluntary pact, unlike wala' al-itaq which arises from emancipation.
2
List the three general conditions
From al-Inayah and al-Nihayah: (1) the convert's lineage must be unknown, (2) he must have no prior wala' (from emancipation or another muwalah) with anyone, and (3) he must not be an Arab.
These are the general conditions needed in all cases; additional conditions like sanity and freedom are considered rare and not mentioned here.
3
Distinguish between general and specific conditions
Note that other sources like al-Kafi and al-Bada'i add conditions: stipulation of inheritance and 'aql, and sanity and freedom of the inferior. These are valid but not part of the core three.
The three general conditions are sufficient for the basic validity; the additional ones address specific scenarios.
4
Explain the ruling and its consequences
Once conditions are met, the contract is sahih (valid). The legal ruling (hukm) is that the patron inherits from the convert and is obligated to pay 'aql (blood money) on his behalf. The convert can also transfer his 'aql to another.
Inheritance and 'aql are both conditions and rulings: they are stipulated beforehand and realised afterwards.
5
Understand the dual nature of inheritance and 'aql
The text resolves the apparent contradiction by stating that they are conditions when viewed before the contract (they must be stipulated) and rulings after the contract (they become the legal effects).
This shows the flexibility of legal reasoning in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الولاء
أسلم رجل على يد رجل ووالاه على أن يرثه ويعقل عنه أو على يد غيره ووالاه صح وعقله على مولاه وارثه له وإن لم يكن له وارث وهو آخر ذوي الأرحام وله أن يتحول عاقلتك وقبل الآخر هذا قال في العناية والنهاية : وأما شرطه فله ثلاث شرائط : أحدها أن يكون مجهول النسب بأن لا ينسب إلى شخص بل ينسب إلى غيره، وأما نسبة غيره إليه فغير مانعة. والثاني أن لا يكون له ولاء عتاقة ولا ولاء الموالاة مع أحد وقد عقل عنه. والثالث أن لا يكون عربياً .اهـ. وفي الكافي : إنما تصح ولاية الموالاة بشرائط منها : أن يشترط الإرث والعقل . قال في العناية : فإن قيل من شرط العقل عقل الأعلى أو حريته فإن موالاة الصبي والعبد باطلة فكيف جعل الشرائط ثلاثة؟ وأجيب بأن المذكور إنما هي الشرائط العامة المحتاج إليها في كل واحد من الصور، وأما ما ذكرت فإنه نادر فلم يذكره. وفي الشارح: ولو ذكر الإرث من الجانبين كان كذلك لأنه يمكن أن يتوارثا بخلاف ولاء العتاقة بحيث لا يرث إلا الأعلى ويدخل فيه الأولاد الصغار ومن يولد بعد عتق الموالاة. وفي البدائع : ومن شرائط عقد الموالاة فمنها عقل العاقدين وحرية الأسفل أيضاً اهـ . وفي المبسوط : وإذا عقد العقد العبد عقد الموالاة بإذن مولاه كان عقده كعقد مولاه فيكون الولاء للمولى اهـ. وأما حكمه شرعاً فالإرث والعقل عنه . واعترض بأن الإرث والعقل شرط صحة العقد فكيف يكون حكماً والشرط متقدم والحكم متأخر؟ وأجيب بأنه يجوز أن يعتبر له حالتان، فباعتبار التقديم شرطاً وباعتبار التأخير حكماً .
Book of Wala'. A man embraced Islam at the hands of a man and made a pact of patronage (muwalah) on the condition that he inherits from him and pays blood money on his behalf, or [he embraced Islam] at the hands of another and made such a pact, it is valid; and his 'aql (blood money) is upon his patron, and his patron inherits from him. And if he has no heir, he [the patron] is the last of the dhawi al-arham. And he has the right to transfer to another 'aql? And the other accepted. This [the text] says in al-'Inayah and al-Nihayah: As for its conditions, it has three conditions: First, that he be of unknown lineage, i.e., not attributed to any person, but rather attributed to someone else. As for someone else being attributed to him, that is not an impediment. Second, that he have no wala' of emancipation nor wala' of muwalah with anyone, and he [the patron] has paid 'aql on his behalf. Third, that he not be an Arab. End quote. In al-Kafi: Wala' al-muwalah is only valid with conditions, among them that inheritance and 'aql be stipulated. He said in al-'Inayah: If it is said that from the conditions of 'aql is the sanity or freedom of the superior, for the muwalah of a minor and a slave is invalid, so how did he make the conditions three? The answer is that what is mentioned are only the general conditions needed in every one of the cases, whereas what you mentioned is rare, so he did not mention it. In al-Sharh: And if inheritance from both sides were mentioned, it would be the same, because it is possible that they inherit from each other, unlike wala' of emancipation where only the superior inherits, and it includes minor children and those born after the pact. In al-Bada'i: Among the conditions of the muwalah contract are the sanity of both parties and also the freedom of the inferior, etc. In al-Mabsut: If a slave makes a muwalah contract with his master's permission, his contract is like his master's contract, so the wala' belongs to the master. As for its ruling in shari'ah, it is inheritance and 'aql on his behalf. And it was objected that inheritance and 'aql are conditions for the validity of the contract, so how can they be the ruling, while the condition precedes and the ruling follows? The answer is that it is permissible to consider two states for them: in terms of precedence they are conditions, and in terms of subsequence they are rulings.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Wala' explains the conditions and ruling of wala' al-muwalah (patronage by agreement). The text begins by stating the basic ruling: if a man converts to Islam at the hands of another and makes a muwalah pact with the condition of inheritance and 'aql, it is valid. The patron becomes responsible for the convert's blood money and inherits from him if the convert has no other heirs, being considered the last of the dhawi al-arham (distant relatives). The commentator then elaborates from al-'Inayah and al-Nihayah, listing three general conditions for the convert: (1) his lineage must be unknown, (2) he must not already have a wala' relationship (either from emancipation or a previous muwalah) with anyone, and (3) he must not be an Arab. A further condition from al-Kafi is that inheritance and 'aql must be stipulated. An objection is raised: why are conditions like sanity and freedom not mentioned, since a minor or slave cannot contract muwalah? The answer is that those are rare and specific, while the three given are general. The ruling of the contract is inheritance and 'aql, but if these are conditions, how can they also be rulings? The resolution is that the same elements can be considered conditions before the contract and rulings after its conclusion.

Key Terms
ولاء الموالاة (wala' al-muwalah): Patronage established by mutual agreement (muwalah) between a convert and his patron, entailing inheritance and 'aql.
العقل (al-'aql): Payment of blood money (diyah) by a tribe or patron on behalf of a person who commits unintentional homicide.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many general conditions for the validity of wala' al-muwalah are mentioned in al-'Inayah and al-Nihayah?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Five

Key Takeaway
Wala' al-muwalah is a valid contract with three essential conditions, and the same elements of inheritance and 'aql serve both as preconditions and as legal effects.

The Dispute on Wala' al-Muwalah: Hanafi vs. Malik/Shafi'i
Critiquing the rejection of wala' al-muwalah by Malik and Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on wala' al-muwalah and identify the key points of disagreement with the Malikis and Shafi'is.

Core Idea
Muwalah is valid in Hanafi law and implicitly includes inheritance and 'aql; opposing schools reject it entirely.

Wala' al-muwalah is a form of patronage established by mutual agreement, not by emancipation or blood relation. The Hanafi school recognizes its validity and considers inheritance and 'aql to be inherent consequences, even if not explicitly stipulated. In contrast, Malik and al-Shafi'i reject the institution altogether. This lesson examines the arguments from both sides and the Hanafi response, as presented in the passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
Determine what is being disputed: is wala' al-muwalah a valid legal institution? If valid, does it require explicit stipulation of inheritance and 'aql?
The passage states Malik and Shafi'i say 'no consideration for this at all'.
2
State the Hanafi position
From the passage, the Hanafi position is that muwalah is valid and that inheritance and 'aql are implied even without mention. Note the citation of al-Hakim al-Shahid.
3
Examine the objection and response
The author of Ghaayat al-Bayan objects that the Hanafi imams did not require stipulation. The response is that the omission was because those rights were obvious and automatically included.
This clarifies the Hanafi view on necessity of explicit stipulation.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Consider the scenario from al-Muhit: a dhimmi woman converts and makes a muwalah pact while having a young son. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say the son's wala' does not go to her patron; Abu Hanifa's analogy suggests it would. Note the practical difference.
This shows disagreement within the school on extension of wala' to offspring.
5
Synthesize the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: non-Hanafis do not recognize inheritance through muwalah; Hanafis enforce it. Internally, the child's wala' may or may not transfer depending on which Hanafi view is followed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال مالك والشافعي : لا اعتبار بهذا أصلاً وقد بين الدليل من الجانبين في المطولات واعترض صاحب غاية البيان على وجوب اشتراط الإرث والعقل في صحة عقد الموالاة حيث قال قال لحاكم الشهيد : إذا أسلم رجل على يد رجل ووالاه فإنه يرثه ويعقل عنه، وهذا قول أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف ومحمد، وهذا يدل على أن اشتراط الإرث والعقل ليس بشرط بل مجرد العقل كافٍ. وأجيب بأن عدم وقوع التصريح بذكرهما بناء على ظهورهما فضمن عقد الموالاة ذلك ولو لم يذكر . وفي المحيط : أسلمت ذمية فوالت رجلاً ولها ولد صغير من ذمي لم يكن ولاء ولدها لمولاها في قولهما، وفي قياس قول الإمام يكون له
And Malik and al-Shafi'i said: There is no consideration for this at all. And the proof from both sides has been explained in the detailed works. And the author of Ghaayat al-Bayan objected to the necessity of stipulating inheritance and 'aql in the validity of the muwalah contract, where he said: al-Hakim al-Shahid said: If a man embraces Islam at the hands of a man and makes a pact with him, then he inherits from him and pays 'aql on his behalf. This is the statement of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad. This indicates that stipulating inheritance and 'aql is not a condition; rather, mere 'aql [agreement] is sufficient. And it was answered that the lack of explicit mention of them is due to their being obvious, so the muwalah contract implicitly includes them even if not mentioned. And in al-Muhit: A dhimmi woman embraced Islam and made a pact of patronage with a man, and she had a young son from a dhimmi; the wala' of her son does not belong to her patron according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and according to the analogy of the statement of the Imam (Abu Hanifa), it would belong to him.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage presents the inter-madhhab dispute regarding wala' al-muwalah. Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i completely reject this institution, considering it invalid. The Hanafi school, however, affirms it. Within the Hanafi school, there is also a dispute about whether it is necessary to explicitly stipulate inheritance and 'aql in the contract. The author of Ghaayat al-Bayan cites al-Hakim al-Shahid's statement that the early Hanafi masters (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) did not require explicit stipulation; rather, the mere fact of the pact implies those rights and duties. The response is that the Hanafi imams did not mention the stipulation because it was obvious; the contract necessarily includes inheritance and 'aql by default. The passage then introduces a scenario from al-Muhit about a dhimmi woman who converts and makes a muwalah pact while having a young dhimmi son. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, the son's wala' does not go to her patron; but by analogy from Abu Hanifa's principle, it would go to him. This intra-Hanafi difference is part of the broader discussion on the effects of muwalah.

Key Terms
موالاة (muwalah): A pact of mutual patronage and support, typically between a convert and a Muslim, creating inheritance and blood money liability.
ولاء الموالاة (wala' al-muwalah): The bond of patronage resulting from a muwalah contract.
غاية البيان (Ghaayat al-Bayan): A Hanafi fiqh work by al-Hakim al-Shahid, cited here for the position on muwalah.
عقل ('aql): Blood money (diyah) liability; the obligation to pay compensation for homicide or injury.
إرث (irth): Inheritance; the right of one party to inherit from the other.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling of Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding wala' al-muwalah?
A) It is valid with stipulation.
B) It is valid but only for inheritance.
C) It is completely invalid.
D) It is valid only if the patron is a relative.

Key Takeaway
Muwalah is a valid institution in Hanafi law, automatically entailing inheritance and 'aql, despite its rejection by Malik and Shafi'i; intra-Hanafi differences exist on its extension to dependents.
